401 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


NO. 2005-CP-01047-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


956 So. 2d 310; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 871



November 21, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/3/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, proceeding pro se, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Warren County (Mississippi), which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two indictments presented against him for the sale and delivery of a controlled substance. He was sentenced to 18 years, with 12 years to serve, six years suspended, and five years of post-release supervision. The trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. On appeal, the court found that there were two distinct factual bases for defendant's guilty plea. First, he admitted that he committed both crimes for which he was entering a plea of guilty. Second, the trial judge asked the assistant district attorney during the plea colloquy what the State expected the evidence to show at trial. Further, defendant failed to provide sufficient evidence demonstrating his attorney's deficiency. Defendant admitted in his brief that he could not name the witness that counsel should have interviewed, nor did he disclose the "mitigating information" that counsel allegedly failed to uncover. Finally, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-2(1) (Rev. 2000) made single, multi-count indictments permissive, not mandatory. The State did not improperly indict defendant under multiple indictments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

402 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01385-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


942 So. 2d 308; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 850



November 14, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PEARL RIVER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/22/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL R. EUBANKS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF AGGRAVATED DUI WITH INJURY IN VIOLATION OF MISSISSIPPI CODE ANNOTATED SECTION 63-11-30(5) AND SENTENCE OF TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF MDOC, WITH FIVE YEARS TO BE SERVED IN THE INTENSIVE SUPERVISION PROGRAM AND FIFTEEN YEARS SUSPENDED PENDING SUCCESSFUL COMPLETION OF A FIVE YEAR PERIOD OF POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION PURSUANT TO MISSISSIPPI CODE ANNOTATED SECTION 47-7-34.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Pearl River County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(5) and sentenced him to 20 years in custody of the department of corrections. The State appealed defendant's sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant ran a stop sign and struck a vehicle driven by the victim who suffered catastrophic injuries. Defendant contended that the four-hour delay in obtaining his blood sample rendered the test results inadmissible under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-8. The court noted that this case did not involve a vehicle accident under § 63-11-8; rather, defendant was convicted under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(5) for aggravated DUI. Although the blood test was administered more than two hours after the accident, the record was devoid of any proof that the arresting officer deliberately delayed the acquiring of a blood sample; defendant was not allowed to eat or drink anything throughout the time period; and thus the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The trial judge properly exercised his gatekeeping responsibility as to the admission of the State's testimony in the manner in which the Mississippi Supreme Court intended. Since the officers' request for and taking of a blood sample could not be considered custodial interrogation under the law, the court could not conclude that a violation of defendant's right to counsel occurred as a result of such tests being administered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

403 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Sherron v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01668-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


959 So. 2d 30; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 832



November 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by, En banc Sherron v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 230 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 3, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Sherron v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 375 (Miss., June 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of being an accessory after the fact to her husband's crime of statutory rape by assisting the victim, who was her minor daughter, to obtain an abortion, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-1-5 (Rev. 2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of being an accessory after the fact to her husband's crime of statutory rape by assisting her minor daughter, the victim, obtain an abortion. That assistance helped hide the husband's crime by removing its most obvious evidence. The appellate court stated that it did not need to decide the constitutionality of charging concealment of a rape due to the assistance that defendant gave her minor daughter to gain an abortion. Defendant raised the issue before trial only later to abandon it. Thus, the issue was waived and the appellate court found no other errors. The evidence supported that defendant concealed, received, relieved, aided, or assisted her husband when she took the victim for an abortion. Those acts themselves were sufficient under the statutory language contained in Miss. Code Ann. § 97-1-5 (Rev. 2006).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

404 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Dimaio v. State


NO. 2005-KA-00782-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


951 So. 2d 581; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 782



October 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Dimaio v. State, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 162 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TALLAHATCHIE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/10/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANN H. LAMAR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: COUNT I - CONVICTION OF BURGLARY OF A CHURCH AND SENTENCE OF TEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS; COUNT II - CONVICTION OF PETIT LARCENY AND SENTENCE OF ONE YEAR IN THE TALLAHATCHIE COUNTY JAIL; COUNT III - CONVICTION OF BURGLARY OF A CHURCH AND SENTENCE OF FIVE YEARS ON POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION, PENDING FUTURE GOOD BEHAVIOR; COUNT IV - CONVICTION OF PETIT LARCENY AND SENTENCE OF ONE YEAR IN THE TALLAHATCHIE COUNTY JAIL; COUNT V - CONVICTION OF FELONY MALICIOUS MISCHIEF AND SENTENCE OF FIVE YEARS ON POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION, PENDING FUTURE GOOD BEHAVIOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Tallahatchie County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of two counts of burglary of a church, two counts of petit larceny, and one count of felony malicious mischief.


OVERVIEW: Police obtained a search warrant for defendant's residence after a church was broken into two different times. Stolen items were found in defendant's home. After defendant was convicted, he sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence found during the execution of the search warrant. Proximate cause existed based on the statements of several witnesses. Next, a motion to sever was properly denied as to the charges relating to the church burglaries because they were part of a common scheme or plan, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-2 (Rev. 2000). Further, an instruction on receiving stolen property was properly denied because no reasonable jury could have found defendant guilty of this offense based on defendant's admission, the codefendant's testimony, and the items found in defendant's home. Moreover, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 97-17-33(2), 97-17-43(2) were not unconstitutional under the Establishment Clause since they did not represent a government endorsement of religion. Finally, an ineffective assistance of counsel claim was not proper on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

Hill v. State


NO. 2005-CP-01367-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


940 So. 2d 972; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 785



October 24, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/31/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was indicted for murder, but eventually entered a guilty plea to the crime of manslaughter. After he received a 15-year sentence, the inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief. The motion was denied, and an appeal was filed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the inmate failed to sufficiently brief his arguments. All that appeared was the issue heading, and no argument followed, as required by Miss. R. App. P. 28(a)(6). Although inartful drafting was sometimes overlooked, the deficiencies in this brief went beyond inartful drafting. In addition, there was no citation to any authority. The table of authorities was not related to any particular argument either. The appellate court also noted that the record was insufficient because it did not include a transcript of his guilty plea. Finally, there were no sworn affidavits; the inmate was required to either furnish them or show cause why he could not, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-9(1)(e) (Rev. 2000).


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

406 of 603 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. Petal Sch. Dist.


NO. 2005-CC-01394-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


956 So. 2d 273; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 672



September 19, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing, en banc, denied by Smith v. Petal Sch. Dist., 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 149 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 20, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Petal Sch. Dist., 957 So. 2d 1004, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 289 (Miss., May 10, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a decision from the Forrest County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which affirmed a decision from a board of trustees for appellee school district to not renew the employee's contract.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked as a teacher and an assistant football coach, was notified that his contract would not be renewed for the following year due to the fact that he failed to attend several football workouts during the summer months. The chancery court affirmed the decision, and the employee sought further review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that a rider to the contract did not violate Miss. Code Ann. § 37-9-23 (2006) based on the fact that it was not officially approved by the Mississippi Board of Education. Next, the rider did not violate the Fair Labor Standards Act because 29 C.F.R. § 541.303(b) exempted teachers, specifically those with coaching duties. At any rate, the additional two months listed in the rider were merely part of the usual coaching duties. Also, the appellate court rejected the argument that Miss. Code Ann. § 37-9-111(5) (Rev. 2001) was unconstitutional as applied under the Fourteenth Amendment. The decision was not arbitrary or capricious because the employment contract and rider referred to the single position of teacher/coach. Therefore, the failure to attend workouts constituted a sufficient basis for nonrenewal.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.


 

407 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Booker v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02143-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 635



August 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by Booker v. State, 2008 Miss. App. LEXIS 77 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/20/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER. SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant participated in the beating death of a victim when he was barely sixteen. He was tried as an adult and convicted of murder. Thereafter, he sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that defendant's trial counsel failed to raise an issue relating to whether he should have been tried in youth court instead; therefore, the issue was waived on appeal. Even if it had not been waived, the circuit court had original jurisdiction over the murder charge under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-151(1)(a) (Rev. 2004). Next, defendant did not show a violation of Batson since the prosecution offered race-neutral reasons for striking several jurors. Further, the appellate court found that his right to a speedy trial under the Sixth Amendment and the Mississippi Constitution was also not violated by a sixteen month delay between arrest and the date of trial after the Barker factors were considered. Finally, the confession given was voluntary since a showing of mental weakness was not enough, defendant waived an objection to the swearing of the jury, and evidence of the victim's pain was properly admitted, as were gruesome crime scene photographs.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

In the Interest of C.B.Y.


NO. 2005-CA-00256-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


936 So. 2d 974; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 617



August 22, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY YOUTH COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/5/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL W. MCPHAIL. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: TERMINATION OF NATURAL MOTHER'S PARENTAL RIGHTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The mother appealed the decision of the Forrest County Youth Court (Mississippi), which terminated her parents rights to her minor child.


OVERVIEW: The mother appealed the termination of her parental rights to her minor child, but the court affirmed. The mother's testimony alone was sufficient evidence to support the youth court's finding that her behavior, choosing to remain on runaway status to avoid the Department of Human Services (DHS), was the reason that her child could not be returned to her within a reasonable amount of time. Additionally, the court found that the findings of the youth court met the statutory grounds for termination of parental rights contained in Miss. Code Ann. § 93-15-103(3)(d)-(f) (Rev. 2004). The child was in the custody of the DHS since July 31, 2001, which was well over the statutory requirement of one year, and the mother's ongoing behavior was a ground for termination of her parental rights. The ongoing behavior cited by the youth court was the mother's decision to remain on runaway status, thus preventing her from maintaining a bond with the child, as it was impossible to return the child to her custody and care when she chose to avoid the DHS.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kelly v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01961-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


947 So. 2d 1002; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 571



August 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Kelly v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 940 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 21, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Kelly v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 89 (Miss., Jan. 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/31/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENT MCDANIEL. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF GRAND LARCENY AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Rankin County (Mississippi), which sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole after he was convicted of grand larceny.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was ordered to work at a police department to pay off fines by washing cars and doing janitorial work. While working at the police department, a municipal court clerk noticed that a money bag was missing from a drawer at the municipal building. After acquiring defendant's consent, the police searched his car and found the money bag under the back seat. Defendant was found guilty of grand larceny. Prior to the grand larceny conviction, defendant had pled guilty to three charges of armed robberies, one strong arm robbery, and one other grand larceny charge. Therefore, defendant was sentenced as a habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (Rev. 2000). He was sentenced to life in prison without the possibility of parole. On appeal, defendant claimed that his sentence violated the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court found that he was sentenced within the mandatory statutory limits set out in § 99-19-83 for habitual offenders. Therefore, his sentence was not grossly disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Herring Gas Co. v. Miss. Empl. Sec. Comm'n


NO. 2004-CC-01765-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 530



July 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Herring Gas Co. v. Miss. Empl. Sec. Comm'n, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 913 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/19/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRM DECISION OF THE MISSISSIPPI EMPLOYMENT SECURITY COMMISSION BOARD OF REVIEW.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employer sought review of a decision of the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which affirmed a decision of appellee the Mississippi Employment Security Commission dismissing the employer's administrative appeal. The Commission had determined that the employer's appeal was untimely pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 71-5-517 (2005).


OVERVIEW: The former employee was terminated from her position as a secretary after the employer suspected that the employee was misappropriating employee property. The employee filed for unemployment benefits, and the claims examiner recommended payment of benefits. The notice of chargeability was mailed to the employer, along with a notice that the employer had 14 days in which to appeal the decision of the claims examiner. The employer did not file an appeal until 18 days after the deadline. The employer claimed that the appeal was based upon alleged new evidence concerning the employee's embezzlement activity. The Commission's Board of Review agreed with the hearing officer that the employer's notice of appeal was not timely and the circuit court affirmed. The circuit court found that the employer had failed to show good cause for filing an untimely appeal. Affirming, the court noted that it was undisputed that the employer had notice that the appeal needed to be filed within 14 days and that the employer did not comply. Because the employer did not file the appeal within the period specified in Miss. Code Ann. § 71-5-517 (2000), the Board properly refused to consider the new evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

Carbin v. State


NO. 2005-CP-00819-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


942 So. 2d 231; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 377



May 16, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Carbin v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 706 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 12, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Carbin v. State, 942 So. 2d 164, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 765 (Miss., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Carbin v. Mississippi, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 6145 (U.S., May 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/24/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tate County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of kidnapping, armed robbery, jail escape, conspiracy to commit jail escape, aggravated assault on a law enforcement officer, and grand larceny. He was sentenced to forty-five years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. His petition for post-conviction relief was dismissed as time-barred and as a successive writ. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his sentence was illegal, the indictment failed to allege an essential element, and his attorney was ineffective. The appellate court noted that by pleading guilty, defendant waived his right to a jury trial. Therefore, he had no standing to claim his right to a jury trial was violated. It was the burden of defendant to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that his claims were not barred as successive writs. Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(7) (Supp. 2005). Defendant did not even allege that these issues survived the successive writ bar.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

412 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02106-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


928 So. 2d 984; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 359



May 9, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/29/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF COUNT I, DRIVE-BY SHOOTING AND SENTENCE OF THIRTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH FIVE YEARS SUSPENDED; COUNT II, AGGRAVATED ASSAULT AND SENTENCE OF TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH TEN YEARS SUSPENDED TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE SENTENCE IN COUNT I. AND REIMBURSE JONES COUNTY THE AMOUNT OF $ 750.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of a drive-by shooting and aggravated assault. For the drive-by shooting defendant was sentenced to serve 30 years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections with five years suspended. He also received a sentence of 20 years with 10 years suspended for the aggravated assault charge, with the sentences to run consecutively. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's wife told him that she and defendant had been having an affair. While reconciling with the victim, the wife attempted to end the affair. One night defendant waited in his truck outside the restaurant where the victim worked as a manager. As the victim drove home, defendant followed him in his truck. Defendant then pulled his truck beside the victim's vehicle and shot the victim in the face with a 12 gauge shotgun and drove away. As a result of the shooting, the victim sustained serious, permanent, disfiguring injuries to his face and has, to date, endured eight of a series of twelve operations. Defendant failed to make an initial showing that his sentences were grossly disproportionate to the crimes he committed. Additionally, the appellate court disagreed that sentences of 30 years and 20 years were disproportionate to defendant's crimes because (1) he fired a 12 gauge shotgun at the victim while both men were driving, jeopardizing himself, the victim, and any other persons on the road that night; (2) defendant then ambushed the victim at home, where he attempted to shoot the victim again; and (3) the victim suffered a grievous injury to his face.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2004-KA-00784-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


935 So. 2d 1108; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 371



May 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Jackson v. State, 936 So. 2d 367, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 433 (Miss., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jackson v. Miss., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1079 (U.S., Jan. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF MORE THAN THIRTY GRAMS OF COCAINE WITH INTENT TO TRANSFER OR DISTRIBUTE WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A CHURCH AND SENTENCED TO SIXTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH FIFTY YEARS TO SERVE AND TEN YEARS SUSPENDED ON POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION AND FINE OF $ 25,000.00. AFFIRMED - 09/13/2005.
Jackson v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 631 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 13, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of possession of more than thirty grams of cocaine with the intent to transfer or distribute, with said act having been committed within 1,500 feet of a church. The Forrest County Circuit Court, Mississippi, sentenced defendant to a term of 60 years, with 10 years suspended on post-release supervision. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial that was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Investigation of a series of thefts from construction sites led the police to defendant's home. Defendant did not answer the door, but when the police called him on the phone, he agreed to come outside. The police explained why they were there and read defendant his Miranda rights. Defendant executed a consent form to search his house. The search revealed a large quantity of cocaine along with three adults. Defendant was found guilty and filed a motion for a new trial. On appeal, defendant assigned fifteen errors. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and held, inter alia, (1) the search of defendant's home was valid as defendant consented to search, (2) the trial court did not err in admitting hearsay testimony from an officer about a third party who had said there were stolen items at defendant's residence as the testimony was not offered for the truth of the matter asserted but to show why the officer was at defendant's home, and (3) defendant's sentence was not excessive as Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142 authorized a sentence up to twice the maximum sentence in Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139 where the sale of a controlled substance occurred within 1500 feet of a church.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

414 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Fulks v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01673-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


944 So. 2d 79; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 338



May 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Fulks v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 687 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 12, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Fulks v. State, 946 So. 2d 368, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 696 (Miss., 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Fulks v. King, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66881 (N.D. Miss., July 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLAY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/14/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: GUILTY OF TRANSFER OF A CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE AND SENTENCE OF SIXTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AS AN HABITUAL OFFENDER AND FINED TWO MILLION DOLLARS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clay County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of transfer of a controlled substance. Defendant was sentenced as a habitual offender, which imposed a sentence of 60 years not to be reduced, suspended, or eligible for probation or parole, in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections, in accordance with Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-147 (Rev. 2004). He was also fined two million dollars. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A confidential informant working with the Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics was wired with a video camera when he purchased crack cocaine from defendant During the first trial, the confidential informant testified against defendant. Defendant's attorney was allowed to cross-examine the confidential informant thoroughly. Defendant's first trial resulted in a mistrial as a result of a hung jury. Before the second trial began, the confidential informant died; therefore, he was unavailable to testify. The confidential informant's testimony from the first trial's transcript was read into evidence during the second trial. On appeal, defendant argued that the confidential informant's testimony from the previous trial should not have been allowed into evidence because defendant was not able to cross-examine the confidential informant and the jury was unable to observe the confidential informant's demeanor. When the transcript of prior testimony of an unavailable witness reflected extensive cross-examination, the former testimony was admissible under Miss. R. Evid. 804(b)(1). Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing that evidence under that hearsay exception.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

415 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Zinn v. City of Ocean Springs


NO. 2005-CA-00347-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


928 So. 2d 915; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 320



April 25, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/31/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED STATE LAW CLAIMS AND ENTERED DIRECTED VERDICT ON SECTION 1983 CLAIM IN FAVOR OF THE CITY AND OTHER DEFENDANTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual appealed the dismissal of her state law claims against appellees, city and individuals, and the directed verdict in favor of appellees in her claims pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: A third party bought two cats from the individual, and the cats were later found to be afflicted with fleas, ringworm, respiratory infection, and Giardia, a harmful parasite. The veterinarian told the third party to contact the health department to prevent the spread of the disease. After a complaint was filed, an animal control officer inspected the home with the individual's permission and found the home to be unsuitable for cats or humans. The cats were malnourished and had other health issues. A search warrant was issued based on the officer's inspection. The individual's cats were seized, and the present action was filed. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the state law claims as there was probable cause to search her home based on the consensual animal control inspection, and the individual's Sixth Amendment rights were not violated as they did not attach because the individual was not charged with a crime. The 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims were properly dismissed because the individual failed to prove that she was deprived of a right secured by the Constitution and that the city inflicted injury upon her in the execution of governmental policy or custom.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Edmonds v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02081-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


955 So. 2d 864; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 311



April 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Edmonds v. State, 933 So. 2d 982, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 375 (Miss., July 20, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Edmonds v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 7 (Miss., Jan. 4, 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Edmonds v. State, 955 So. 2d 787, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 349 (Miss., May 10, 2007)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Edmonds v. Oktibbeha County, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 126800 (N.D. Miss., Nov. 30, 2010)
Related proceeding at Edmonds v. State, 2017 Miss. LEXIS 269 (Miss., June 29, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/24/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS. AFFIRMED: 01/31/2006.
Edmonds v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 88 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 31, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of murder and sentencing him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 13 years old, was convicted of shooting the victim, his brother-in-law, to death. On appeal, the court held that defendant's confession was voluntary and intelligent and therefore his motion to suppress was properly dismissed because there was no merit to the argument that defendant's mother should have been present while he was being questioned about his involvement in the murder, if defendant's sister had applied the pressure that defendant contended at least one of his statements would have been more favorable to her, and defendant admitted to his mother that he and his sister killed the victim. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to allow a false juvenile confession expert to testify under Miss. R. Evid. 702 because the expert admitted that her theory could not be ethically tested, the proponents of the field of expert testimony regarding false confessions seemed to be a small group, the expert testified that there was no way to discern a possible rate of error in the filing of false confessions, and the trial court could not say that expert opinion in the field of false confessions was widely accepted within the scientific community.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Edmond v. Miller


NO. 2005-CP-00549-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


942 So. 2d 203; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 182



March 21, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Edmond v. Miller, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 754 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 1, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Edmond v. Miller, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 718 (Miss., Nov. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/1/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: WRIT OF MANDAMUS - DENIED AND DISMISSED.
Edmond v. State, 845 So. 2d 701, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 187 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Sunflower County (Mississippi) that denied his petition for a writ of mandamus naming appellees, the parole board and the board's chair, and alleging that the parole board had repeatedly denied his rights to due process and equal protection in failing to order a psychiatric evaluation prior to each of the inmate's parole hearings as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3 (1972).


OVERVIEW: The inmate's parole had been revoked and he was returned to prison to serve the rest of his life sentence on a rape conviction. The inmate sought a writ of mandamus after parole was denied several times, arguing that he was denied due process and equal protection due to the parole board's failure to give him a psychiatric evaluation prior to his parole hearings. The court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3 (1972) did not require an evaluation prior to a parole hearing; rather § 47-7-3 clearly stated that an inmate must be eligible for parole before he was entitled to a psychiatric evaluation. The court found that the inmate did not have a liberty interest in parole because Miss. Code Ann. §§ 47-7-3 and 47-7-17 used the permissive "may" and not the mandatory "shall." The court rejected the inmate's claim that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-27 was unconstitutionally vague because it applied to offenders who had previously had parole revoked, and clearly provided that the inmate's eligibility for a second parole was subject to the board's discretion, and that the inmate was only entitled to a psychological evaluation if the parole board exercised its discretion to grant him a second parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and assessed all costs of the appeal to the county.

 

418 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Ross v. Epps


NO. 2005-CP-00430-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


922 So. 2d 847; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 141



February 28, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/3/2005. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMING DECISION OF MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS TO DENY TRUSTY TIME ALLOWANCE.
Ross v. State, 802 So. 2d 171, 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 534 (Miss. Ct. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Greene County (Mississippi), which upheld a decision from the Mississippi Department of Corrections (MDOC) that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138.1 (Rev. 2004) was not an unconstitutional ex post facto law as applied to offenders who committed the crime of sale or manufacture of a controlled substance prior to the effective date of the amendment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the sale of cocaine and was sentenced to prison. He entered trusty status under § 47-5-138.1. Section 47-5-138.1 was amended in 2004 to allow a trusty time allowance of 30 days' reduction of sentence for 30 days' participation. However, under the amendment, an offender was not eligible for trusty status if the offender was convicted of trafficking in controlled substances. Defendant filed a petition with the MDOC Administrative Remedy Program, arguing that § 47-5-138.1, as amended, was an unconstitutional ex post facto law. The MDOC responded that while defendant would not be eligible for the 30 days' reduction for 30 days' participation, he would maintain the previous trusty time status of 10 days for 30 days. The trial court upheld the MDOC's decision. On appeal, the court found that the amendment to the statute did not, in any way, disadvantage defendant. He remained in the same position regardless of the amendment. Because he entered trusty status in 2002, he continued to receive the 10 days for 30 days time benefit under the prior statute. The statute did not violate the ex post facto clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Moore v. State


NO. 2004-KA-00275-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


938 So. 2d 1254; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 86



January 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Moore v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 408 (Miss. Ct. App., May 23, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. State, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 750 (Miss., Oct. 5, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. State, 939 So. 2d 805, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 749 (Miss., 2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Moore v. Jacquelyn Banks, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 128267 (S.D. Miss., Feb. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/30/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF KIDNAPPING: SENTENCED TO TWENTY-FIVE YEARS IMPRISONMENT AND PAYMENT OF $ 8,000 RESTITUTION; CONVICTED OF ROBBERY BY USE OF A DEADLY WEAPON: SENTENCED TO THIRTY YEARS IMPRISONMENT; SENTENCES TO RUN CONCURRENTLY.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of the crimes of kidnapping and robbery by use of a deadly weapon. For the kidnapping charge, he was sentenced to 25 years' imprisonment plus payment of restitution. For the armed robbery charge, he was sentenced to 30 years' imprisonment. The sentences were to run concurrently. His motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or a new trial was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two masked gunmen broke into the victims' home, bound them with duct tape, and proceeded to take their money, rings, and property, while repeatedly threatening to kill them during the 45 minute ordeal. Defendant, represented by appointed counsel, entered into a plea bargain with the State, in which he agreed to a plea of guilty to armed robbery and to testify truthfully against his co-defendant. During his co-defendant's trial, defendant refused to testify, despite his earlier plea agreement with the State. As a result of his refusal to testify, the State moved to revoke defendant's plea bargain, vacated the armed robbery sentence, and reinstated the kidnapping charge. Defendant's voluntary refusal to testify against his co-defendant constituted a material breach of the plea bargain. As a result of that breach, the parties were returned to the status quo ante, and defendant had no double jeopardy defense available concerning re-indictment and conviction on the charges. Also, the transcript of his guilty plea hearing clearly showed that he was aware that the State would seek to invalidate his plea and reinstate the charges if he failed to testify truthfully against his co-defendant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Edmonds v. State


NO. 2004-KA-02081-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 88



January 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, En banc, Modified and rehearing denied by Edmonds v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 311 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: OKTIBBEHA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/24/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES T. KITCHENS, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Oktibbeha County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of the murder of his half-sister's husband and sentencing him to life. Defendant was almost 14 at the time of the offense.


OVERVIEW: According to defendant's confession, he shot the victim in the head with a gun he brought at the request of the half-sister. Defendant and his mother signed a Miranda statement, then his mother left the room. The court held among other things: (1) Admission of defendant's confession was proper as it was not required that defendant's mother be present during questioning, and court was bound to apply the same standards for the voluntariness of the confession as it would for any confession; (2) considering the Daubert factors, the testimony of a false confession expert did not satisfy Miss. R. Evid. 702 because the hypothesis could not be tested empirically; (3) a doctor's testimony regarding the path of the projectile was not a previously undisclosed opinion that two people pulled the trigger; (4) a statement by a witness who had died that the half-sister asked to borrow a gun to shoot a dog was properly denied under Miss. R. Evid. 804(b)(5) because another witness testified to virtually the same information; (5) a statement the half-sister made to defendant's father about wanting to kill the victim was properly denied because it was never proven that the half-sister was unavailable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Passman v. State


NO. 2004-KP-02364-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


937 So. 2d 17; 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 89



January 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Passman v. State, 936 So. 2d 367, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 482 (Miss., 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Passman v. Miss., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3842 (U.S., Apr. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/8/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MIKE SMITH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: JURY VERDICT OF GUILTY OF POSSESSION OF METHAMPHETAMINE WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE WHILE IN POSSESSION OF A FIREARM, AND SENTENCED OF SIXTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS, A TWO MILLION DOLLAR FINE AND FIFTY DOLLARS RESTITUTION TO THE MISSISSIPPI BUREAU OF NARCOTICS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of possession of methamphetamine with intent to distribute and with possession of a firearm while intending to distribute; and sentenced him to an enhanced 60 year sentence in prison under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-152 (Rev. 2005), two million dollar fine and fifty dollars restitution to the Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after police recorded telephone conversations between defendant and a confidential informant regarding the sale of methamphetamine. When police went to defendant's house, he refused consent for police to search the home. Police obtained a search warrant and found a gun, drugs, scales, and a police scanner. Defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was denied. On appeal, the court held that defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied because the defendant's arrest and the search warrant were based on probable cause to believe defendant had or was committing a crime, where defendant admitted he had drug paraphernalia in the house, and the informant's reliability was corroborated by the recording of the conversations. The court also held that defendant's enhanced sentence under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-152 was not disproportionate and did not amount to cruel and unusual punishment because his sentence did not exceed the statutory limits. Also, the trial court was not required under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-149 to reduce the statutory sentence for first time offenders. The court rejected defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant for possession of methamphetamine with intent to distribute and with possession of a firearm while intending to distribute.

Edwards v. State


NO. 2004-CP-02331-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


916 So. 2d 542; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 1018



December 13, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PONTOTOC COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/6/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SHARION R. AYCOCK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF - DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a motion for post-conviction relief after he pled guilty to two counts of sale of cocaine. The Pontotoc County Court, Mississippi, dismissed the inmate's motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his motion, the inmate claimed (1) that his sentence was illegal; (2) that his due process rights were violated because of a flawed indictment; (3) that his right to effective assistance of counsel was violated; and (4) that his guilty plea was involuntary and unknowing. The appellate court affirmed the denial of the inmate's motion and held that (1) the inmate's sentence was not illegal as the maximum punishment for possession of cocaine under Miss. OUTCOME: The denial of the motion for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

Bradley v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01260-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


934 So. 2d 1018; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 1015



December 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bradley v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 280 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 11, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Bradley v. State, 933 So. 2d 982, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 394 (Miss., 2006)
Related proceeding at Bradley v. Jordan, 2016 Miss. LEXIS 28 (Miss., Jan. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/15/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF POSSESSION OF A FIREARM BY A FELON AND SENTENCE OF LIFE AS AN HABITUAL OFFENDER IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted as an habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (2000) on the charge of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 (2000). After his motion to suppress any and all tangible evidence, statements, and information acquired by the State was denied, he was convicted, and a life sentence was imposed. He appealed on numerous grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested pursuant to a felony warrant. Later at the police station, during an inventory search of his suitcase, a firearm was recovered. Defendant asserted that the search of his suitcase was in violation of the Fourth Amendment and that he was entitled to a second Miranda warning once the officers confronted him with the gun they discovered in his suitcase. However, the appellate court held the gun was the result of a valid search; therefore, his confession (admitting that he was holding the gun for a friend), which stemmed from the fruit of the search, was also admissible. Secondly, during trial, while the testimony regarding defendant's prior arrest for kidnaping was improper (apparently, a charge for which he was not convicted), the trial judge sustained the objection and instructed the jury to disregard the testimony. Thus, defendant did not suffer prejudice. Third, where defendant had two prior felonies, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-37-5 (2000) did not limit the State to proving that defendant had only been convicted of one prior felony. Finally, counsel was not ineffective for failing to "timely" file a motion to suppress. Again, the evidence at issue was admissible.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Jordan v. State


NO. 2002-KA-02057-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


936 So. 2d 368; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 830



November 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Jordan v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 39 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 17, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Jordan v. State, 929 So. 2d 923, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 270 (Miss., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/6/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BOBBY BURT DELAUGHTER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF TWO COUNTS OF KIDNAPING, TWO COUNTS OF SEXUAL BATTERY, AND ONE COUNT OF RAPE. SENTENCE OF 160 YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of two charges of kidnaping, two charges of sexual battery, and one charge of rape. The Hinds County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi) sentenced him to a 160 year term in the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant filed unsuccessful motions for a directed verdict, for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant claimed that the sexual battery and rape charges were duplicitous, giving rise to a double jeopardy violation. He argued that the elements of rape were the same as sexual battery as both required a sex act against a victim's will. The appellate court held that there was no merit to defendant's claim. The jury found him guilty of one charge of rape and two charges of sexual battery. The rape charge was incident to forced intercourse and the two sexual battery charges followed forced oral sex and sodomy. Rape and sexual battery were not duplicitous. Rape was forcible sexual intercourse. Sodomy could never qualify with the statutory definition of rape. Likewise, oral sex could never fall within the statutory meaning of rape. Sexual battery, involved unconsented "sexual penetration." "Sexual penetration" could include intercourse, sodomy, or fellatio. The three charges clearly alleged three distinctly separate acts, they were not duplicitous and they did not expose defendant to double jeopardy. In another issue, since defendant's sentence for any one count was not greater than the maximum sentence for that count, the sentence could not be disturbed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Parker v. State


NO. 2003-KA-02593-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


917 So. 2d 120; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 835



November 8, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/21/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE B. READY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF RAPE AND SENTENCE OF THIRTY YEARS, TWENTY-FIVE SUSPENDED, IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DeSoto County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted his motion for a directed verdict, request for peremptory instruction, or his motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict; and his conviction was void because the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional. The appellate court determined that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The victim testified that she became very drunk and blacked out; when she awoke, she was naked in defendant's bedroom. The subsequent birth and DNA match corroborated the sexual assault. The victim's testimony regarding the effect that the alcohol had on her was sufficient to show that it was defendant's administration of alcohol that caused her to be unable to resist or consent to his sexual advances. Defendant's behavior violated Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-65(4), and he knew or should have known that his conduct was prohibited. The statute intended to prohibit and penalize someone who administered to another a substance or liquid that caused the other to be incapable of consenting or resisting sexual intercourse, and thereafter proceeded to have sexual intercourse with the incapacitated individual.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Smith v. State


NO. 2004-CP-01205-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


914 So. 2d 330; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 793



November 1, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/27/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Smith v. State, 708 So. 2d 103, 1998 Miss. App. LEXIS 332 (Miss. Ct. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted in the Harrison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, for the offense of kidnapping and sexual battery. He received 2 concurrent sentences of 20 years in prison. Some six years after his conviction, he requested and received leave from the Mississippi Supreme Court to file a "motion to correct sentence"; however, the trial court denied the motion. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that his "motion to correct sentence" should have been granted because he was illegally sentenced under a statute that was not in effect at the time of his crime, and as a result he had been improperly denied parole. The trial court and the State contended that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 did not apply to appellant. The appellate court noted that in Puckett v. Abels, the Mississippi Supreme Court ruled that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 was an unconstitutional ex post facto law when applied to persons who were charged with committing crimes prior to July 1, 1995, but who were not to be sentenced until on or after July 1, 1995. Appellant committed his crimes on September 2, 1994, he was indicted on February 24, 1995, and he was sentenced on September 7, 1995. The appellate court concluded that applying Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 to appellant was clearly impermissible. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3, because he was an offender over the age of 19, he was clearly ineligible for parole.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Ramage v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


914 So. 2d 274; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 772



October 25, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Ramage v. Thornton, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29835 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/22/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate fell asleep at the wheel while under the influence of drugs and alcohol, killing his two passengers. He pled guilty to aggravated DUI in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(5) (Supp. 2001) (amended 2002 and 2004), and culpable negligence manslaughter in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-47 (Rev. 2000), and currently appealed the denial of his motion for post-conviction relief. The court affirmed however, stating that the two convictions did not subject him to double jeopardy because aggravated DUI required an element not required by culpable negligence manslaughter, which was intoxication. The inmate argued that the trial judge violated Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-2 (Rev. 2000) by entering a single order sentencing him for both of the offenses for which he was convicted, but the court disagreed, stating that the circuit court imposed separate sentences for each count of the indictment. His counsel was not ineffective because the inmate failed to prove deficient performance on the part of his counsel since there was no double jeopardy violation and the indictment against him was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:

Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Supp. 2004). The Mississippi Supreme Court had specifically held that claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were subject to the three-year statute of limitations.

Foster v. State


NO. 2004-KA-01470-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


928 So. 2d 873; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 733



October 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Foster v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 212 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 14, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Foster v. State, 929 So. 2d 923, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 309 (Miss., May 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PRENTISS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/1/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF POSSESSION OF MARIJUANA WITH INTENT TO SELL WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A PUBLIC PARK AND SENTENCED AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER TO FORTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC WITHOUT THE BENEFIT OF PAROLE AND A $ 60,000 FINE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Prentiss County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of the possession of 73.7 grams of marijuana with the intent to distribute in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(a)(1) (Rev. 2001). He was also sentenced as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Rev. 2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appeal followed his conviction of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute. Due to his proximity to a public park, his conviction carried an enhanced sentence pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142(1) (Rev. 2001). Additionally, the trial court sentenced him as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Rev. 2000). On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that the State did not fail to prove that the park was a public park. There was a wealth of testimony that indicated that the park was a city park and was maintained by the city. Viewed in a light most favorable to the State, a reasonable juror would have been justified in concluding that a city park would have been available for public use. Although the trial court abused its discretion when it permitted the State to introduce evidence forbidden by Miss. R. Evid. 803(5), the court was unable to say that the trial court's decision prejudiced defendant's case. The trial court did not err in overruling his motion to suppress his statement because defendant himself initiated the contact with the officer and also signed a document by which he waived his Miranda rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jackson v. State


NO. 2004-KA-00784-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 631



September 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Jackson v. State, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 371 (Miss. Ct. App., May 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/19/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT B. HELFRICH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF MORE THAN THIRTY GRAMS OF COCAINE WITH INTENT TO TRANSFER OR DISTRIBUTE WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A CHURCH AND SENTENCED TO SIXTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH FIFTY YEARS TO SERVE AND TEN YEARS SUSPENDED ON POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION AND FINE OF $ 25,000.00.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Forrest County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine with the intent to transfer or distribute, within 1,500 feet of a church. Defendant was sentenced to 60 years in prison with 10 years suspended on post-release supervision. Defendant's motion for a new trial or, in the alternative, a judgment notwithstanding the verdict was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant maintained that the trial court erroneously denied his motion to suppress. The officers proceeded to search defendant's property only after being authorized to do so, pursuant to the consent to search form executed by defendant in writing. There was no error in admitting a police officer's testimony to show why he was at defendant's residence. There was no error in introducing evidence of the cocaine seized as defendant offered no proof of either a break in the chain of custody or any tampering with the evidence. A police officer's fingerprint opinion testimony was admissible under Miss. R. Evid. 701. The trial court did not err in instructing the jury that it could consider the street value of the cocaine when determining whether the substance was possessed with intent to distribute. The indictment gave proper notice to defendant, even though it contained an error of imprecise language. Defendant's sentence was within the statutory limits and not disproportionate to the crime he committed, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142(1). As there was no reversible error in any part, there was no reversible error to the whole.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Eastman v. State


NO. 2004-CP-00877-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


909 So. 2d 171; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 583



August 23, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/6/2004. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: REVERSE AND RENDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Monroe County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief as moot as defendant had been released from prison upon an administrative error. He was then re-incarcerated to serve the remaining portion of his ten year sentence. His motion to reinstate his petition for post-conviction relief was granted, and then denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by restructuring the sentence imposed from concurrent to consecutive, thereby increasing the total term of imprisonment imposed and subjecting him to double jeopardy. After failing several times to conduct himself with the terms of his probation, defendant's sentence was restructured to change the original concurrent fifteen year sentence received to a consecutive ten year sentence. The appellate court found that the trial court acted improperly by amending the initial sentence. The Mississippi Supreme Court adopted the legal theory that once a circuit or county court exercised its option to impose a definite sentence it could not subsequently set that sentence aside and impose a greater sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and rendered.

Magee v. State


NO. 2003-KA-02358-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


914 So. 2d 729; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 415



June 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Magee v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 720 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 11, 2005)
Related proceeding at McGee v. Krebs, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 155837 (S.D. Miss., Nov. 18, 2015)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McGee v. Jackaquline Banks, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 89033 (S.D. Miss., June 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/4/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: THE DEFENDANT WAS FOUND GUILTY OF MURDER AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of murder and sentenced to life in prison in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met the victim in a bar. They drove to a bridge, argued over the price of sex, and he punched her and then threw her over the bridge railing into a river, where she drowned. Defendant argued that his counsel was ineffective for failing to request a mental evaluation of his competence to stand trial. However, the defense made a motion to have defendant examined for competency, and the mental evaluation was in fact performed. Counsel's motion to try separately the issues of insanity and the merits of the case was a defense strategy and not grounds for an ineffectiveness claim. The court assumed that the mental evaluation, which was not in the record, dispelled the lower court's question that defendant could be incompetent to stand trial; hence, the trial court was not required to hold a hearing under Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. R. 9.06. The trial court's order of a mental evaluation was not a finding of reasonable ground entitling defendant to a competency hearing, because under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-13-11, no reasonable ground was required for an evaluation. The court rejected defendant's constitutional challenges to Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-139(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel without prejudice to his ability to seek post-conviction relief on this ground. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

Kiker v. State


NO. 2003-KA-02376-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


919 So. 2d 190; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 372



June 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Kiker v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 721 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 11, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Kiker v. State, 921 So. 2d 1279, 2006 Miss. LEXIS 40 (Miss., 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Kiker v. Hood, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 63623 (S.D. Miss., Aug. 27, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Kiker v. State, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 782 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/1/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT P. KREBS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: GUILTY OF MURDER; SENTENCED TO LIFE IN PRISON IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life in prison in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant moved for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or in the alternative, a new trial. The Circuit Court of George County (Mississippi) denied his motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it allowed a witness to testify in the State's rebuttal case because he remained in the courtroom for much of the testimony of the State's case-in-chief. The appellate court found no error, noting that when the State realized that the witness was going to testify, he was removed from the courtroom. As for the contention that it was reversible error for the trial court not to have administered the capital juror oath, the appellate court disagreed, noting that the oath administered was substantially equivalent. The appellate court also concluded that testimony that defendant was seen holding the gun used and that gunshot residue was only found on defendant was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. The appellate court further concluded that the admission into evidence of photographs of the scene was proper because they were probative of various issues before the jury. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the trial court did not err in preventing the victim's mother from testifying about a statement made by defendant an hour after the incident because it was too remote to be an excited utterance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Davis v. State


NO. 2003-KA-00988-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


914 So. 2d 200; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 269



April 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Davis v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 514 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 2, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Davis v. State, 921 So. 2d 344, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 746 (Miss., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davis v. Miss., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6743 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 1/16/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DALE HARKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CAPITAL MURDER - SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(a) (Rev. 2000) and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his capital murder conviction, but the court affirmed on appeal, stating that depraved heart murder subsumed "deliberate design/premeditated murder." Therefore, the depraved heart murder instruction did not constructively amend the indictment. Further, the indictment cited to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(a) (Rev. 2000), which made the case a capital offense and informed defendant of what made his offense a capital crime. Because defendant did not request a sentencing hearing prior to the imposition of his sentence, that issue was procedurally barred. Even absent a procedural bar, however, the issue lacked merit. Section § 97-3-19(2) did not violate U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV because the fact that Mississippi's capital murder scheme made the death penalty a possible punishment for felony murder where there was no requirement to prove an intent to kill, and not premeditated murder, did not make the Mississippi capital murder statute unconstitutional. The evidence was substantial to support the verdict based on the testimony of an officer and the fact that the credibility of the witnesses' testimony and its weight was for the jury to resolve.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Farmer v. State Dep't of Pub. Safety


NO. 2004-CA-00647-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


907 So. 2d 981; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 156



March 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Farmer v. State Dep't of Pub. Safety, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 320 (Miss. Ct. App., May 10, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Farmer v. State Dep't of Pub. Safety, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 461 (Miss., July 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/9/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PLAINTIFFS' CLAIMS DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, five former officers, brought an action against appellee, the Mississippi Department of Public Safety, asserting that they possessed a right in equity to unused leave time. The Chancery Court in the First Judicial District of Hinds County, Mississippi, granted the Department's motion to dismiss on the grounds of res judicata, collateral estoppel, and/or for the failure to exhaust all administrative remedies. The officers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the officers were entitled to equitable review of their claims relating to compensation and retirement benefits, which were excluded from state service grievance procedures. A first officer had tried the issue on appeal before the Mississippi Supreme Court previously. Upon the release of the aforementioned decision, the remaining officers' cases were dismissed by the circuit courts. All officers then sought equitable relief in a single action. Central to the officers' appeal was Miss. Code Ann. § 25-13-11(e) (Rev. 2003), which at the time their cause of action accrued provided, in part, that the aggregate amount of the employer's annuity and prior service annuity would not exceed more than 85 percent of the average compensation regardless of the years of service. In the first officer's individual action, the Mississippi Supreme Court had already found § 25-13-11(e) constitutional. As said former decision addressed the claims at issue in the instant proceeding, said issues could not again be litigated in the form of an equitable issue. Thus, the officers' grievances were barred for the reasons set forth by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs on appeal were assessed to the officers.

Moore v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01663-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


914 So. 2d 185; 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 60



January 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Moore v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 610 (Miss. Ct. App., Sept. 6, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Moore v. State, 921 So. 2d 344, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 745 (Miss., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Moore v. State, 2013 Miss. App. LEXIS 145 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 2, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 5/30/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CAPITAL MURDER - LIFE SENTENCE IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of the capital murder of the deceased victim. Defendant was sentenced to serve a term of life imprisonment in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his Batson challenge, defendant did not establish a prima facie case that the State excluded jurors on the basis of race, thus there was no need for the State to present race-neutral reasons for its peremptory strikes. Additionally, there was ample evidence to support the guilty verdict for capital murder because (1) an accomplice testified that he and defendant attempted to rob the victims and thus proved the underlying felony of robbery, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79; (2) three detectives testified that defendant confessed to shooting the deceased victim; and (3) defendant's letters to the accomplice apparently expressed his concern in the accomplice's testimony against him. Because the evidence was not such that reasonable jurors could only find defendant not guilty, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss and for a judgment of acquittal. In addition, the appellate court could not say that the trial judge abused his discretion in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial because he did not suffer serious and irreparable damage from the investigator's statement inferring that defendant was incarcerated when he interviewed him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Sweat v. State


NO. 2003-CP-00909-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


910 So. 2d 12; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1110



November 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by Sweat v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 162 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 1, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted Sweat v. State, 904 So. 2d 184, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 374 (Miss., 2005)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Sweat v. State, 912 So. 2d 458, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 661 (Miss., Oct. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 4/14/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PAUL S. FUNDERBURK. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Itawamba County (Mississippi), which denied his motion for postconviction relief after he pled guilty to conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a prior convicted felon, pled guilty to conspiracy to manufacture methamphetamine. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison, with 12 years suspended and five years of post-release supervision. The trial court dismissed his motion for postconviction relief. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in suspending a portion of defendant's sentence. It was not disputed that defendant was a prior convicted felon. Because he was a prior convicted felon, the trial court did not have the authority under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-33 (Rev. 2004) to suspend the imposition or execution of his sentence. As to defendant's remaining contentions, the court found that it was clear from the transcript of the guilty plea hearing that he understood that the maximum sentence for his crime was 20 years, that his plea was an open plea, and that the trial court could sentence him to the maximum, regardless of the State's recommendation. Hence, his guilty plea was knowingly and voluntarily entered. The court further found that defendant was not entitled to relief on his Fourth Amendment claim, because he waived his right to challenge the State's evidence by entering a valid guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for the entrance of a proper sentencing order. The court affirmed the order of the trial court in all other respects.
