Myers v. State


NO. 2003-CP-00218-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


897 So. 2d 198; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1185



November 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Myers v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 41 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/31/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. STEPHEN B. SIMPSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that denied his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant had pled guilty to sexual battery and received a suspended 10-year sentence and was placed on post-release supervision for three years and probation, which was later revoked for violating the terms of his post-release supervision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of post-conviction relief. Defendant had pled guilty to sexual battery based upon a charge that he ordered his victim at knife point to perform oral sex. On appeal, defendant argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel; his guilty plea was involuntary; he was not competent to enter a plea of guilty; and that he received an illegal sentence because he had two prior convictions and was not entitled to a suspended sentence as provided in Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-33. The court held that defendant failed to establish that his attorney's performance was deficient because the record showed that he was advised of the charges and all possible defenses and sentences. The court agreed with the trial court's finding that defendant failed to provide sufficient evidence regarding his alleged mental disorder. The court found that defendant did not plead guilty as a result of an offer of a suspended sentence because he clearly understood that he could have received the maximum of 30 years; also he benefited from the illegal sentence since it was more lenient than he was actually entitled to receive, thus he did not suffer any fundamental unfairness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Jones v. State


NO. 2003-KA-00470-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


902 So. 2d 593; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1011



November 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing, en banc, denied by Jones v. State, 2005 Miss. App. LEXIS 143 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 22, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Jones v. State, 901 So. 2d 1273, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 336 (Miss., 2005)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jones v. Waller, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47923 (N.D. Miss., May 30, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of robbery and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83(3) (Rev. 2000). Defendant claimed errors regarding the indictment, the lack of a competency hearing, the peremptory challenges, the identifications, his speedy trial right, refused instructions, and the proportionality of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for robbery and sentenced to life imprisonment as a habitual offender after snatching a woman's purse in a store parking lot. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's claim that the timing of the amendment of the habitual offender portion of the indictment did not allow him sufficient time to prepare his defense. The court held that it was within the trial court's discretion to decide whether to hold a competency hearing. The court noted that the principal offense of robbery was not a capital crime, and thus defendant was not entitled to 12 peremptory challenges under Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. R. 10.01 and Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-3 (2004). The court found that defendant failed to present any evidence of an improperly suggestive pretrial identification by the victim that tainted subsequent identifications at trial. There was no violation of defendant's constitutional or statutory right to a speedy trial because he was responsible for much of the 37-month delay. The court concluded that there was no inference that the habitual offender sentence was disproportionate where defendant had four felony convictions, with two for violent crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of robbery and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a habitual offender.

Hodges v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01577-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI

November 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari dismissed Hodges v. State, 904 So. 2d 184, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 348 (Miss., 2005)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Hodges v. Goff, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66433 (S.D. Miss., July 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 8/30/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MIKE SMITH TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: UNLAWFUL POSSESSION OF MARIJUANA, WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE WITHIN 1,500 FEET OF A SCHOOL - SENTENCED TO FORTY YEARS, TO SERVE THE FIRST TWENTY YEARS WITH THE REMAINING TWENTY TO BE SERVED UNDER POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION AND TO PAY A FINE OF $ 25,000, AND RESTITUTION OF $ 10,000.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pike County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of possession of marijuana, with the intent to distribute the same within 1,500 feet of a school. He was sentenced to serve a term of 40 years, with 20 years suspended, and ordered to pay a fine of $25,000. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him to forty years and in denying his post-trial motions. Defendant argued that the informant, who provided information establishing probable cause for the search warrant, was not reliable. The appellate court noted that defendant did not raise the issue at trial. The issue was without merit where testimony established that the informant was searched before the initial buy and subsequent attempted buy. The transactions were recorded. The informant had worked as a confidential informant prior to the transaction. Defendant's sentence was neither excessive nor did it exceed the bounds of the penalty allowed under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-142(1) (Rev. 2000). Since he did not contend that the sentence was unconstitutional and allow the trial judge an opportunity to consider the issue, he could not assert this allegation on appeal. Because the sentence was within the guidelines of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b)(1), it was not disproportionate to the crime charged. The jury chose to believe the State's witnesses, which emphasized that the evidence placed before the jury by the State was more credible than defendant's testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Pittman v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01509-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


904 So. 2d 1185; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1043



November 2, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 8/15/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF POSSESSION OF PRECURSOR CHEMICALS WITH THE INTENT TO MANUFACTURE METHAMPHETAMINES; SENTENCED TO TWENTY-FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AND ORDERED TO PAY A FINE OF $ 10,000.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a couple, were convicted of possession of precursor chemicals with the intent to manufacture methamphetamines in the Circuit Court of Greene County, Mississippi. Both were sentenced to a term of 25 years. They appealed, asserting, in part, that the search warrant was not valid for want of probable cause, that the State failed to establish a proper chain of custody, and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain their convictions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendants argued that an "underlying facts and circumstances" sheet was not attached to the affidavit for the search warrant and that no information was given to establish the reliability of the informant. However, the "totality of the circumstances" standard for determining the existence of probable cause applied. The officer who applied for the search warrant gave detailed information regarding the location of the residence where the drugs were being manufactured and testified that the informant, an eyewitness, stated that he bought and supplied defendants with precursor elements. Thus, there was sufficient probable cause to support the search warrant. Secondly, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the State failed to establish a proper chain of custody by not producing to testify, every officer that seized an item the State wanted to introduce into evidence. Finally, the fact the State sought and obtained the removal of one precursor chemical from the indictment caused no prejudice to defendants, where the State did prove they possessed two or more precursor chemicals, and defendants' sentences, within the statutory limits, was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed.

Odem v. State


NO. 2002-KM-01689-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


881 So. 2d 940; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 899



September 7, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 9/20/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM E. CHAPMAN, III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: RESISTING ARREST, COUNTS I AND II: SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF SIX MONTHS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MADISON COUNTY SHERIFF IN CAUSE NO. 2000-0411, COUNT I, AND TO SERVE SIX MONTHS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MADISON COUNTY SHERIFF IN CAUSE NO. 2000-0411, COUNT II. PROVIDED, HOWEVER, THAT THE EXECUTION OF THE LAST SIX MONTHS IS STAYED AND THAT PORTION OF THE SENTENCES IS/ARE SUSPENDED ON THE TERMS, PROVISIONS AND CONDITIONS PRESCRIBED ELSEWHERE IN THIS ORDER. THE SENTENCES IMPOSED IN COUNT II SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO THE SENTENCE IMPOSED IN COUNT I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of two counts of misdemeanor resisting arrest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was unlawfully arrested for his spoken words alone in violation of his right to freedom of speech. The court of appeals disagreed. The confrontation occurred not out in public but at the sheriff's department. The officer neither initiated nor had an opportunity to walk away from defendant's words and combative conduct. Defendant became agitated and began shouting profanities when the officer told him about the protocol he would have to follow to retrieve his vehicle from the impound lot. Defendant expressed his displeasure with the inconvenience. Defendant did not stop with simply expressing his displeasure. He was combative, and he created a stalemate that arose to the level of "fighting words" that were likely to inflict injury or incite an immediate breach of the peace. Indeed, defendant indicated no intent to back down until the officer gave him his vehicle without following the proper procedure.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist.


NO. 2003-CA-01062-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


910 So. 2d 1; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 761



August 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Green v. Cleary Water, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1059 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 26, 2004)
Writ of certiorari granted Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 892 So. 2d 824, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 70 (Miss., 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Green v. Cleary Water, Sewer & Fire Dist., 910 So. 2d 1022, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 394 (Miss., June 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 4/17/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JASON H. FLOYD, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGMENT GRANTED TO CLEARY WATER, SEWER & FIRE DISTRICT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City and residents, sought review of a judgment of the Rankin County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment to appellee, the water, sewer & fire district, in the residents' action seeking a declaratory judgment and an injunction to enjoin the district from disengaging water service to individuals who refused to comply with an ordinance regulating individual on-site wastewater disposal systems.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that the district lacked the authority to enact the ordinance that regulated individual wastewater systems and that the ordinance was preempted by the Mississippi Individual On-Site Wastewater Disposal System Law, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 41-67-1 to 41-67-31 (Rev. 2001). The district argued that the ordinance was not preempted by § 41-67-31and that it was enacted pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 19-5-173 (Rev. 2003). The court found that the district acted under the authority of its general police powers and that the ordinance was a valid exercise of its authority under § 19-5-173. The court noted that the Wastewater Law did not mention sewer districts and did not expressly prevent sewer districts from regulating individual on-site wastewater disposal systems. Also the court held that the Wastewater Law did not repeal Miss. Code Ann. § 19-5-173, which gave the district the power to regulate the general health of its residents. The court noted that the ordinance was adopted at the request of the Department of Health, which was the agency given the authority under the Wastewater Law over wastewater disposal systems.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and taxed costs to appellants.

King v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00928-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


897 So. 2d 981; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 689



July 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by King v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 1181 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2004)
Writ of certiorari denied King v. State, 896 So. 2d 373, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 224 (Miss., Mar. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WALTHALL COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 3/22/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MIKE SMITH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED ON SIX COUNTS OF SALES TAX EVASION AND, FOR EACH COUNT, ORDERED TO PAY A $20,000 FINE AND SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF FIVE YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC ON EACH COUNT WITH TERMS TO BE SERVED CONSECUTIVELY TO EACH OTHER AND TO ANY OTHER SENTENCES PREVIOUSLY IMPOSED.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Walthall County Circuit Court, Mississippi, of tax evasion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant built a business based on the sale of peanut brittle, which generated substantial income. On appeal, defendant argued that his conviction violated the prohibition against double jeopardy. Defendant also claimed, among other things, that the jury instructions were improper, that certain evidence should have been suppressed, that counsel rendered ineffective assistance, that the cumulative effect of the errors destroyed the trial's fundamental fairness, and that the evidence was insufficient. This matter, however, had already been litigated. Counsel did not render ineffective assistance. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction; there was no reversible error in any single part of the trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Vinson v. Prather


NO. 2003-CP-01648-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


879 So. 2d 1053; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 555



June 15, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Vinson v. Prather, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 889 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: UNION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 6/20/2003. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM R. LAMB. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: COMPLAINT DISMISSED FOR FAILURE TO STATE A CLAIM UPON WHICH RELIEF CAN BE GRANTED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals brought suit against appellee supreme court chief justice arguing that the chief justice violated their due process rights by appointing a special chancellor to hear outstanding matters regarding two underlying cases that had been recently appealed to the supreme court. The Union County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed the individuals' complaint with prejudice. The individuals appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the individuals contended the trial court erred by dismissing their complaint pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) as it looked outside the pleading when it considered three exhibits attached to the chief justice's motion to dismiss. The appellate court disagreed, finding no evidence that the trial court considered anything outside the pleadings, especially when no discovery had been propounded. Even so, the trial court could have considered information outside the pleadings without converting the dismissal motion into one for summary judgment. The appellate court also found that the chief justice enjoyed the protection of judicial immunity as she had no authority to act as she did in appointing a special chancellor other than by virtue of her position as chief justice. Further, an appointment pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 9-1-105 was a judicial act; the individuals' attempt to label the appointment as administrative or non-adjudicative was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bell v. State


NO. 2002-CP-01627-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


886 So. 2d 739; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 456



May 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bell v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 915 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 24, 2004)
Writ of certiorari denied Bell v. State, 887 So. 2d 183, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1386 (Miss., 2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Bell v. Miss. Dep't of Corr., 118 Fed. Appx. 874, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 166 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bell v. Mississippi, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2526 (U.S., Mar. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 8/6/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.
Bell v. State, 751 So. 2d 1035, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 400 (Miss., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed from an order entered in the Circuit Court of Forrest County, Mississippi, denying his motion for post-conviction relief. Two issues were raised on appeal: 1) whether he waived his double jeopardy claim by pleading guilty to armed robbery and 2) whether double jeopardy occurred in violation of his constitutional rights when he was re-indicted for the same armed robbery which secured his conviction of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of capital murder in 1977 and sentenced to death. The death sentence was subsequently overturned and a life sentence was imposed. In 1996, the inmate filed his first petition for post-conviction relief claiming that he had an ex post facto claim. The state supreme court affirmed that the inmate had waived those claims. In his second petition for post-conviction relief, the inmate claimed that the trial court committed reversible error by sentencing him for armed robbery since that same crime was the underlying felony used to elevate the killing of the victim to capital murder. The appellate court affirmed the denial of the inmate's motion for post-conviction relief as the inmate did not cite any intervening cases or newly discovered evidence that would except his claim from the procedural bar in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-27(9) (Rev. 2000). Further, the inmate's claim was time barred as it was not filed within three years after entry of the judgment of conviction as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Supp. 2002).


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

In the Interest of C.A.


NO. 2003-CA-00060-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


872 So. 2d 705; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 405



May 4, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re C.A., 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 511 (Miss. Ct. App., May 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY YOUTH COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/17/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GAYLON K HARPER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MINOR CHILD ADJUDICATED A DELINQUENT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Youth Court Division of the County Court of Jones County adjudicated appellant juvenile a delinquent on a petition alleging a violation of the simple assault statute by knowingly, and unlawfully causing bodily injury to the victim, another minor, by touching the victim's private area. Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The petition in the case stated that appellant did purposely, knowingly, and unlawfully cause bodily injury to the victim by touching him in his private area in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7(1)(a). Appellant claimed that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt each element of the crime of simple assault. Specifically, appellant argued that the State did not carry its burden because no evidence was adduced that the victim suffered any bodily injury. The appellate court found that the petition did not give the trial judge the option of an attempt charge in this simple assault case. Additionally, the record was devoid of any questions or answers regarding injury to the victim. Although touching was mentioned, even by the victim, there was nothing about pain, hurt, or injury caused at the hands of appellant. Thus, the State failed to prove all of the elements of simple assault as charged in the petition and appellant was improperly adjudicated a delinquent.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed appellant's adjudication as a delinquent and rendered judgment in favor of appellant.

Robinson v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01238-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


875 So. 2d 230; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 275



April 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Robinson v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 704 (Miss. Ct. App., June 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 7/22/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC S. RICHARDSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF MANSLAUGHTER AND SENTENCED TO TWENTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of manslaughter and sentenced her to 20 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the fact that the victim had been treated for anger management in a prior unspecified year did not prove that, during the period of time leading up to the killing, he had engaged in such aggressive and violent behavior with defendant so as to warrant her having a reasonable apprehension that, in any altercation between them, he was likely to do her serious bodily harm. Defendant did not testify that the victim was still engaging in aggressive and uncontrollable behavior toward her or that his past behavior toward her left her apprehensive of him. Hence, the trial court did not commit reversible error when it failed to review the victim's medical records and take testimony from the victim's psychotherapist before ruling that the victim had not waived the medical privilege by taking defendant to one of his psychotherapy sessions. The court further found no merit to defendant's insufficiency of the evidence argument. The court's reading of the record convinced it that the jury was more than generous to defendant in not returning a verdict of murder. Finally, the court found no merit to defendant's argument that her 20-year sentence was excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

McCray v. State


NO. 2002-CP-02044-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


869 So. 2d 442; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 247



March 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at McCray v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 351 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 11/15/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MIKE SMITH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF MOTION DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pike County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of murder, pursuant to a guilty plea, and sentenced him to life in prison. Defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a free copy of his plea hearing transcript. The appellate court disagreed. Defendant's motion for record was not filed until after the trial judge denied his motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant's motion for record was untimely. Even if defendant's motion for record was timely filed and denied, an inmate was not entitled to a free transcript in a post-conviction relief setting, if his post-conviction motion could not withstand summary dismissal under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-11(2). The law did not require the State to furnish the documents free of charge under the circumstances. Defendant attempted to raise an involuntary guilty plea for the first time in his motion for reconsideration and attempted to raise it again in his amended and rebuttal briefs. Defendant chose not to raise it in his original motion for post-conviction relief and was precluded from raising it before the appellate court. Defendant did not allege with any degree of specificity what constituted the mitigating evidence or the manner in which his counsel coerced him.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Plair v. State


NO. 2003-KA-00474-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


867 So. 2d 289; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 192



March 9, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 2/20/2003. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANN H. LAMAR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF AGGRAVATED ASSAULT AND SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF TWELVE YEARS IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tate County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his request to disallow the State's use of peremptory challenges during jury selection. He also contended that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to an inquiry made by the prosecutor, made during defendant's cross-examination, that was intended to call into question his credibility. The appellate court determined that there was no Mississippi precedent binding on the appellate court that suggested that Miss. Code § 13-5-69, authorizing peremptory strikes, was unconstitutional. Defendant did not contend that any strikes actually exercised by the prosecution violated any of the provisions of Batson. The prosecutor's questioning of defendant was irrelevant and, on its face, argumentative and had no possibility of eliciting information that would have been helpful to the jury in determining any fact of consequence in deciding defendant's culpability. The error in permitting the State to propound the question and requiring defendant to answer was harmless error as defendant did not allege any particular basis for concluding that this inquiry resulted in any prejudice or harm to the defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Miss. Manufactured Hous. Ass'n v. Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 2002-CA-01613-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


878 So. 2d 180; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 124



February 17, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 8/23/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ACTIONS OF THE BOARD OF SUPERVISORS AFFIRMED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Mississippi Manufactured Housing Association (MMHA), sought review of the decision of the Tate County Circuit Court, which found in favor of appellee Board of Supervisors of Tate County (board) and affirmed an amendment of a zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The MMHA appealed from the circuit court's affirmance of the amendment of a zoning ordinance, asserting that ordinance was arbitrary and capricious and therefore violated its rights to due process as secured under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court affirmed however, finding that the MMHA failed to show that the ordinance was not substantially related to a legitimate government purpose. The record failed to show how any homeowner or MMHA member suffered injury from the amended zoning ordinance. Moreover, by MMHA's own admission, the previous zoning ordinance encompassed greater disparate requirements for lot size than the amended ordinance, and under the previous ordinance any attempt by a developer to build a subdivision of manufactured housing required a variance, and that appears unchanged by the amendment of the ordinance. MMHA was actually benefitted by the amendment to the ordinance which MMHA never challenged prior to the amendment. The presumption that a political entity exercised its zoning power to further a legitimate purpose was not overcome.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Holbrook v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01722-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


877 So. 2d 525; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 23

Writ of certiorari denied Holbrook v. State, 878 So. 2d 67, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 865 (Miss., 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Holbrook v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 1166, 125 S. Ct. 1340, 161 L. Ed. 2d 141, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1746 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Holbrook v. Epps, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50754 (N.D. Miss., July 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PANOLA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 10/10/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ATTEMPTED BURGLARY, ARSON, MURDER, AS AN HABITUAL OFFENDER, SENTENCED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT PAROLE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Panola County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of attempting a burglary, arson, and a murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told an individual that he loved his former wife and that her sister was to blame for the divorce. He explained that he wanted to rob and burn the sister's store and then her house, where his former wife was living. Defendant was subsequently convicted of attempting a burglary, arson, and a murder, and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The errors contained in the search warrants were clerical and did not rise to the level necessary to invalidate them. Further, there was probable cause for the issuance of the second warrant in order to search defendant's home concerning conviction records from Tennessee, because the wife informed the officers that she had seen those papers at her home during her marriage. Venue was proper pursuant to U.S. Const. art. III, § 2 cl. 3, U.S. Const. amend. VI, and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 26, because there was nothing conceptually outrageous or bizarre in bringing charges in the count for attempting to burn a building in that county. Whether the target buildings in the county were seen as the effects or the means of the crime, there was the right under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-11-19 (Rev. 2000) to bring the charges in that county.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Poole v. State


NO. 2002-KA-01725-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


862 So. 2d 1285; 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 26



January 13, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Poole v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 100 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 10/22/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KEITH STARRETT. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: UNLAWFUL SALE OF MORE THAN ONE OUNCE OF MARIJUANA: SENTENCED TO THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC FOR TWENTY YEARS. DEFENDANT WILL SERVE THE FIRST EIGHTEEN YEARS WITH THE REMAINING TWO YEARS TO BE SERVED ON POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION. DEFENDANT IS ORDERED TO PAY A FINE IN THE AMOUNT OF $10,000 AND COURT COSTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pike County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of the sale of marijuana. Following his conviction and sentence, defendant filed a motion for a new trial or, in the alternative, for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Defendant's motions were denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The underlying action arose when narcotics agents set up a buy-bust, enlisting the service of an informant to attempt to purchase marijuana from defendant. After defendant was processed, according to the agents, defendant agreed to cooperate with the agents' investigation of marijuana trafficking in the area. On review, defendant contended that he was entitled to be set free or at least granted a new trial because the State reneged on a deal and engaged in improper conduct, arguing that he had no other choice but to agree to work as a confidential informant. The appellate court found that defendant voluntarily agreed to become a confidential informant and never actually performed any act as a confidential informant. Moreover, defendant did not show the terms and conditions of his agreement with the State. The only evidence that did exist regarding the agreement was that defendant would act as a confidential informant, that he would not make any contact with the informant, and that the agents learned that defendant violated the prohibition against contacting the informant and terminated the agreement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Starns v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00709-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


867 So. 2d 227; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 873



 December 31, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, En banc Starns v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 265 (Miss., Mar. 18, 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Starns v. Bingham, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26465 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] BILBO MITCHELL. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/20/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS. DISTRICT ATTORNEY.
Starns v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 896 (Miss., Dec. 31, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the only person alone with her stepdaughter when she died from asphyxiation. She contended that the child's arm became caught in a sofa, causing her to suffocate. After her conviction, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that an investigator was not required to inform defendant of her Fifth Amendment rights. The evidence showed that defendant was not in custody. The fact that defendant was the primary target of investigation did not change the court's decision. Further, the State was not required to set forth a coherent theory and prove through evidence that defendant committed an act to cause the victim to asphyxiate. The jury instruction given properly set forth the State's theory of suffocation and death by asphyxiation, despite how defendant might have committed the crime. The court determined that the indictment was also not required to set forth the manner of death, and it sufficiently apprised defendant of the nature and cause of the accusations. Finally, defendant's motion for an acquittal and for a new trial were properly denied because the verdict was not against the overwhelming weight of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Mauldin v. Branch


NO. 2002-CA-00146-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


866 So. 2d 429; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 849



December 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Mauldin v. Branch, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 865 (Miss., Dec. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/21/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PATRICIA D. WISE.
Branch v. Smith, 538 U.S. 254, 155 L. Ed. 2d 407, 123 S. Ct. 1429, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2709 (2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) assumed jurisdiction after appellee voters filed for injunctive relief and requested that it adopt and implement a new congressional redistricting plan because the state legislature appeared unlikely to meet its statutorily-mandated duty to do so and certain time deadlines had to be met. Appellant intervenors objected. The chancery court adopted a submitted plan. The intervenors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following the most recent census, the State's delegation to the United States House of Representatives was reduced from five to four representatives. However, the state legislature left the old five-district plan in place. Concerned about the State's failure to act, the voters filed for injunctive relief in the chancery court. They alleged that the state legislature would not submit a new redistricting plan. They requested that the chancery court adopt and implement a plan in time for the required preclearance mandated by federal voting law and a state law candidate qualifying deadline. The intervenors objected. The chancery court assumed jurisdiction and adopted a submitted congressional redistricting plan. In the meantime, a federal trial court ordered that the State use a plan it had adopted until the State produced a congressional redistricting plan that was precleared. The intervenors appealed. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the chancery court, pursuant to state law, did not have jurisdiction to adopt a submitted congressional redistricting plan, as state law dictated that only the state legislature had the power to authorize new congressional districts.


OUTCOME: The chancery court's judgment was reversed, and the action was dismissed without prejudice due to lack of jurisdiction.

Stevens v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00939-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


867 So. 2d 219; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 822



December 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Stevens v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 839 (Miss., Dec. 11, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stevens v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 858, 125 S. Ct. 222, 160 L. Ed. 2d 96, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6409 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Stevens v. Epps, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69564 (S.D. Miss., Sept. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/4/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL R. EUBANKS.
Stevens v. State, 806 So. 2d 1031, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 234 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted in the Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of four counts of capital murder and sentenced to death on all four counts. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate filed an application for leave to seek post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate shot his former wife, his daughter, and three others; only the daughter survived. The inmate told his current wife that "I just killed a family." The inmate claimed, inter alia, that: (1) the State improperly exercised peremptory strikes; (2) Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(7) (regarding aggravating factors in capital cases) was unconstitutional; (3) evidence the inmate had been abusing substances should have been admitted in the guilt phase to show that he lacked the ability to formulate specific intent; (4) the use of felony child abuse and burglary charges as underlying offenses for capital murder placed him in double jeopardy; (5) the death sentences were disproportionate; and (6) he had been entitled to formal notice of the aggravating circumstances to be used by the prosecution. The supreme court held that, as these claims had been considered and rejected on direct appeal, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3), res judicata barred further consideration of them. The inmate's crimes fit squarely within the definition of "heinous, atrocious, and cruel" provided in the jury instruction given by the trial court. Ring v. Arizona would not be applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court denied all of the inmate's applications for leave to seek post-conviction relief.

 

457 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Woodell v. Parker


NO. 2001-CA-01679-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


860 So. 2d 781; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 752



December 4, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/26/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS WRIGHT TEEL.
Woodell v. Parker, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 795 (Miss., Dec. 4, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptive parents challenged a decision from the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which granted a visitation petition filed by appellee paternal grandparents.


OVERVIEW: A minor child was born to a young, unmarried couple. Several days after the birth, the biological mother's parents adopted the child. For several years, the grandparents enjoyed visitation with the child. After the relationship between the couple deteriorated, the adoptive parents sought to stop all visitation. Thereafter, the grandparents filed a petition for visitation under the Mississippi Grandparents' Visitation Statute, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 93-16-1 to 93-16-7 (1994). After the grandparents' petition was granted, the adoptive parents sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the Visitation Statute was not unconstitutional. Further, the adoptive parents enjoyed no presumption with regards to their opinion that visitation would not have been in the best interest of the child. The chancery court properly examined 10 factors in determining that visitation was appropriate. The evidence showed that the grandparents had a relationship with the child, the child lived nearby, the grandparents were at home to watch the child, the child was of an appropriate age, and the grandparents were in good health. Finally, the court determined that attorney fees were not appropriate.


OUTCOME: The decision of the chancery court was affirmed.

Perkins v. State


NO. 2001-KA-01135-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


863 So. 2d 47; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 657



November 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Perkins v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 663 (Miss., Nov. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 4/20/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of aggravated assault, rape, two counts of armed robbery, and six counts of kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped a woman and her children when they arrived to look at a home for sale. Defendant forced the woman to perform sexual acts and took some of her belongings. They also beat and robbed the owner of the home. During the assaults, the woman's children were locked inside of a closet. After defendant was convicted of numerous crimes, he sought review. On appeal, the court determined that evidence obtained during a traffic stop was admissible under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-3-7(1) (Rev. 2000) because the officer had a reasonable belief that a crime had been committed and that defendant committed the crime. The evidence showed that the officer recognized defendant from an ATM videotape. Further, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-53 was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant was informed of the crime of kidnapping. The fact that the woman knew where the children were during the assault did not invalidate defendant's convictions for kidnapping under § 97-3-53. Also, there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction for aggravated assault, and defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of counsel. However, the 35-year sentences for kidnapping were contrary to § 97-3-53.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the judgment that sentenced defendant to 35 years on each count of kidnapping. The case was remanded with instructions to sentence defendant to 30 years on each count. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

Tew v. Estate of Doe


NO. 2002-CA-00969-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


859 So. 2d 347; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 599



November 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 20, 2003.
Judgment entered by Tew v. Estate of Infant Doe, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 621 (Miss., Nov. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NESHOBA COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/13/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. LOVE, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Neshoba County Chancery Court, Mississippi, granted judgment in favor of appellee, estate administratrix to the deceased Jane Doe, finding that appellant, the natural father of Jane Doe, had failed to comply with the one-year limitation established by Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15 (Rev. 1994) in that he had taken no action to be declared the father within one year of her death. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court erred in finding that the administratrix was not de son tort since she knew of the wrongful death claim of the child and willfully concealed it. The father argued that he had to be excused from the statutory period of Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15(3) because of the administratrix's conduct and that he should be declared the rightful and exclusive wrongful death beneficiary. The appellate court noted that there was no evidence that the administratrix took any action relative to the assets or estate of the child during the period of May 31, 1999 through May 31, 2000. The administratrix did not have any idea that there were assets until the estate was opened on June 13, 2001. There was nothing to indicate that she took any action as an administratrix de son tort prior to May 31, 2000. The father failed to raise his constitutional challenge as required by Miss. R. App. P. 44, by not giving the required notice of the issue to the state attorney general; as such, the appellate court declined to address the issue of constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15(3)(c).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Elkins v. McKenzie


NO. 2002-IA-00845-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2002-CA-00853-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


865 So. 2d 1065; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 582



October 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Elkins v. McKenzie, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 585 (Miss., Oct. 30, 2003)
Motion granted by Elkins v. McKenzie, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 221 (Miss., Feb. 26, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Elkins v. McKenzie, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 229 (Miss., Feb. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/13/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT I. PRICHARD, III.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed, rendered and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow filed an amended complaint against defendants, a city, its police chief, the officer who shot the decedent, and a second officer, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and alleging state tort claims. The Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted summary judgment in favor of the city, the chief, and the second officer and denied such to the shooting officer. The widow and the shooting officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent pointed a gun at the officers and backed into his house. Refusing the officers' demands that he put down the gun, he fired on the shooting officer. The shooting officer returned fire as he followed the decedent into the house. The decedent was mortally wounded in the exchange. In the instant suit the widow alleged constitutional tort and state law tort claims. In the widow's appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the city as the widow failed to show a facially invalid city policy; that the city demonstrated any deliberate indifference to any known or obvious consequences that might have resulted in any constitutional deprivation from execution or any city policy or any persistent, widespread practice or custom; or that causation existed between any city policy or custom and that such was the moving force for the shooting officer's actions. On the officer's interlocutory appeal the court reversed the judgment. The shooting officer was entitled to qualified immunity because the decedent had pointed a loaded gun at officers, refused to lower the gun, and backed into the house, which made the officer feel that he and others were in imminent danger.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the city, the chief, and the second officer. The court reversed the denial of summary judgment as to the shooting officer and rendered judgment for him. The court also reversed the dismissal of the state tort law claims and remanded those claims to the trial court for further proceedings.

Howell v. State


NO. 2001-DP-01104-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


860 So. 2d 704; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 556

US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Howell v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 440, 125 S. Ct. 856, 160 L. Ed. 2d 873, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1371 (2005)

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Union County, Mississippi, convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to death by lethal injection. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised 27 issues for review. The supreme court found that defendant did not demonstrate an abuse of discretion by the trial court's denial of the motion for change of venue. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tishomingo County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found defendant guilty of the capital murder of her husband and sentenced her to death by lethal injection. After defendant's motions for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict or, in the alternative, a new trial were denied, defendant appealed. The execution of the death sentence was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged her conviction and sentence, raising numerous procedural and evidentiary issues. The supreme court determined that the trial judge did not err by requiring the disclosure of psychiatric reports about defendant to the State prior to the sentencing phase. Exclusion of a pornographic home video of defendant taken by the victim was not error, as the jury received other evidence showing the victim's abusive and pornographic tendencies. The trial judge did not abuse his discretion in admitting the statement an investigator took from defendant; defendant repeatedly detailed her involvement in hiring co-defendant to kill the victim in her subsequent statements, which were obtained after she gave separate and adequate consent. As sufficient evidence existed to support the finding that the crime was committed for pecuniary gain and, given the heinous nature of the crime, imposition of the death penalty was neither excessive nor disproportionate in comparison to the crime. Although there were instances of trial court error, the trial was constitutionally fair.


OUTCOME: The conviction of capital murder and the imposition of the death penalty were affirmed.

Walker v. State


NO. 97-DR-00376-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


863 So. 2d 1; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 534



October 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Walker v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 544 (Miss., Oct. 16, 2003)
Stay denied by, Motion denied by, Post-conviction proceeding at Walker v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 9 (Miss., Jan. 8, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Walker v. Mississippi, 543 U.S. 842, 125 S. Ct. 281, 160 L. Ed. 2d 68, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5982 (2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Summary judgment denied by, Motion denied by Walker v. Epps, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 35700 (S.D. Miss., Apr. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/12/1991. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR.
Walker v. State, 671 So. 2d 581, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 494 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Harrison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of capital murder during the commission of a sexual battery, rape, and kidnapping, and, among the sentences imposed, defendant was sentenced to death. Upon his automatic appeal, the convictions and sentences were affirmed. Defendant's petition for writ of certiorari with the U.S. Supreme Court was denied. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction collateral relief.


OVERVIEW: In his post-conviction motion, defendant raised numerous claims that he was denied effective assistance of counsel at the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial. On review, the supreme court found that it had already addressed the merits on direct appeal of defendant's underlying ineffectiveness claims. Because the supreme court previously held that the underlying claims were without merit, defendant could not show the requisite deficient performance and resulting prejudice necessary to establish the various claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. Additional substantive claims raised in the instant application were all held to be procedurally barred and/or addressed on the merits on direct appeal. Since the claims had been addressed on the merits on direct appeal, defendant could not relitigate those claims on post-conviction review as they were res judicata under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3). Further, based on the supreme court's prior decision, there were no errors to cumulate; therefore; there was no cumulative error. Defendant demonstrated no reason, singly or cumulatively, warranting his convictions and sentences to be vacated.


OUTCOME: Defendant's request for post-conviction relief was denied.

Wilcher v. State


NO. 1998-DR-01820-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


863 So. 2d 776; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 492



October 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 4, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wilcher v. Mississippi, 542 U.S. 942, 124 S. Ct. 2917, 159 L. Ed. 2d 821, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4678 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SCOTT COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/21/1994. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.
Wilcher v. State, 697 So. 2d 1087, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 100 (Miss., 1997)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was found guilty of murdering two women and was sentenced to death. Upon the direction of the federal circuit court, the state supreme court vacated both of the inmate's death sentences and remanded the cases for resentencing. He was sentenced to death again. The inmate then filed a post-conviction application for leave of the state supreme court to proceed in the trial court regarding one of his convictions and death sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmate murdered the two victims while attempting to rob one of the victims and while he engaged in the kidnapping of both victims. After the reversal of his previous sentences, the inmate was again sentenced to death for both murders. The inmate then filed an application for post-conviction relief. The inmate filed numerous claims that he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel. The supreme court found that many of his claims for ineffective assistance of counsel were procedurally barred. The remainder of his claims that were not procedurally barred did not pass the Strickland test for ineffective assistance of counsel because he could not show deficient performance or that he suffered actual prejudice. Additionally, the inmate's constitutional rights to confront a key witness were not violated by the trial court's refusal to allow him to cross-examine the sheriff about his conviction for extortion which occurred seven years after the sheriff's testimony in the inmate's case. Also, the inmate was not deprived of his right to a fair and impartial jury. Finally, there was no accumulation of errors in the inmate's case that required that his death sentence be set aside.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied the inmate's application for leave to seek post-conviction relief.

Wilcher v. State


NO. 1998-DR-01821-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


863 So. 2d 719; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 526



October 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wilcher v. Mississippi, 542 U.S. 942, 124 S. Ct. 2917, 159 L. Ed. 2d 821, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4678 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SCOTT COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/23/1994. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.
Wilcher v. State, 697 So. 2d 1123, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 101 (Miss., 1997)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner was found guilty of capital murder and sentenced to death for the murders of two women. Pursuant to the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-1 to -29 (Rev. 2000 & Supp. 2003), the prisoner filed a post-conviction application for leave of the court to proceed in the trial court regarding his capital murder conviction and death sentence for one of the murders.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner murdered two women while attempting to rob one of them and while he was kidnapping both women. The court held that the doctrine of res judicata barred the issue of the trial court's refusal to allow evidence of a sheriff's extortion conviction, which occurred seven years after the sheriff gave testimony against the prisoner during the guilt phase. The issue concerning the trial judge's recusal was also procedurally barred, and the prisoner could not show prejudice because the sheriff's testimony was not the only link to robbery as an aggravating circumstance to the capital murder charge. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to make a Batson challenge, particularly in light of the silent record on the racial composition of the jury and the prisoner's failure to show prejudice. Victim impact evidence was properly admitted, and the State's biblical references did not violate the prisoner's constitutional rights. Two veniremembers who stated they could not impose a death penalty were properly excused for cause. Even if a dictionary was given to the jury, the prisoner failed to show that an extraneous influence was injected into the jury deliberations by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court denied the prisoner's applications for leave to seek post-conviction relief.

In re Assessment of Ad Valorem Taxes on Leasehold Interest Held by Reed Mfg., Inc.


NO. 2002-CA-01434-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


854 So. 2d 1066; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 472



September 25, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/30/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD D. BOWEN.
In re Assessment of Ad Valorem Taxes on Leasehold Interest Held by Reed Mfg., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 485 (Miss., Sept. 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Itawamba County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee county board of supervisors allowing the county to assess back taxes on a leasehold interest held by appellant holder. The holder appealed.


OVERVIEW: The holder argued that, based on the plain language of Miss. Code Ann. § 27-31-33 (Rev. 2002), the legislature carved out an exemption for private companies holding a leasehold interest in any property owned by a political subdivision that did not exist prior to 1985, at which time the statute became effective. The county's failure to raise the issue of the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-31-33, 27-31-34 and 27-35-155 at trial resulted in the procedural bar on this issue. The appellate court concluded that, after reviewing legislative history, attorney general opinions, case law, and the unambiguous language of the statutes, a leasehold interest held by a private company was entitled to the exemption provided for under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-31-33, 27-31-34, and 32-35-155. Because the county admitted to omitting the holder's leasehold interest from the ad valorem tax rolls, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 27-35-155, the leasehold interest was not subject to ad valorem taxation for any past year that it was not listed on the tax roll. Once the leasehold interest was properly placed on rolls, the county could begin assessing the appropriate ad valorem taxes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the board of supervisors' orders were set aside.

Simon v. State


NO. 98-DR-00517-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


857 So. 2d 668; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 447



September 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Simon v. Mississippi, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2641 (U.S., Apr. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: QUITMAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/13/1990. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS H. PEARSON.
Simon v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 462 (Miss., Sept. 18, 2003)



DISPOSITION: PETITIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought post-conviction relief from the guilty verdicts returned and death sentences imposed for the murders of three members of a family. After the prisoner filed a pro se petition for relief, appointed counsel filed a separate petition and a motion for leave to proceed in the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The victims' bodies were found inside their burning house. The victims died from gunshot wounds, while a fourth family member died of smoke inhalation. The court found that a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was barred from review by res judicata because the true issue was whether the prisoner's confession was voluntary. The questions of whether the prisoner's trial counsel was ineffective for failing to call his family to corroborate his claim that he was beaten by police, to object to the delay in the prisoner's initial appearance, and to challenge specific portions of the State's case were all without merit. The prisoner could not show how a supposed Brady violation affected the outcome of his case. Had his counsel possessed the transcript of a police officer's testimony from another trial, he would have done the same thing he did, which was to make the point that the officer may have embellished his testimony. The death sentence was not barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause as the evidence presented by the State in a trial for the murder of the fourth victim was sufficiently different from the proof presented in the second trial to prove each element of the murders.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitions for post-conviction relief and the motion for leave to proceed in the trial court.

Stockstill v. State


NO. 2002-CA-01047-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


854 So. 2d 1017; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 449



September 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Stockstill v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 455 (Miss., Sept. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PEARL RIVER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/18/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL R. EUBANKS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged a decision of the Pearl River County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed their action under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act (MTCA), Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (Rev. 2002 & Supp. 2003), against appellees, the State and various state agencies. The trial court found that the action was barred by the statute of limitations, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002).


OVERVIEW: The parents' son drowned in a river near the site of a project designed to restore water flow to the river. The parents initially brought an action against appellees in federal court, but the action was dismissed on sovereign immunity grounds. More than one year after their son's death, the parents' brought the current action, but the trial court dismissed it as time-barred. The court affirmed on appeal. The court rejected the parents' argument that the savings clause under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-69 (Rev. 2003) applied to the MTCA to toll the statute of limitations under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Rev. 2002). The court found that, pursuant to § 11-46-11 and Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-1 (Rev. 2003), Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-69 (Rev. 2003) did not apply to the MTCA. Because the one-year statute of limitations had run, the trial court properly dismissed the action. The court refused to consider any of the parents' constitutional claims on appeal because they had not been first raised in the trial court as required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

470 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Mann v. Mann


NO. 2001-IA-01699-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


853 So. 2d 1217; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 412



September 11, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TISHOMINGO COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/5/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. ROSS, JR.
Mann v. Mann, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 421 (Miss., Sept. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tishomingo County Chancery Court, Mississippi, dismissed a complaint for partition and a claim of heirship by appellant, the alleged illegitimate son of the decedent against appellees, the decedent's adopted daughters. The son filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The petition was filed over 18 years after the father's death. The son argued that the time period during which a father could seek an adjudication of paternity under Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15(3) did not apply to an illegitimate seeking an adjudication of paternity. The court disagreed, holding that the clear language of the statute established that it was applicable to both the natural father inheriting from an illegitimate and to an illegitimate child inheriting from or through the father. The use of the conjunction "and," indicated that the statute was applicable in either situation. The allegation that the son delayed filing a claim of heirship until the widow died, presumably out of respect for her, did not excuse failing to take timely action to establish paternity. Therefore, the claim for heirship was barred by § 91-1-15. Because they were not raised below, claims were barred with respect tolling the statute of limitations and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the chancery court.

 

471 of 603 DOCUMENTS


McGowen v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00676-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


859 So. 2d 320; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 413



September 11, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/22/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.
McGowen v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 423 (Miss., Sept. 11, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to life in prison without parole. The court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his constitutional right to confrontation was violated when a crime lab serologist testified on behalf of her former coworker as to the results of tests for blood and semen on various items in evidence. The supreme court disagreed. The witness was actively involved in the production of the report and had intimate knowledge of the analysis even though she did not perform the tests first hand. Furthermore, the expert testimony did not concern an essential element of the crime and was not damaging to defendant's case. The testimony was essentially moot to the determination of the case. The witness testified that the tests for semen and blood on a comforter were negative, the tests for blood on the mallet were negative, and the tests from the sexual assault kits for semen were negative. The only potentially damaging testimony was a comment that if digital penetration were the only sexual act performed on the victim, then one would not expect to find semen. Therefore, the trial court clearly did not err in allowing the witness's testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

472 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. State


NO. 2002-KM-01650-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


853 So. 2d 100; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 371



August 21, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PANOLA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/5/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANN H. LAMAR.
Hill v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 429 (Miss., Aug. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Panola County Circuit Court, Mississippi, for the offense of animal cruelty. The trial court imposed a $ 750 fine, $ 3,000 in restitution, and sentenced him to six months in jail pending compliance with the trial court's orders and pending future good behavior. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant readily admitted that he shot a dog twice in the head with a shotgun and that the dog was posing no threat whatsoever at the time. In addition, he dragged the dog's corpse down a paved road before disposing of it. On appeal, defendant argued that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-41-16 (2000) was unconstitutionally vague under the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution, as it did not define "spirit of revenge," did not indicate whether the spirit of revenge must be directed toward the dog or its owner, and failed to define what constituted wanton cruelty in killing a dog. The appellate court held that an ordinary person giving a fair reading of the statute would have concluded that defendant's conduct was prohibited and that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-41-16 (2000) was not unconstitutionally vague such that it would not have given defendant sufficient notice that the conduct in which he engaged was proscribed. The appellate court concluded that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-41-16 (2000) was not unconstitutionally vague under the due process clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

473 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


NO. 2001-KA-00640-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 285; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 363



August 14, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 568 (Miss., Oct. 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/22/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction of a lesser-included charge of manslaughter based upon a jury verdict from the Cohoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi), asserting that his constitutional right to the nature and notice of the charge was violated by the lack of a stated means of homicide in the indictment, that the court committed evidentiary errors, and that the verdict was not supported by sufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant arrived at a nightclub where his sister was fighting with a male. After firing his gun into the air, defendant was rushed by the male and his two brothers, and defendant shot them, killing one. Witnesses testified that defendant was free from the grasp of the victims before he shot them, and the jury rejected self-defense. Defendant first argued that the homicide statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-37 (2000), was constitutionally defective because it did not require the inclusion in the indictment of a specific overt act by which the murder was allegedly committed. The trial court had allowed the State to amend the indictment to allege "by shooting with a pistol," and it was clear from the record that defendant was not prejudiced in the preparation of his defense by the indictment. The supreme court found no error where medical record evidence of one of the victim's statement to a doctor that his fellow victim went on a "rampage" was not made for treatment purposes under Miss. R. Evid. 803(4). Finally, the supreme court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict, as there was sufficient credible, corroborated eyewitness testimony of the crime.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

474 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Goodin v. State


NO. 2002-DR-00686-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 267; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 353



August 7, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Goodin v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 565 (Miss., Oct. 23, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Goodin v. Mississippi, 541 U.S. 947, 124 S. Ct. 1681, 158 L. Ed. 2d 375, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2196 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NEWTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/19/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.
Goodin v. State, 787 So. 2d 639, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 135 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder in the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi) and sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant filed an application for leave to file a petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was entitled to a trial by jury on the issue of his mental retardation for execution purposes. The supreme court agreed. Defendant had a verbal IQ of 65, a performance IQ of 60, for a full scale IQ of 60 on the Wechsler Test. On another test called the Shipley, an expert witness found that defendant had an estimated IQ of 50, which also fell within the mildly retarded range. Defendant was reading at a second grade level and capable of doing math at a first grade level. Defendant spent three years in third grade and he acted strangely at times. The expert stated that if he had known about defendant's schizophrenia, he might have made different findings on the issues of IQ and retardation; the original report showed that the expert was aware of defendant's claim of hearing voices, of considering suicide, of difficulties in school, and of being disabled. Defendant produced enough evidence to be granted leave to proceed in the trial court on the issue of his mental retardation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's application for leave to file petition for post-conviction relief was granted, limited to the following issues: (1) mental retardation; (2) ineffective assistance of counsel on the issue of mental illness and (3) ineffective assistance of counsel on the issue of competency. The application was otherwise denied. The State's motion to strike defendant's rebuttal brief was denied.
