Jackson v. State


NO. 98-DR-00708-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


860 So. 2d 653; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 355



August 7, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jackson v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 860 (Miss., Dec. 18, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Jackson v. Epps, 447 Fed. Appx. 535, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 20841 (5th Cir. Miss., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/14/1991. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS.
Jackson v. State, 684 So. 2d 1213, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 7 (Miss., 1996)



DISPOSITION: PETITIONS FOR POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF, DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought relief under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 99-39-1 to -29 (2000 & Supp. 2002), from a judgment on jury verdict of the Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of capital murder and related crimes and applied for leave to move for vacation of his convictions and death sentence, on grounds of various constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to death after his conviction of murdering four children, his nieces and nephews, in the course of an attempt to steal money from his mother's safe. The high court held that every single constitutional issue raised by petitioner was procedurally barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21 (Supp. 2002), either because of res judicata, or because of failure to raise the issue earlier, since in no case was petitioner able to show that intervening case law entitled him to raise the issue in the instant proceeding. Because of the death sentence, however, the high court reviewed his claims on the merits as well. It reiterated its determination, from prior case law, that the Mississippi death penalty statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101, was not violative of due process or guarantees against cruel and unusual punishment, and that petitioner could not show that any supposed error at trial or deficiency of counsel affected his outcome.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitions and the application for leave to file a motion to vacate.

 

476 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. State


NO. 97-DR-00046-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


849 So. 2d 95; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 297



June 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 4, 2003. As Corrected July 23, 2003.
Reported at Russell v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 329 (Miss., June 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/4/1993. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS.
Russell v. State, 670 So. 2d 816, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 617 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF GRANTED ON THE SOLE ISSUE OF DETERMINATION OF MENTAL RETARDATION; POST-CONVICTION RELIEF OTHERWISE DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a capital murder case, defendant was sentenced to death on remand by a second sentencing jury of the Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi). Defendant filed an amended petition for post-conviction relief, the State filed its response, defendant filed a second amendment and reply to response, and the State filed its response.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder of a corrections officer. Defendant raised a significant number of issues for post-conviction relief. The supreme court denied relief on all issues but one, that being defendant's claim that he was mentally retarded. The supreme court held that not being mentally retarded was not an aggravating factor necessary for imposition of the death penalty, and the Ring standard, requiring a finding of aggravating circumstances necessary for imposition of the death penalty to be found by a jury, had no application to an Atkins v. Virginia determination, prohibiting the execution of mentally retarded offenders. The burden of proof for the issue was on defendant. One doctor testified that defendant was mildly retarded, while another doctor testified that defendant's IQ was borderline low to normal and he was not retarded. After thorough consideration, the supreme court found that defendant should be granted leave to proceed in the trial court on the sole issue of whether he was mentally retarded such that he could not be executed under Atkins.


OUTCOME: The amended petition for post-conviction relief was denied except for the sole ground of defendant's alleged mental retardation. Defendant was granted leave to proceed in the trial court on the sole issue of whether he was mentally retarded such that he could not be executed under Atkins v. Virginia. The standard or definition of mental retardation was to be that enunciated in Atkins, and the issue was to be decided without a jury.

 

477 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Calhoun v. State


NO. 2002-CP-00552-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH, NO. 2002-CP-00553-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


849 So. 2d 892; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 233



May 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Calhoun v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 351 (Miss., July 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/21/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. I. PRICHARD, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being charged with capital rape, appellant inmate pled guilty to the charge of sexual battery and was sentenced to 30 years' imprisonment, with 10 suspended. He filed a petition for post-conviction relief drawn up by appellant writ writer. The Circuit Court of Marion County, Mississippi, summarily dismissed the petition as frivolous and sanctioned both the inmate and the writ writer for filing a frivolous pleading. Both men appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, who was 23 years old at the time of the crime, confessed to raping an 11-year-old girl. The inmate underwent extensive psychiatric examinations at the state hospital. Physicians concluded the inmate was not mentally retarded, but rather somewhat limited intellectually. Upon review, the supreme court held that the relevant statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (Rev. 2000) was not unconstitutionally vague and that there was little doubt that § 97-3-95 gave a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that the inmate's conduct was forbidden. Indeed, the inmate himself admitted that he knew what he wanted to do was wrong, but he did it anyway. The court also concluded that the record showed the inmate was competent to stand trial, even though the inmate claimed otherwise. Two separate psychiatric evaluations showed he was competent to stand trial and competent to have understood the difference between right and wrong. Because most of the inmate's post-conviction petition was at least arguable, the merits of the other issues raised in the petition should have been addressed and sanctions should not have been imposed. Nevertheless, the summary dismissal was harmless.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's petition and reversed and rendered the imposition of sanctions against both the inmate and the writ writer.

 

478 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Helmert v. Biffany


NO. 2001-CA-01690-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


842 So. 2d 1287; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 188



April 17, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Helmert v. Biffany, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 230 (Miss., Apr. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY YOUTH COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/30/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL H. WARD.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The family court of Harrison County, First Judicial District (Mississippi), adjudicated appellant father as the natural father of appellee mother's child, and set child support and visitation. Later the family court was abolished. The father sought to modify a prior order, and was instructed to file the matter in the Harrison County Youth Court. The youth court denied a motion to transfer the matter to the chancery court. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1995 the family court entered a judgment adjudicating the father to be the natural father of the subject child, and set forth child support obligations, and a visitation schedule for the minor child. However, in 1999, the legislature abolished the family court. Then, in 2001, the father sought to modify certain provisions of the family court's prior orders. The youth court judge concluded that he had no authority to transfer the matter to the chancery court. The appellate court disagreed. The appellate court stated that nowhere did the Youth Court Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-101 et seq., provide for it taking jurisdiction over a case involving exclusively child support, contempt, and modification issues (as opposed to abuse issues). Further, paternity actions (the subject of the original action here) could never be brought in youth court. No allegations of abuse, neglect, or delinquency had been asserted, thus the matter was not one for which the youth court had been granted jurisdiction. Furthermore, the matter, was not "pending" within the meaning of the law repealing the family court. Thus, jurisdiction was properly in the chancery court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held the original paternity action could not have been brought in youth court. No allegations of abuse, neglect, or delinquency had been asserted, thus the matter was not one for which the youth court had been granted jurisdiction. The appellate court reversed the youth court's retention of jurisdiction, and remanded the matter for transfer to the chancery court.

Clark v. Stephen D. Lee Found.


NO. 2002-CA-00197-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


2003 Miss. LEXIS 148



April 3, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Clark v. Stephen D. Lee Found., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 627 (Miss., Apr. 3, 2003)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Clark v. Stephen D. Lee Found., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1413 (Miss., Dec. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/16/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JASON H. FLOYD, JR.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee foundation requested the Lowndes County Chancery Court, Mississippi, to confirm leasehold title against appellee secretary of state requesting that a lease entered into with a school be confirmed and ratified. The trial court entered summary judgment for the foundation, thereby ratifying the lease. The secretary of state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The school district acquired title to sixteenth section land that it used to build two schools. The property also had an historic home on it, which it leased to the foundation to preserve it. The lease provided for the nominal rental fee of $ 1 per year for five years with certain renewal rights. After the secretary of state questioned the constitutionality of the lease, the foundation was successful in the trial court in having the lease confirmed and ratified. The appellate court initially noted that, under Miss. Const. art. IV, § 95, lands belonging to or under the control of the state shall not be donated directly or indirectly to private corporations, private individuals, or to railroad companies or sold to corporations or associations for a less price than that for which it was subject to sale to individuals. The appellate court held the school board simply had no authority to lease the property on the terms that it did to the foundation and, because the $ 1 per year nominal rental was insufficient consideration, it amounted to an unconstitutional donation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and judgment rendered such that the foundation's complaint was dismissed with prejudice.

City of Belmont v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n


NO. 2001-CA-00729-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


860 So. 2d 289; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 132



March 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 24, 2003.
Rehearing denied by City of Belmont v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 838 (Miss., Dec. 11, 2003)
Motion to strike denied by City of Belmont v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 846 (Miss., Dec. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT:04/06/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipalities sued appellee Mississippi State Tax Commission (MSTC) to require the MSTC to comply with state law in its diversion of state sales tax funds to the cities. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted the MSTC's motion to dismiss pursuant to, inter alia, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 27-65-75 (1972) and 27-3-57. The municipalities appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the lawsuit was pending, the legislature enacted 2000 Miss. Laws 304, which abated any suits brought by a municipality to recover additional payments under Miss. Code Ann. § 27-65-75 (1972) in excess of the amounts authorized in 2000 Miss. Laws 304. The trial court held that the municipalities lacked standing, and were also precluded from maintaining the suit by 2000 Miss. Laws 304. The supreme court held that the trial court erred in ruling that the municipalities lacked standing; they had a colorable interest in the subject matter of the suit, and Miss. Code Ann. §§ 7-7-67 and 7-7-71 (Rev. 2002) did not bestow exclusive authority to the Mississippi State Auditor to bring such an action. But it agreed with the trial court that 2000 Miss. Laws 304 barred the suit. This statute was constitutional. It did not violate the separation of powers doctrine since it did not revive the right to bring the same suit in the name of another. Nor did it violate the non-delegation doctrine by setting no standards to guide the MSTC, as Miss. Code Ann. § 27-65-93 (Rev. 2000) authorized the MSTC to promulgate rules and regulations deemed necessary to enforce the provisions of § 27-65-93.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

481 of 603 DOCUMENTS


McGilberry v. State


NO. 2000-DR-00343-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


843 So. 2d 21; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 93



March 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McGilberry v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 228 (Miss., May 1, 2003)
Remanded by McGilberry v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 598 (Miss., Sept. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/12/1996. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.
McGilberry v. State, 741 So. 2d 894, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 196 (Miss., 1999)



DISPOSITION: POST CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of four counts of capital murder and was sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. He filed a petition for post-conviction relief and an application for leave to seek post-conviction relief in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, then 16, bludgeoned his mother and three other family members to death, and fled in his slain relative's car. He confessed; blood on his clothing matched the blood types of the victims. The supreme court held that many of the contentions in the petition were procedurally barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1) and (3) (Supp. 2002), as they were either not been raised at trial or on appeal, or were raised and decided adversely to him. Further, none of the contentions had merit. An instruction which required the jury to consider whether the crimes were especially heinous, atrocious or cruel was proper. While the instruction on the "great risk of death" aggravator instruction did not recite that petitioner "knowingly" created the risk, there was sufficient evidence for the jury to find he knowingly put his family in jeopardy. Even if this aggravating circumstance were invalid, the remaining aggravating circumstances supported imposing the death penalty. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to do more than just file a motion to transfer the case to youth court, as under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-151, petitioner had not been within the jurisdiction of that court.


OUTCOME: The petition for post-conviction relief and the application for leave to seek post-conviction relief in the circuit court were denied.

 

482 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Dillard v. Musgrove


NO. 2001-CP-00247-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


838 So. 2d 261; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 60



February 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Dillard v. Musgrove, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 99 (Miss., Feb. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 1/18/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LAWRENCE J. FRANCK.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired state employee appealed from a Hinds Chancery Court (Mississippi) order dismissing for failure to state a claim his complaint against defendant officials, in which he challenged the existence of the Mississippi Supplemental Legislative Retirement Plan, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 25-11-301 to -3109 (1999 & Supp. 2002) (SLRP), as violative of the equal protection guarantee of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Like all other retired state employees, the employee received retirement benefits under the Mississippi Public Employees' Retirement System, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 25-11-1 to 25-11-145 (1999 & Supp. 2002) (PERS). His constitutional challenge to the SLRP benefit was based on the argument that the legislators had provided a special benefit to themselves in addition to their PERS eligibility. Applying a presumption of constitutionality, the high court reviewed federal constitutional case law dealing with public employee benefit programs, and held that under the standards applied in that area of law, since treating different groups of employees did not amount to a suspect classification, it would examine the legislative scheme solely to determine whether it had a rational basis. The legislature's stated purpose of protecting legislators against the uncertainty of their tenure and the time taken away from their private careers survived that level of scrutiny. Inclusion of the lieutenant governor in SLRP was permissible because she performed some legislative functions. If the employee regarded that situation as unfair, he would have to seek a political remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

483 of 603 DOCUMENTS


D. J. Koenig & Assocs. v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n


NO. 2001-CC-01087-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


838 So. 2d 246; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 61



February 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at D. J. Koenig & Assocs. v. Miss. State Tax Comm'n, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 106 (Miss., Feb. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/24/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM JOSEPH LUTZ.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ON DIRECT AND CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Madison County Chancery Court, Mississippi, affirmed the suspension of appellant business's solicitor permit by appellee Alcohol Beverage Control Division of the Mississippi State Tax Commission. The business appealed.


OVERVIEW: The business argued that the Commission had no authority to suspend its permit, the evidence was not clear and convincing, proper notification of the charges was not received, the Commission improperly amended the indictment, and the penalties assessed were inappropriate. The appellate court found that Miss. Code Ann. § 67-1-57(a) did not apply. However, the business could be suspended under Miss. Code Ann. § 67-1-37(b). The Commission was given authority under § 67-1-37 to revoke, suspend, or cancel a permit for either non-compliance or for other sufficient cause. The business continued to sell items even after it was on notice that they were not proper items to sell. The business totally disregarded the authority and power of the Alcohol Beverage Control. The business should have followed the mandate given in the cease and desist letter until further review was had. Sufficient grounds were stated for the charges brought against the business. Due process was afforded pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 67-1-37 via notice and an opportunity to be heard. The business made independent decisions about what to sell and made false representations to package dealers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

484 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Mabus v. Mabus


NO. 2001-CA-00381-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


890 So. 2d 806; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 62



 February 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Mabus v. Mabus, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 274 (Miss., June 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 8/8/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. STUART ROBINSON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former wife appealed from those aspects of a judgment of the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) that granted defendant former husband a divorce on his counterclaim seeking divorce on the grounds of adultery, relating to custody, a prenuptial agreement, alimony, and property distribution.


OVERVIEW: The parties executed a prenuptial agreement before their marriage, and kept much of their property separate throughout the marriage. The high court reviewed with deference the chancellor's findings. If it was error to exclude a marriage counselor's testimony offered by the wife, it was harmless error, because there was plenty of similar expert testimony regarding custody issues. Although the wife argued after the fact that she had impliedly petitioned for joint custody, which the trial court would have granted if requested, the record supported the trial court's determination that neither party had requested it, so it was unavailable under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-5-24 (1994 & Supp. 2002). Since the evidence indicated that the prenuptial agreement was voluntarily entered with full disclosure, it was properly enforced, and although the wife had less property than the husband, she was provided for amply enough; alimony was not necessary. Finally, equitable considerations did not require that the husband's considerable inherited property be included in the pool for equitable distribution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Lamar County v. City of Hattiesburg (in Re Extension of the Boundaries of Hattiesburg )


NO. 2001-AN-00634-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


840 So. 2d 69; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 41



February 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re Extension of the Boundaries of Hattiesburg v. City of Hattiesburg, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 158 (Miss., Mar. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/22/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS WRIGHT TEEL.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the objectors, Lamar County, its Board of Supervisors, and others, challenged the Lamar County Chancery Court's (Mississippi), entry of a final judgment which had the practical effect of granting appellee City of Hattiesburg's petition to annex five separate and non-contiguous parcels of land located in neighboring Lamar County.


OVERVIEW: The judgment at issue had the practical effect of causing Hattiesburg (the county seat of Forrest County) to move further into Lamar County. Appellants raised three issues: (1) whether the chancery court erred in its order wherein it allowed the City to amend the legal description of the area proposed for annexation; (2) whether it erred in not dismissing the case once it went to trial as there were still errors with the legal description at the time of trial; and, (3) whether it erred in determining that the proposed annexation by the City was reasonable. Regarding the first two issues, appellants claimed that the legal description errors were so egregious that they deprived the chancery court of jurisdiction, but the court concluded that appellants were in no way prejudiced by the amended descriptions. It also rejected appellants' argument that the practice of liberal amendments to pleadings, as permitted in Miss. R. Civ. P. 15, did not pertain to annexations. As to reasonableness, the court reviewed the 12 relevant indicia, and found that the chancery court's findings were supported by substantial evidence. Finally, Miss. Code Ann. § 21-1-27 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Corey v. Skelton


NO. 2001-CA-00730-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


834 So. 2d 681; 2003 Miss. LEXIS 6



January 9, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/19/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee physician based upon his employment status at the University of Mississippi Medical Center in appellant estate administrator's medical malpractice case arising under the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (Rev. 2002). The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The administrator argued that the trial court erred in finding that the physician was an employee of the university medical center and was acting within the course and scope of his employment during the course of his treatment with the patient. The appellate court found that the physician was an employee of the medical center. The physician was the admitting physician assigned to the hospital on the day the patient was admitted and did not come into contact with the physician until his rounds the next morning. Because the patient was a Medicaid patient, doctors did not receive direct payment from Medicaid patients. The existence of professional liability insurance did not waive a state employee's immunity. The administrator's failure to raise the issue of constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7(2) before the trial court or notify the attorney general's office of his challenge of the statute resulted in the procedural bar on the issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Little v. Miss. Dep't of Human Servs.


NO. 2001-CP-01970-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


835 So. 2d 9; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 333



November 7, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified January 16, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Little v. Miss. Dep't of Human Servs., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 71 (Miss., Jan. 23, 2003)
Later proceeding at Little v. Miss. Dep't of Human Servs., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 741 (Miss., Jan. 30, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Little v. Miss. Dep't of Human Servs., 157 L. Ed. 2d 142, 124 S. Ct. 296, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6253 (U.S., 2003)
Motion denied by Little v. Miss. Dep't of Human Servs., 2004 Miss. LEXIS 1331 (Miss., Oct. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/15/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT H. WALKER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Harrison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed a complaint filed, pro se, by plaintiff father against defendant Mississippi Department of Human Services alleging the Department improperly took custody of the father's son. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department first argued that the father's claim was improperly before the circuit court. The appellate court found there was no evidence in the record of any appeal taken from the judgment of the youth court, much less any appeal taken within the requisite 10 days. The father filed a complaint almost a year and a half later. The filing of an original circuit court complaint against the Department was not the appropriate remedy for seeking relief. Proper service, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(1) (2002), would have been had on the chief executive officer of the Department. There was no attempt by the father to serve the chief executive officer, or anyone at the Department. The action was not filed within the statutory time period. The father did not do that which was required under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 of the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 11-46-1 to -23 (2002), to sue a governmental entity. The Department was authorized to take a child into custody by Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-301(2000) when there was an order by the judge which met certain criteria. There was no evidence supporting any of the father's allegations against the Department.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Falco Lime v. Mayor & Aldermen of Vicksburg


NO. 1999-CA-01284-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 1999-CA-01277-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


836 So. 2d 711; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 314



October 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Walker v. Falco Lime, Inc., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 83 (Miss., Feb. 13, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Mayor & Aldermen v. Falco Lime, Inc., 2003 Miss. LEXIS 181 (Miss., Feb. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 6/30/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR.

COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/7/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed & rendered in part; reversed & remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi) enjoined appellant board of aldermen from closing an airport and ruled it was obliged to create a separate corporate authority before jointly operating a second airport with a Louisiana city. The board and appellee businesses sought review. In a second case, the businesses appealed dismissal of their appeal of the board's creation of a municipal airport authority and its appointment of commissioners.


OVERVIEW: The board executed an agreement with Louisiana entities, under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 61-3-7, to create an airport (airport 2) and an authority to run it and to close an existing airport (airport 1). Later, the board voted to close airport 1. The businesses sued to keep airport 1 open and to recover from board members all tax money the board spent on airport 2. The circuit court, citing Miss. Code Ann. §§ 61-3-5 and 61-3-7, ruled the board could not conduct joint operations with Louisiana entities or fund airport 2 until it created a separate airport authority. The board then voted to create a municipal airport authority and appointed its commissioners. The businesses filed the second suit, alleging, inter alia, that two of the appointed commissioners were ineligible for service. A different judge of the same circuit court affirmed the board's creation of the authority and its appointments. The supreme court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 11-51-75 (2002), which authorized the circuit court's review of the board's actions, did not also empower that court to grant injunctive relief. The board's closure of airport 1 was not arbitrary or capricious. The businesses' appeal lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The circuit court was reversed in the first case insofar as it overturned the board's order closing airport 1, found that airport 1 had been dedicated by implication to the public for use as an airport, and issued a permanent injunction. That case was remanded with orders to the circuit court to lift the permanent injunction. The remaining orders in the first case and all orders in the second case were affirmed.

Ill. Cent. R.R. Co. v. Hawkins


NO. 2001-CA-01124-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


830 So. 2d 1162; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 296



October 3, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing dismissed by Ill. Cent. R.R. Co. v. Hawkins, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 380 (Miss., Dec. 5, 2002)
Later proceeding at Ill. Cent. R.R. Co. v. Winters, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 15 (Miss., Jan. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HOLMES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/18/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JANNIE M. LEWIS
Ill. Cent. R.R. Co. v. Winters, 815 So. 2d 1168, 2002 Miss. LEXIS 149 (Miss., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and rendered in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action arising from a locomotive collision, appellants, railroad company, engineer, and conductor, challenged judgment of the Holmes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered on jury verdicts, awarding actual and punitive damages to the beneficiaries of a mother and her two sons, in appellee father's wrongful death suit and appellee grandmother's negligent infliction of emotional distress suit.


OVERVIEW: A locomotive belonging to railroad collided with a vehicle driven by the mother and occupied by two of her sons, all who died in the collision. The grandmother witnessed the accident. On appeal, the railroad raised 29 issues on appeal, including the weight and sufficiency of the evidence, Batson problems, numerous evidentiary decisions, failure of the jury to deliberate adequately, a claim that the verdict was excessive, that the punitive damages verdict violated the United States and Mississippi constitutions, and that the 15 percent statutory penalty was unconstitutional. The supreme court found nearly all of the issues to be without merit. However, the supreme court held that there was no evidence that anyone ignored the railroad's vegetation policy, and this was not willful, egregious behavior. Thus, the conduct involved did not rise to the level which would warrant punitive damages. Additionally, the grandmother's vague testimony regarding visits to the psychiatrist could not support a damage award for emotional distress, and she failed to offer substantive proof for her claim.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment below, with the exception of the grandmother's damage award on her negligent infliction of emotional distress claim and the punitive damages award, both of which were reversed and rendered.

In re S.A.M.


NO. 2001-CA-00113-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


826 So. 2d 1266; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 291



September 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: FORREST COUNTY COUNTY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/14/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL H. WARD.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and Department of Human Services (DHS), challenged a judgment of the Youth Court Division of the County Court of Forrest County (Mississippi), granting durable legal custody of the child to long-time foster parents, and extinguishing the necessity for DHS to oversee and monitor the case and fulfill the requirement of annual reviews. In response, the foster parents filed briefs in support of the youth court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: The child was placed in the physical custody of the foster parents after being adjudicated abused. The primary issue raised by the mother for consideration on appeal was whether the youth court erred in granting durable legal custody to the foster parents rather than reuniting the mother with her child. The supreme court held that the youth court did not err in ordering that it was in the best interest of the child to grant durable legal custody to the foster parents, based on the child's situation of chronic abuse and long-term physical placement with the same foster family. Additionally, the mother argued that the 1998 amendments by the Mississippi Legislature to Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-609(b), creating durable legal custody as a dispositional alternative, were unconstitutional, but the supreme court refused to address the issue on appeal, because the mother did not raise her constitutional challenges at the youth court level. Finally, the supreme court held that the youth court erred in relieving DHS in the case, as the intent of durable legal custody was merely to avoid the required annual dispositional reviews, not a complete preclusion of further involvement.


OUTCOME: The youth court's judgment was affirmed as to granting durable legal custody to the foster parents, and reversed and remanded back to the youth court in order to correct the remainder of its judgment regarding relieving DHS from having any further involvement in the placement of the child.

 

491 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Nichols v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00807-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


826 So. 2d 1288; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 293



September 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEAKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/12/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of burglary of a business in the Leake County Circuit Court (Mississippi), and sentenced to pay a $ 3,000 fine, and to serve a term of seven years in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed, asserting the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him to the maximum period of confinement allowed by law.


OVERVIEW: Police were dispatched to a store pursuant to an alarm call and found defendant in the building. Outside a door were boxes of boots usually kept inside the store. A broken window was found with defendant's footprints below the window. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that his sentence was disproportionate or cruel and unusual in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 28. Mississippi case law provided that sentencing was at the discretion of the trial court, and not subject to appellate review if it was within the limits prescribed by statute. Here, the maximum sentence for burglary was seven years. Further, where a sentence did not exceed statutory limits, it did not constitute cruel and inhuman treatment. The trial court found that defendant had previously been convicted of numerous misdemeanor crimes. The fact that defendant was convicted of a felony for the first time, did not preclude a sentence for the maximum statutory limit. Finally, the appellate court held it was not bound to analyze the sentence pursuant to a three-prong test for an Eighth Amendment proportionality analysis as set forth by the United States Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

MIC Life Ins. Co. v. Hicks


NO. 1998-CT-01217-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


825 So. 2d 616; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 221



July 25, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/19/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILLY JOE LANDRUM. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
 Mic Life Ins. Co. v. Hicks, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 296 (Miss. Oct. 31, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, insurer and financing corporation, appealed, and appellee, insured's wife, cross-appealed after the Jones County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered directed verdicts in favor of the wife, the jury awarded the punitive damages, the award was remitted, and the Mississippi Court of Appeals reversed the trial court on all questions except the award of compensatory damages against the insurer, in a premium refund case.


OVERVIEW: When purchasing a truck, the insured also chose to obtain credit life insurance. The corporation advanced the premium and added it to the principal of the installment contract for the truck. The insured traded the truck for a smaller model and the installment loan was satisfied, and the insurer was then holding unearned premiums. After the insured died, the wife filed suit for failure to timely refund the unaccrued credit life insurance premium. On appeal, the corporation argued the trial court erred in directing verdict against it. The supreme court held that while there was evidence of a conspiracy between the corporation and insurer, it was not of such a nature as to take it out of the province of the jury. The wife argued on appeal that the court of appeals improperly reversed the punitive damage award against the insurer. The supreme court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 83-53-17(2) did not contain a notice requirement, and that while punitive damages were warranted by the insurer's conduct, the award was grossly excessive, as the trial was sufficiently flawed due to numerous prejudicial errors.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed and remanded the case as to the corporation for a new trial in harmony with the opinion, and reversed and remanded as to the insurer for a new trial on the amount of punitive damages awarded against it.

Sanders v. Estate of Chamblee


NO. 2000-CA-01354-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


819 So. 2d 1275; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 201



June 20, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/18/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GRAY EVANS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The LeFlore County Circuit Court, Mississippi, entered a permanent injunction in favor of appellee estate against appellant medical examiner preventing her from performing an autopsy on the body of the deceased in order to determine the cause of his death. The examiner and State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that, under the plain language of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-61-65(3) (2001), the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to hear the case, as the estate failed to exhaust administrative remedies by first appealing to the State Medical Examiner for further review. The appellate court found that the legislature did not intend that a deceased person's burial be delayed indefinitely while his next-of-kin pursued administrative hearings. The trial court was permitted to take immediate jurisdiction without the exhaustion of administrative remedies. The circuit erred by ordering that an autopsy not be done, as it involved a death affecting the public interest, as defined in Miss. Code Ann. § 41-61-59(2) (2001). Violent death, including homicide, and suicidal or accidental death were statutorily defined as affecting the public interest such that a coroner's decision to order an autopsy was proper. The only purpose for taking the bodily fluids was to help determine the cause of death. The record was devoid of any postmortem privacy interest the decedent could have that outweighed public interest in determining the circumstances surrounding an accidental death.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Buffington v. State


NO. 2001-KA-00325-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


824 So. 2d 576; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 206



June 20, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/14/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried in the Circuit Court of Warren County, Mississippi, and convicted of felony child abuse in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-39(2) (2000). She was sentenced to 20 years in prison with 7 years suspended and 5 years of post-release supervision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A caretaker of defendant's two-year-old daughter discovered the child had bruises all over her body. An emergency room physician found the child dehydrated, malnourished, and with numerous injuries. All of the child's bruises and abrasions caused temporary disfigurement. Each of the child's parents blamed the other for some of the abuse of the child. On appeal, defendant argued the child's bruises were not enough evidence to convict her under the felony child abuse statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-39(2) (2000). The supreme court disagreed. It found the instant case did not involve just a few bruises, but rather was a severe case, which clearly met the established felony criteria. The court held that "serious bodily harm," as it pertained to § 97-5-39(2), was any physical injury that amounted to child maltreatment such as death, or permanent or temporary disfigurement, or impairment of any function of any bodily organ or function. The supreme court also concluded the trial court did not err in holding that acts of omission, such as allowing a child to become dehydrated and malnourished, were adequate to constitute felony child abuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

495 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Wallace v. Town of Raleigh


NO. 2001-CA-00455-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


815 So. 2d 1203; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 169



May 9, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 2/26/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SMITH COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT G. EVANS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Smith County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee town, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1)(m) (Supp. 2001), which barred appellant inmate from bringing suit against a governmental entity. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that a strict interpretation of Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-9(1)(m) & (n) violated the Remedy Clause, the Due Process Clause, and the Equal Protection Clause of the Mississippi and United States Constitutions. The appellate court held that the remedy clause did not require exceptions to sovereign immunity and did not grant an absolute guarantee of a trial. There was no property right to sue the State or other governmental entities, and therefore no due process violation of the Mississippi Constitution. This applied to the United States Constitution, as state law defined property interests, and there were no exceptions to overcome sovereign immunity. In the Tort Claims Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7 (Supp. 2001), the legislature provided for an exemption from the government's liability for claims made by inmates. No exceptions, restrictions, or distinctions were made to allow an inmate to bring a claim against a governmental entity. There was no genuine issue of material fact, as the inmate was an inmate of the Mississippi Department of Corrections and in the custody of the work center at the time his claim occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stewart v. Hoover


NO. 2001-CA-00585-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


815 So. 2d 1157; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 139



April 18, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 3/7/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GLENN BARLOW.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adjoining landowner sued appellee homeowners and the state in the Jackson County Chancery Court, Mississippi, alleging the homeowners' pier improperly extended onto his property. The state asserted that part of the subject property was public trust land and successfully moved for summary judgment. The adjoining landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners obtained a permit from the state to construct their pier, which stated the tidal wetlands crossed by the pier belonged to the state. On appeal, the landowner argued the state was precluded from claiming ownership of the disputed land because it was not shown on the public trust tidelands map, and that his riparian rights were violated when the homeowners built the pier and when the state intervened. The appellate court initially noted title to tidelands could not be lost via adverse possession, limitations, or by laches, and under no circumstances could title held by the state for the public use or benefit be lost. The appellate court held although the disputed land had not originally appeared on the map of public trust tidelands, the legislature's goal of establishing certain and stable land titles did not contemplate a loss of public trust lands because of an oversight in the mapping process. The appellate court held the landowner's riparian rights were not affected as the homeowners obtained a permit from the state granting them littoral rights to the subject property.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the chancery court was affirmed.

Poole v. State


NO. 2000-KA-01831-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


826 So. 2d 1222; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 121



April 4, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TALLAHATCHIE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/18/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Tallahatchie County Circuit Court, Mississippi, which convicted him of capital murder and conspiracy to commit robbery, and sentenced him to life in prison for the capital murder and five additional years for conspiracy to commit robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) he was entitled to a mistrial because of comments made by one of the prospective jurors to the effect that defendant had terrorized her during her childhood; (2) his constitutional and statutory right to a speedy trial was violated; and (3) the trial court made erroneous rulings on jury instructions. The instant court found that because the trial court conducted an examination, and because of the brevity of the prospective juror's comment, the comment was not substantially prejudicial so as to warrant a mistrial. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial. Defendant was responsible for most of the delay in bringing the case to trial. Defendant failed to show any real prejudice, as he did not state or prove any exculpatory evidence which would have been available had he been brought to trial earlier. The trial court did not err in refusing defendant's requested instruction on manslaughter, as there was no evidence to support such an instruction. The trial court properly granted the State's accomplice instruction and an instruction on the elements of capital murder.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Bd. of Trs. of State Insts. of Higher Learning v. Ray


NO. 2000-IA-00962-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


809 So. 2d 627; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 64



February 28, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/30/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM HALE SINGLETARY.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court reversed and judgment rendered dismissing the cause with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Mississippi Board of Trustees of State Institutions of Higher Learning (IHL) and individuals, interlocutorily appealed from the Hinds County Chancery Court's (Mississippi) denial of their motion to dismiss and the grant of a preliminary injunction in favor of appellees, the Mississippi State Board for Community and Junior Colleges (SBCJC), individuals, and association affiliates.


OVERVIEW: A university and a community college operated in conjunction on the coast. Miss. Code Ann. § 37-102-3 provided that the IHL was prohibited from allowing its universities to offer lower level undergraduate courses at an off-campus site unless approved by the SBCJC. The attorney general allowed the IHL to establish a full four year university on the coast. Appellees filed suit, claiming that the IHL violated Mississippi law in allowing the university to begin offering freshman and sophomore courses as part of its curriculum. The supreme court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 7-5-1 required consent of the attorney general prior to filing suit between state agencies. Appellees did not receive consent prior to filing suit; therefore the suit was procedurally barred. The IHL created a dual campus, rather than an off-campus when it created the coast location; therefore, state law was not violated. The supreme court also held that the SBCJS could not be established as a body with veto power over the IHL's constitutionally mandated power to manage and control the state's universities; therefore, § 37-102-3 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial's court preliminary injunction and its denial of the motion to dismiss, and rendered a judgment in favor of the board, dismissing the complaint and action with prejudice.

Richmond v. City of Corinth


NO. 2000-KM-01581-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


816 So. 2d 373; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 29



February 7, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 7/19/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ALCORN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Alcorn County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of indecent exposure in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-31 (2000), and denied her writ of certiorari. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-31 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in violation of the First and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and the Mississippi Constitution. Defendant claimed that the statute was vague because it failed to specify the conduct prohibited, and that the terms "lewdly," "person," "private parts," and "public place" were not defined. The appellate court found that the statute did not define the terms, yet the statute was not ambiguous, and the appellate court applied the statute according to its plain meaning without further use of the principles of statutory construction. A common sense reading of the statute adequately provided an individual of common intelligence an understanding and notice of what conduct was acceptable or prohibited. Defendant's examples of situations in which the statute was overbroad were unpersuasive. The statute only prohibited nudity accompanied by lewdness. Certain conduct was allowed, in cases where serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value were present. Defendant did not demonstrate a real or substantial effect on a legitimate expression.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Knox v. State


NO. 1999-DP-01812-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


805 So. 2d 527; 2002 Miss. LEXIS 24



January 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied: Knox v. Mississippi, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5042 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Knox v. Mississippi, 536 U.S. 965, 122 S. Ct. 2677, 153 L. Ed. 2d 849, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5042 (2002)
Related proceeding at Knox v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 569 (Miss., May 20, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Knox v. State, 901 So. 2d 1257, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 190 (Miss., 2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by Knox v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 263 (Miss., May 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: AMITE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/29/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Amite County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied defendant's post-trial motion after defendant was convicted of capital murder while in the commission of a robbery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19. He was sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer called to a home noticed in a carport what appeared to be a blood trail leading to the rear of the victim's car. He could not locate the car keys, so he obtained a duplicate key. He opened the trunk and found the victim's body inside. It was later determined she had died from manual strangulation. Defendant was identified as a person likely involved in the death. Defendant was found wandering along a road. He denied knowing the victim. At the police station, a set of keys which were later determined to be the victim's house and car keys where found in defendant's back pocket. Investigators found defendant's clothes had spots of blood on them. At trial, the doctor who performed the autopsy explained how the strangulation caused a slow, heinous death. After defendant was convicted and sentenced to death, the state supreme court found: (1) the evidence was sufficient to prove the underlying felony of robbery, (2) the evidence supported the heinous, atrocious, or cruel jury instruction that was given, (3) the heinous, atrocious, or cruel jury instruction was constitutionally adequate, and (4) the death sentence was not disproportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

501 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


NO. 2000-KM-00630-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


806 So. 2d 1098; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 323



December 13, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/10/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PEARL RIVER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL R. EUBANKS.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following separate trials in the county justice court and the municipal court, defendant was convicted of a total of seven counts of animal cruelty. Defendant appealed from both courts to the Circuit Court of Pearl River County (Mississippi) where the cases were consolidated. Following a jury trial in the circuit court, defendant was convicted of one count of animal cruelty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court's instruction was erroneous because it did not require the jury to find his acts motivated by a spirit of cruelty. The supreme court, although the argument was not raised by either the State or defendant, determined that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-41-1 was unconstitutionally vague and agreed that defendant had no way of knowing, from a fair reading of § 97-41-1, whether his discretion in choosing to mend his horse's broken leg without paying for a specialist would result in a violation of the statute. The supreme court agreed with defendant that as the statute contained no language of intent coupled with motive, his only choices were to have the horse destroyed or take the horse to have him treated by experts, a costly endeavor. The court found that the statute, without words of intent and motive, left defendant no room for using his own discretion in deciding whether he would be able to heal his own horse without having to destroy it. The supreme court therefore held that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-41-1 was unconstitutionally vague under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the trial courts and rendered judgment for defendant.

Simmons v. State


NO. 97-DP-01550-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


805 So. 2d 452; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 316



December 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied: Simmons v. Mississippi, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6175 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).

Stay denied by, En banc Simmons v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 322 (Miss., June 21, 2012)
Stay denied by, En banc Simmons v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 320 (Miss., June 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 9/2/1997. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BILL JONES.
Milano v. State, 790 So. 2d 179, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 110 (Miss., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and another were indicted for capital murder during the commission of robbery, kidnapping, and rape. The trials were severed. Change of venue just for jury selection was granted. The Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, by jury, convicted defendant on all three counts. He was sentenced to separate life sentences for the kidnapping and rape, and to death by lethal injection on the capital murder charge. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his ex-brother-in-law owed a drug dealer money. Defendant, a butcher, sharpened all his work knives and took them home for a weekend. The dealer and his girlfriend visited defendant's home where the ex-in-law shot the dealer, defendant bound and raped the girlfriend and cut up the dealer's corpse, and the two culprits dropped his body parts in the bayou. Defendant confessed to a friend. The supreme court held that as the evidence showed a planned assault, self-defense and manslaughter jury instructions were properly denied. An alleged prior bad act by the homicide victim was properly excluded as no overt act by him against the culprits was shown except defendant's testimony. The fact that the actual moment of the victim's death preceded consummation of the robbery did not vitiate the capital charge. An off-handed witness reference to defendant "in prison," during defense counsel's questioning, was not incurably prejudicial to defendant. Contamination of the neighborhood's waters, intending to attract alligators, satisfied Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(5)(c)'s "great risk of death to many persons" aggravating circumstance. Jury sequestration was adequate.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were upheld.

 

503 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Bond v. Marion County Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 2000-CA-00626-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


807 So. 2d 1208; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 325



December 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/20/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sued appellees government officials in the Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi), concerning the financing of an economic development project. The trial court granted the officials' summary judgment motion, and the taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: An employer wanted to locate a facility in the county, but required that one be built before the officials found a site and advertised for public bids. Instead, a private individual built the building and signed a lease-purchase agreement with the county. The officials unsuccessfully sought a bond issue to pay for this, and then obtained private legislation allowing the local development authority to borrow the necessary money, which was to be retired by a special tax. As no tax was yet levied, the taxpayers were not deprived of any constitutionally protected property interest. Competitive bidding was not required, as the development authority bought the building after its was built and leased it back to the employer. The taxpayers received all the results of the bond election they were entitled to, which was that no bond issued. The officials' decision to seek an alternate financing method was not subject to judicial review. The private legislation did not violate the constitution's prohibition of special laws benefitting individuals, as that did not apply to public bodies. The officials were immune from the taxpayers' claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Todd v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00888-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


806 So. 2d 1086; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 305



November 8, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Todd v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 453 (Miss. Ct. App., May 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/15/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of three counts of sexual battery and one count of fondling perpetrated against a female child who was under the age of 14. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in sexual encounters with a child under the age of 14. On appeal, the supreme court found that (1) the victim's testimony was sufficient to support the conviction despite her admissions of past fabrications, which she claimed were the result of coercion; (2) defendant did not prove that there would have been a reasonable probability of a different outcome if the State had revealed to him the existence of an inadmissible polygraph test result of a witness that he claimed he could have used to bolster the testimony of that witness; (3) the trial court did not err in admitting testimony of sexual acts between defendant and the child's aunt and another woman that were intertwined with the fondling of the child; (4) the trial court did not err in refusing to admit into evidence a letter purportedly written by the child in which she recanted her allegations against defendant since the letter was not properly authenticated; (5) defendant could not impeach a witness with the prosecutor's statement of what the witness's testimony would be; and (6) the defense of mistake of age was not available to defendant on the sexual battery and fondling charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GEORGE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/08/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The George County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered a final judgment of conviction after defendant was found guilty of capital murder pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e)(2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A 78-year old woman was found stabbed to death, apparently during a burglary at her home. Defendant had been a prison inmate. Shortly before the killing, he had left a prison work detail. He was arrested after the murder. He signed a waiver of his Miranda rights. However, after police started questioning him, he said he wanted to talk to a lawyer. A few days later, defendant requested to speak with the sheriff. He gave statements implicating himself. The trial court declined to suppress defendant's statements to police. After he was convicted, the state supreme court found the trial court did not err in not suppressing the incriminating statements as defendant waived any otherwise applicable constitutional rights and they were not coerced. It also found the trial court did not err: (1) in denying his motion for change of venue, (2) in allowing crime scene photos to be admitted into evidence, (3) in not declaring the state's death penalty statute or its aggravating factor statute unconstitutional, (4) in not granting a mistrial based on voir dire comments, (5) in striking certain jurors, (6) in denying defendant's motion for funds, or (7) in imposing the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Quitman County


NO. 2000-IA-01477-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


807 So. 2d 401; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 288



October 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Quitman County Miss. v. State, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 438 (Miss., July 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/30/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: QUITMAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ELZY JONATHAN SMITH, JR.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county brought an action for declaratory and injunctive relief in the Quitman County Circuit Court (Mississippi) against defendants, governor and attorney general. The county alleged that the state breached its duties under Mississippi law by forcing the county to fund representation of indigent criminal defendants. The trial court denied the state's motion to dismiss. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the county lacked standing because the complaint did not name any person who had been deprived of the effective assistance of counsel. The supreme court disagreed because the county was particularly interested in the funding scheme as it was the entity required to provide indigent defense funding and it experienced an adverse effect from the state's failure to provide funding for indigent defendants. For these reasons, the supreme court held that the county had standing to bring this action against the state. The state argued that the county's allegations could not overcome the presumption of constitutionality afforded the statutes at issue and that the financing of public defenders was a legislative matter for which the courts could provide no remedy. The supreme court disagreed because it was not the funding that the county argued was unconstitutionally shifted to the counties, but the obligation of indigent defense. The supreme court concluded that the county pleaded facts that were sufficient to demonstrate that the state breached its constitutional duty to provide indigent defendants with effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Stacy v. Ross


NO. 1999-CA-00579-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH, NO. 1999-CA-01725-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 1275; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 300



October 31, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/18/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN C. ROSS, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ALCORN COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and rendered in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents brought an action in the Alcorn County Chancery Court (Mississippi) against defendant parents seeking visitation with their grandchild. The trial court granted visitation to the grandparents. In certain post judgment proceedings, the trial court found the parents in contempt and denied the parents' motion for relief from judgment. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that the Mississippi Grandparents' Visitation Act was unconstitutional because it allowed the trial court to disregard a decision of a fit parent. The supreme court disagreed because the statute specifically limited the court's ability to order grandparent visitation. The parents argued that the chancellor misapplied the statute and, therefore, the order of grandparent visitation was in error. The supreme court agreed because the chancellor never made an express finding that visitation was in the child's best interest as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3(2), much less a finding that overnight and unsupervised visitation was in his best interest, there was no evidence to support the chancellor's belated finding that the parents had "unreasonably' withheld visitation and each mental health professional that testified opined that visitation was not in the best interest of the child. The parents argued that the chancellor erred when he found them in contempt. The supreme court disagreed because even though the judgment in question was not properly executed and served, that did not relieve them of obedience to the earlier, interim, order for visitation.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment of the chancellor and render judgment for the parents on the issue of visitation, affirmed as to contempt for failure to comply with the court's orders, and remanded for determination of attorney's fees for the parents.

Kelly v. State


NO. 2000-CP-02097-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


797 So. 2d 1003; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 262



October 11, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/19/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WAYNE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wayne County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered a judgment dismissing defendant's petition for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for selling cocaine to an undercover police officer on or about January 26, 1996. On October 10, 1996, defendant was convicted pursuant to a guilty plea and was sentenced to 15 years in prison. On October, 12, 2000, defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant's petition for post conviction collateral relief was dismissed by the trial court on the grounds it was statutorily time barred. The trial court did not address the petition's merits. After the petition was dismissed, the appellate court found that Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(1), (2) (2000) dictated that a prisoner in custody had three years from the time he pled guilty in which to file a claim for postconviction relief. It further found that because defendant's petition for postconviction relief was filed more than four years after he was convicted, the trial court did not err in dismissing his petition as time barred. It further found that dismissing his petition without considering its merits, on time limitations grounds, violated neither his federal nor state constitutional rights as statutes of limitations served the important goal of helping the courts manage their business.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Simpson County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of two counts of capital murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was being transported to prison on unrelated charges, defendant shot and killed two deputies. He first shot the driver from the back seat of the car and then climbed out of the car and fired more shots into it. The supreme court held, among other things, that the trial court did not err in: (1) accepting the State's race-neutral reasons for its peremptory strikes of eight African-American jurors; (2) refusing to declare a mistrial following an emotional outburst by members of a victim's family, or based on a note the jury sent during deliberations indicating jurors were concerned about their safety because defendant's family members had followed them back from lunch; (3) finding that there was insufficient proof of improper influence on a juror; (4) determining defendant was competent to stand trial; (5) admitting photographs of the victims; (6) including the "great risk" aggravator in the jury instructions; and (7) refusing to suppress some of defendant's statements to police officers. OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

Edwards v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01487-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


800 So. 2d 454; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 232



September 13, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/12/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of burglary of a dwelling, was found to be a habitual offender, and was sentenced to 25 years in prison. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found in a shed connected to a house by a common roof and ceiling, separated by a breezeway. Defendant did not show beyond a reasonable doubt that the statute defining a dwelling, for purposes of a burglary charge, was unconstitutionally vague, and his burglary of the outbuilding was a burglary of a dwelling. Defendant agreed at pre-trial hearings to be represented by counsel, allowed counsel to conduct his trial, and fully participated in the new trial motion hearing. His right to self-representation was not denied. A threshold comparison of defendant's crime to his sentence did not require application of the three-part sentence proportionality test by being grossly disproportionate, making statistics regarding sentences for similar crimes in neighboring counties irrelevant. Defendant had 16 prior convictions and was correctly found to be an habitual offender. The fact that defendant's sentence was more severe than that offered in a plea bargain did not mean defendant received a harsher sentence for exercising his right to trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Madere v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00347-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


794 So. 2d 200; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 235



September 13, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/18/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HANCOCK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALKER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for forcible rape. The Circuit Court of Hancock County, Mississippi, by jury, found him guilty of forcible sexual intercourse and sentenced him to 15 years' imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A 64 year old woman who lived alone was hysterical one night when she called friends for help, saying that she had been sexually assaulted. They helped her clean up. She maintained her claim at hospital. No bite marks, tearing, or bleeding were found. Police took defendant, her handyman, into custody and he confessed on tape. With his motion to suppress, defendant claimed police beat him with a cane to get his statement. Officers admitted they had had a cane but claimed it was either for an injury or a stolen cane case. At trial, defendant completely contradicted his confession. The Mississippi Supreme Court held that defendant did not prove Miss. The victim's hospital statements were properly admitted as Miss. R. Evid. 803(2), (4) exceptions to the hearsay rule. As the trial court had immediately restored order both when the victim appeared to faint during cross-examination and later when she declared, "Liar," from the audience during closing arguments, mistrial was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Post-conviction relief denied at Stevens v. State, 867 So. 2d 219, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 822 (Miss., 2003)

Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion denied by Stevens v. State, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 254 (Miss., May 12, 2011)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi), by jury, convicted defendant of four counts of capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2) and one count of aggravated assault under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7(2). The jury sentenced him to death on the murder counts and 20 years in prison for the assault. Defendant went to his ex-wife's place and shot her, her husband, her son, and the son's friend to death, and shot and injured his own daughter. The girl, hiding after she was shot, heard defendant tell his ex-wife that he had said that he would kill her. Defendant returned home. Before his wife and brother he said he killed a family. Defendant's peremptory challenge rights were not abused under Batson principles. Defendant's wife's testimony was not excludable under the Miss. R. Evid. 504 marriage privilege. Defendant's counsel admitted defendant was not insane under M'Naghten. Defendant never alleged he could not differentiate between right and wrong.
