Miss. Gaming Comm'n v. Henson


NO. 1999-CA-00422-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 1999-IA-00911-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


800 So. 2d 110; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 225



September 6, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/27/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. CHARLES D. THOMAS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: UNION COUNTY CHANCERY COURT.

DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/24/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. ASHLEY HINES. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WASHINGTON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff amusement center owners filed two separate complaints in two counties regarding the propriety of defendant Mississippi Gaming Commission's seizure of certain amusement devices. The Union County Chancery Court, Mississippi, and the Washington County Circuit Court, Mississippi, ruled the majority of the owners' machines had been illegally seized. The commission appealed the trial courts' decisions to the Mississippi Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: One group of the owners sought clarification and interpretation of the Mississippi gaming laws as to the criteria for determining the legality of certain amusement devices owned and/or leased by the specific group of the owners and seized by the commission, on the grounds they were illegal gambling devices. One trial court found the statute in question, Miss. Code Ann. § 75-76-5(ff) (2000), required proof of a payoff before the commission could have seized a machine under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-7(1) (2000). The second trial court agreed with the payoff requirement. Both trial courts concluded the commission improperly seized most of the owners' amusement devices. The appeals court disagreed, concluding that where the elements of consideration and chance were present, § 75-76-5(ff) required only that the machines possess the "potential for reward" to be considered a slot machine subject to seizure and destruction under § 97-33-7(1). The award of credits by one type of machine to play free additional games was something of value. Thus, the gaming device was illegal under state law and subject to seizure.


OUTCOME: The Mississippi Supreme Court reversed the trial courts' judgments and rendered judgments in favor of the commission.

 

514 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


NO. 1998-DR-01266-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 481; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 196



August 9, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/07/95. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.
Brown v. State, 690 So. 2d 276, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 681 (Miss., 1996)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATIONS FOR LEAVE TO SEEK POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of killing three victims, including a 13-year-old, who suffered severe chop wounds to their heads, and was sentenced to death for one of the murders. The Mississippi Supreme Court affirmed. Defendant sought post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: When the victim's bodies were found, bloody shoe prints leading in the direction of defendant's home were found. Defendant admitted to going out-of-state, buying a gun, and registering under a different name in the days after the crime when he knew the sheriff was looking for him. Defendant's friend, as part of a plea bargain in a separate matter, testified that defendant had gone to the 13-year-old's home to have sex with her and that he had beaten her. Defendant was convicted. The Mississippi Supreme Court held that as defendant was under a suspended sentence at the time, he was "under sentence of imprisonment" for purposes of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101(5)(a) aggravating factors. Many issues he raised were procedurally barred. Counsel's failure to investigate the story of a man in the woods weeks after the crime was not ineffective assistance, nor was the failure to investigate a potential witness who claimed nothing more specific than that the sheriff had a reputation for dishonesty. Defendant was not constitutionally entitled to effective assistance of an expert psychological witness. Counsel was not in conflict for having previously represented someone remotely suspect.


OUTCOME: The applications for leave to seek post-conviction relief were denied.

Williams v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01666-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


794 So. 2d 181; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 173



June 28, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. King, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60380 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 30, 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Transfer granted by Williams v. Diaz, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 59589 (S.D. Miss., Aug. 10, 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at Williams v. State, 2012 Miss. App. LEXIS 187 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MARION COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/28/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. I. PRICHARD, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment based on a jury verdict from the Marion County Court (Mississippi), convicting defendant for possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute, and sentencing defendant as a habitual offender for the felony offense of sale or transfer of a controlled substance within 1,500 feet of a school, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 41-29-139, 41-29-142, 41-29-147.


OVERVIEW: Defendant negotiated for the sale of crack cocaine with agents in planned drug purchase, from which an audio and video recording was made. The cocaine was placed in a sealed bag in an evidence locker and later tested. After defendant was convicted, he was sentenced as a habitual offender and his motion for a new trial or JNOV was denied. The appellate court held that the State's juror challenges did not suggest a pattern or raise an inference of discrimination, and there was not a reasonable inference of tampering or substitution of evidence, as defendant failed to break the chain of custody; thus the evidence supported the verdict of guilty. However, the testimony of an officer revealed that the drug transaction took place approximately 1,105 feet from a school. Miss. Code. Ann. § 41-29-142 denoted measuring points for sentencing enhancement to be 1,500 feet from the school building or outbuilding or 1,000 feet from the real property comprising the school. Because the testimony was imprecise and failed to prove the transaction occurred within either of the distances provided by the statute, the proof failed and the sentencing enhancement was not applicable.


OUTCOME: Because the appellate court concluded that the trial judge improperly applied the sentence enhancement for a sale of a controlled substance within 1,500 feet of a school, it reversed and remanded for resentencing without the enhancement. In all other respects, it affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

516 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Ryals v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00752-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


794 So. 2d 161; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 152



June 14, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/26/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAMAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R.I. PRICHARD, III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Lamar County Circuit Court, Mississippi, which convicted her of manslaughter and sentenced her to a term of 20 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On review, the supreme court found that there was no indication that the State's use of peremptory challenges against female venire persons created an inference of purposeful discrimination and held that defendant did not make a prima facie case of gender-based discrimination in the State's use of peremptory strikes against women. The supreme court also held that the arresting officer's questioning of defendant were part of his general on-the-scene investigation; therefore, Miranda warnings were not required and the trial court did not err in failing to suppress her statements made during that questioning, including her statement, "I shot him." Statements made at trial by defendant's witness were admissible since they were made in response to State's questions on cross-examination and were proper for impeachment purposes. The supreme court further held that the State produced sufficient evidence that defendant's version of what happened was materially contradicted by the physical evidence, and the jury was properly instructed as to the issue of self-defense. Defendant's sentence was not extreme since it was within the statutory limit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

517 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Lofton v. United States


NO. 2000-CP-00671-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


785 So. 2d 287; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 138



May 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 7016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/03/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. L. BRELAND HILBURN, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granting the State's motion to dismiss appellant's complaint which had alleged violations of his federal constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: At the time appellant filed his civil action, he was incarcerated in the state penitentiary. Appellant's complaint only made general allegations and identified no specific persons acting under the color of state law who were responsible for any of the wrongs he alleged had been done. Appellant sought millions of dollars in compensatory and punitive damages, as well as 500 acres of land and a family home at the government's expense. He argued the trial court erred in dismissing his complaint without giving him the opportunity to present evidence to support his claims. The judgment was affirmed on appeal. Appellant filed his complaint pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. One of the essential elements of a § 1983 claim was that the conduct complained of was committed by a person acting under the color of state law. Appellant's complaint did not name any persons who acted under the color of state law. The State was not a "person" that Congress intended to subject to liability, and therefore, could not be sued under § 1983 in state court. As a result, the State's Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b) motion was properly granted.


OUTCOME: The trial court properly granted the State's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim under which relief could be granted. Appellant's civil rights complaint failed because it did not name any persons who acted under the color of state law. The State, itself, was not considered a "person" under the applicable civil rights statute.

Goodin v. State


NO. 1999-DP-00975-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


787 So. 2d 639; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 135



May 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified October 25, 2001. Certiorari Denied April 15, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2500.
Writ of certiorari denied Goodin v. Mississippi, 535 U.S. 996, 122 S. Ct. 1558, 152 L. Ed. 2d 481, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 2500 (2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at Goodin v. State, 856 So. 2d 267, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 353 (Miss., 2003)
Motion denied by Goodin v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 374 (Miss., June 28, 2007)
Remanded by Goodin v. State, 2009 Miss. LEXIS 405 (Miss., Aug. 27, 2009)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Remanded by Goodin v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 616 (Miss., Dec. 13, 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Newton County, Mississippi, convicted defendant of armed robbery and capital murder, sentenced him to life imprisonment without parole for the armed robbery, and upon finding aggravators, including for robbery, sentenced him, by jury, to death by lethal injection for the capital murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both defendant's nephew and a tow truck operator notified police of the location of a store-owner shooting-victim's stolen truck, which implicated defendant in the murder and theft. At trial, both the victim's grandson, who had not been present at the crime, and defendant himself, identified defendant from a surveillance video from the time of the crime. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. The appellate court held that the jury, at sentencing, could consider any matter brought up during the guilt phase. The State's error in instructing the prospective jury of the law during voir dire was harmless as the verdict was not attributable to the misstatements. Counsel's failure to object to the grandson's testimony did not constitute ineffective assistance in that defendant did not show prejudice, as the evidence against defendant was overwhelming. The prosecutor's misconduct in instructing the jury to ignore defendant's constitutional rights by referring to how the victim's rights had not been protected was harmless, in that evidence of defendant's callousness was overwhelming. Defendant did not deserve a manslaughter instruction because he offered no evidence to support one.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Zeman v. Stanford


NO. 2000-CA-00757-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


789 So. 2d 798; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 130



May 10, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/18/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. PERCY L. LYNCHARD, JR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees filed a petition for visitation rights pursuant to the Grandparents' Visitation Rights Statutes, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 93-16-1 to -7 (1994). The Desoto County (Mississippi) Chancery Court entered an order granting appellees visitation rights. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellees petitioned for visitation with their two grandchildren under the grandparent visitation statute. The children's mother was divorced from the father and the father gained sole custody of the children. The mother was subsequently incarcerated and her visitation rights were considerably restricted. Following trial, the chancellor awarded appellees visitation and denied appellant's request for attorney fees under the statute. On appeal, appellant contended that the chancellor misinterpreted the statute, and challenged the statute's constitutionality. The supreme court affirmed, holding that the chancellor correctly applied Miss. Code Ann. § 93-16-3(1) (1994), which applied when one parent, such as the mother, was awarded no custody. Second, the statute was not unconstitutional, because it was narrowly interpreted to protect appellant's right to determine his children's care. Third, the visitation awarded was not excessive. Finally, the chancellor was within his discretion in determining that the proceedings imposed no financial hardship on appellant, thereby denying appellant his request for attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment was affirmed.

 

520 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Austin v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00234-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


784 So. 2d 186; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 121



May 3, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/03/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT PAROLE IN THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. SAID SENTENCE SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVELY TO ANY AND ALL SENTENCES PREVIOUSLY IMPOSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Coahoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi), of capital murder and sentenced to life in prison without possibility of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed a bill payment center, killed a teller, and stole cash. People saw the crime and saw defendant run from the scene. Defendant alleged sentencing instructions to consider the killing's occurrence during a robbery and to avoid arrest as aggravating factors impermissibly "double counted" the underlying crime in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII. As defendant received life, he was not prejudiced, so those issues were not considered. Defendant's proposed instruction that a law enforcement officer's testimony should not be given greater weight impermissibly commented on evidence and duplicated the instruction the jury was the sole judge of each witness. Admission of evidence of defendant's flight out of town required that the flight was unexplained and had considerable probative value. Defendant asserted his flight was explained, as he regularly took the bus to Chicago. Under the circumstances, his flight was unexplained. A circumstantial evidence instruction was not required, as direct evidence of defendant's guilt was presented. Inconsistencies in testimony identifying defendant did not make the case a circumstantial evidence case.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed as he was not prejudiced by jury instructions, nor was he entitled to an instruction not to give law enforcement testimony greater weight or a circumstantial evidence instruction. Evidence of his flight was properly admitted as it was not explained.

Milano v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00097-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


790 So. 2d 179; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 110



April 26, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/19/1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. EDWIN C. HARDIN. DISTRICT ATTORNEY:KEITH MILLER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Jackson County Circuit Court, Mississippi, that convicted him on a jury verdict of capital murder and kidnapping, challenging jury instructions and evidentiary rulings, the jury qualification statute's constitutionality, the validity of the indictment, and other alleged errors.


OVERVIEW: Trial evidence showed that defendant and the co-defendant went to the murder victim's hotel room, that defendant fatally shot the victim and the co-defendant tied up the victim's friend and locked her in a box. Defendant helped the co-defendant dispose of the body, and they both removed the victim's and the friend's belongings from the hotel room. Defendant was charged with capital murder and kidnapping, was convicted by a jury, and appealed. The appellate court affirmed: (1) use of an erroneous jury instruction was harmless error, as the other instructions cured its defects; (2) an instruction that did not require a finding as to which victim was robbed was proper; (3) the indictment was not defective; (4) judgments notwithstanding the verdicts were properly denied, as the evidence was sufficient to convict on both charges; (5) requiring jurors to be over 21, literate, and electors, was not unconstitutional; (6) defendant waived an objection to alleged prosecutorial misconduct; (7) no error occurred in admitting gruesome photos of the victim, or in excluding an irrelevant videotape; (8) the duress instructions were proper, as there was some evidence to support them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. However, because of continuing confusion with improper instructions concerning aiding and abetting, the appellate court adopted the Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals pattern jury instruction on aiding and abetting.

Reynolds v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01463-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


784 So. 2d 929; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 115



April 26, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 07/29/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GRENADA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III. DISTRICT ATTORNEY: DOUG EVANS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury in the Grenada County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of murder and possession of a firearm and sentenced him as a habitual offender to life in prison without parole. The trial court denied defendant's post-trial motions. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, at gunpoint, ordered two men to leave a bar. One of the men was shot and killed when the gun went off. The trial court permitted the surviving man to testify defendant had pointed the gun at him first before pointing it at the victim. Defendant argued this was a prejudicial admission of another crime. He further alleged that he was denied a speedy trial, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that his prior felony burglary convictions did not support his habitual offender status as he did not serve a year under either conviction. The appellate court found the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting testimony that defendant had threatened another man with a gun before shooting the victim. Further, defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated because of continuances granted, defendant failed to prove that his attorney's performance was defective, and defendant's two prior felony burglary convictions supported his habitual offender status.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed as the trial court did not err in admitting evidence of defendant threatening another man, defendant was not denied a speedy trial, defendant did not show his attorney was ineffective, and defendant's prior convictions supported his habitual offender status.

Jordan v. State


NO. 1998-DP-00901-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


786 So. 2d 987; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 109



April 26, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied January 7, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 318.
Writ of certiorari denied Jordan v. Mississippi, 534 U.S. 1085, 122 S. Ct. 823, 151 L. Ed. 2d 705, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 318 (2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at Jordan v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 685 (Miss., June 10, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jordan v. State, 912 So. 2d 800, 2005 Miss. LEXIS 170 (Miss., 2005)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Jordan v. Epps, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 71724 (S.D. Miss., Sept. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/24/1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS. DISTRICT ATTORNEY: CONO CARANNA.
Jordan v. State, 697 So. 2d 1190, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 344 (Miss., 1997)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon remand for resentencing, the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) sentenced defendant to die for a 1976 kidnapping and murder. Defendant sought review in his case for the 10th time.


OVERVIEW: Defendant called a bank to speak to its officer and found his home. Defendant pretended to be utility man, got in, seized the officer's wife, left her three year-old, drove her to a remote place, killed her, then told the officer for two days that she was alive and well. Defendant confessed, fully cooperated, and was sentenced. On a remand, defendant agreed with the State to forego another sentencing trial and accept life without parole. Later that sentence was ruled illegal and he was resentenced. The supreme court held that it had authorized the State to seek death upon resentencing, and that was in the jury's hands; thus there was no prosecutorial vindictiveness. "Heinous" aggravator was found in victim's abduction away from three year-old, not just her murder. There was no impermissible "doubling" of the heinous and kidnapping aggravators. As defendant requested a court-appointed psychiatric examination and evidenced the report, the State, in rebuttal, could do so too without disclosing its substantive contents. The district attorney retained control over its special prosecutor. Double jeopardy was not violated. Death could be imposed for killing regardless of intent.


OUTCOME: The capital murder conviction and death by lethal injection sentence were affirmed.

King v. State


NO. 1998-DP-01134-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


784 So. 2d 884; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 99



April 19, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at King v. State, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 317 (Miss., May 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/10/1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LOWNDES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HARVEY S. BUCK.
King v. State, 656 So. 2d 1168, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 264 (Miss., 1995)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty in the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of capital murder and sentenced to death. After numerous procedural matters, defendant filed a motion for new trial. The trial court denied the motion for new trial. Defendant appealed that judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his capital murder conviction and sentence on the ground the trial court erroneously excused jurors from the jury venire who generally opposed the death penalty but vowed to follow the court's instructions and vote for death if warranted, denied defendant the expert assistance of a pathologist, and improperly instructed the jury that sympathy could have no part in the case. The supreme court found no abuse of discretion by the trial court in striking the potential jurors who expressed reservations about imposition of the death penalty, or in denying defendant the funds to procure an expert pathologist since defendant showed no substantial need for his own expert. However, the supreme court found the trial judge committed reversible error by commenting that the jury could not consider sympathy in its deliberations.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and remanded for new sentencing.

Edmond v. Miss. Dep't of Corr.


NO. 2000-CP-00086-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


783 So. 2d 675; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 91



April 12, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Edmond v. State, 845 So. 2d 701, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 187 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/21/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES W. BACKSTROM.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that appellee Department of Corrections unlawfully revoked his parole. The Greene County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed the petition. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a convicted rapist, was paroled and given work in appellee Mississippi Department of Corrections as a staff chaplain. Appellant, of his own accord, went to the sheriff's office and admitted he "entered into an unknown house". The sheriff investigated. The record was insufficient to determine whether appellant was denied proper procedure. It showed no trespass complaint filed, nor why the house was entered. The unlawful revocation claim was not time-barred as it fell within the Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) exception to the three year limitation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case remanded.

Public Emples. Ret. Sys. v. Hawkins


NO. 97-IA-01214-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


781 So. 2d 899; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 78



April 4, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/19/1997. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CIRCUIT COURT OF THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF CHICKASAW COUNTY. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY LAFAYETTE LACKEY.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of February 7, 2001, Previously Reported at: 2001 Miss. LEXIS 27.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, RENDERED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired supreme court justice sued defendant Public Employees Retirement System for a declaratory judgment that his expense reimbursements were earned compensation under Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-103(k), and that he was entitled to pension benefits on them. The Chickasaw County Circuit Court, Mississippi, denied PERS's motion to dismiss for failure to exhaust administrative remedies and improper venue. PERS sought interlocutory review.


OVERVIEW: The justice sought, unsuccessfully, to obtain a ruling from PERS as to whether his reimbursements for meals, travel, lodging, and utilities were considered earned compensation on which he was entitled to retirement benefits. He sued PERS, seeking a declaratory judgment. PERS's motion for summary judgment on grounds that the justice failed to exhaust his administrative remedies, and that venue was improper, was denied. PERS petitioned for interlocutory review. The instant court found it proper to rule on the dispositive legal issue as well as the grounds raised in the appeal, and affirmed. Venue was proper, as the justice filed the case in the county where his retirement checks would be sent. The justice was relieved of exhausting administrative remedies, because: (1) the dispositive question was one of law; (2) agency's expertise was not required; (3) judicial economy would be served; and (4) PERS's sluggish response to the justice's case deprived him of an adequate administrative remedy. The instant court held that the justice's expense reimbursements were earned compensation for retirement purposes under § 25-11-103(k).


OUTCOME: Judgment that the justice was not required to exhaust administrative remedies, and that venue was proper, was affirmed. As the instant court also ruled on the merits of the action, the case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

In the Interest of D. O.


NO. 1999-CA-02120-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 417; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 64



March 15, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY YOUTH COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 12/13/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MICHAEL H. WARD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents challenged the judgment of the Harrison County Youth Court, Mississippi, adjudicating their children of abuse and neglect with aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents challenged judgment of the youth court, adjudicating their children abused and neglected. Appellants alleged the State failed to meet its burden of proof, believing that the evidence considered was insufficient to support the ultimate finding. Additionally, appellants asserted that all evidence relating to the mother's statements to a social worker was based upon hearsay. The appeals court affirmed the findings. Because no hearsay objection was made when the statements were proffered, the argument was barred. Expert medical opinion was that the victim suffered trauma to her anus and rectum. The trier of fact chose to believe testimony from the medical professionals and the social worker over the parents. Such was the charge of the fact finder. Clearly, sufficient evidence was present to support the trial court's finding. Second, appellant's failure to raise a constitutionality issue at trial or to notify the Attorney General's office of their challenge of the statute, resulted in the procedural bar. Appellants failed to make any showing that any of their fundamental constitutional rights were violated, thus the issue was meritless.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Sufficient evidence was presented through both medical and social service professionals to support the abuse and neglect adjudication. Constitutional issues were procedurally barred for failure to raise them at trial.

Tuck v. Blackmon


NO. 2000-CA-00759-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 402; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 61



March 8, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/01/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. DENISE OWENS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi) declared that defendant lieutenant governor, in failing to order the reading in full of a conference report upon the demand of a plaintiff, a member of the senate, violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 59. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Mississippi Senate was considering conference committee reports when plaintiff senator rose on a point of order and asked that whatever was going to be passed into law be read in full. The request was made pursuant to Miss. Const. art. 4, § 59 (1890). Defendant lieutenant governor ruled that plaintiff senator was not entitled to have a house bill read because the matter before the senate was not a bill, but was a conference report, not subject to the requirements of Miss. Const. art. 4, § 59 (1890). Plaintiffs did not suggest that they or other senators were uninformed as to the text of either the bill or the conference report or that they had not been distributed; or did they argue that there was confusion or misunderstanding of those texts or their import. The complaint merely asserted the violation of Miss. Const. art. 4, § 59 as a violation of the plaintiffs' right and that they had no other remedies at law. Such a statement was not a clear and specific statement of irreparable injury. In her temporary restraining order, the chancellor erred by abandoning normal judicial processes, failing to abide by Miss. R. Civ. P. 4.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and judgment was rendered for the defendant lieutenant governor, dismissing plaintiff senators' complaint with prejudice. In the absence of compelling justification, the court determined it would leave disputes within the deliberative bodies as to their practices and procedures to be decided by those bodies.

 

529 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Red Roof Inns, Inc. v. City of Ridgeland


NO. 1999-CA-00653-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


797 So. 2d 898; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 49



March 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/12/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN T. KITCHENS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee adopted a sign ordinance requiring removal of certain signs over a five-year period. At the end of that period, appellant was notified its sign was non-conforming. Appellant sought review by the Sign Appeals Board, which affirmed the original decision, and appellant sought review in the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which also affirmed. Appellant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: After public hearings, appellee adopted a sign ordinance with an amortization period within which appellant had to bring its sign into compliance. At the end of this period, appellant was notified its sign was not in compliance, and would have to be removed or brought into compliance. Appellant alleged this was an unconstitutional taking of its property under Miss. Const. art. III, § 17. There was a distinction between zoning regulations, which merely restricted the use and enjoyment of property through a lawful exercise of the police power, and the taking of property for public use. The former did not entitle a property owner to compensation, while the latter did. The right to continue a nonconforming use was not a perpetual easement to make a use of one's property detrimental to his neighbors and forbidden to them. Incidental injury would not prevent the operation of the police power, once it was shown to be exercised for proper purposes of public health, safety, morals, and general welfare, and there was no arbitrary or unreasonable application in the particular case. The right to continue a nonconforming use could be lost even where significant value remained in the prior use.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed because appellee engaged in a valid exercise of its police power, in adopting the sign ordinance and providing an amortization period. The ordinance was not a taking under the Mississippi Constitution.

Jensen v. State


NO. 1999-CA-01747-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 383; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 41



February 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 09/22/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER III.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Lee County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that required him to serve out the remainder of his original prison sentence, after the Mississippi Department of Correction (MDOC) decided to remove him from the Intensive Supervision Program (ISP).


OVERVIEW: After appellant pled guilty to possession of marijuana with intent to sell, the trial court sentenced him to 20 years in the custody of the MDOC and placed him in the ISP program. When an MDOC field officer removed appellant from ISP for violating a condition of supervision, appellant sought review from the trial court. It refused to consider his constitutional challenges to the ISP law, and ordered him to serve the rest of his sentence in prison. Appellant sought review. The appellate court reversed the order of imprisonment. While the trial court had reserved the right to review appellant's sentence for one year, the ISP statute had later been amended to vest sole jurisdiction in the MDOC regarding ISP violations. Appellant had to exhaust all administrative remedies before petitioning the trial court for review, and the record did not show that he did so. Thus, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to enter its order, but the appellate court also refused to consider his constitutional challenge to the ISP law, because it could not do so until there was a proper record of the administrative proceedings. The case was remanded so appellant could pursue his administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: Judgement removing appellant from ISP and sending him to prison reversed. Under amended statute, MDOC had initial jurisdiction over ISP issues, and the trial court lacked jurisdiction in this matter until appellant had exhausted his administrative remedies with the MDOC. Order declining to consider appellant's constitutional objections to the ISP law was affirmed, as such review was impossible without a record of the administrative proceedings.

 

531 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Miss. Waste of Hancock County, Inc. v. Bd. of Supervisors


NO. 2000-CA-00187-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


818 So. 2d 326; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 43



February 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/26/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HANCOCK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant waste corporation filed a bill of exceptions before the Circuit Court of Hancock County (Mississippi) after an election was held and appellee Hancock County Board of Supervisors enacted resolutions effectuating certain relief requested in the election. The trial court dismissed the bill of exceptions and appellant challenged the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the appellate court was whether appellee Hancock County Board of Supervisors properly suspended contract negotiations between appellant waste corporation and the regional waste authority. Numerous citizens opposed the location of a privately owned waste facility in county and presented to the board a petition for a special election under Miss. Code Ann. § 19-3-55 (Supp. 2000). The board declined to take unilateral action on the issue, but called for the county-wide special election. Appellant challenged the board's authority to call such an election. Appellant argued the statute was unconstitutional. Appellee was dealing with a petition to determine if its citizens approved of a private company owning their landfill. The restriction sought was not to the use of land, but rather what entity should be vested with the authority to manage the county's waste. Absent a liberty interest, appellant had no basis for asserting a U.S. Const. amend. XIV violation. The board's acts were lawful and authorized by § 19-3-55. Nothing in the record supported the allegation that the board's acts were arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of appellant's bill of exceptions. Appellee's actions in holding special election was not unconstitutional nor unlawful.

 

532 of 603 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Patterson v. Patterson


NO. 1999-CA-00524-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


798 So. 2d 347; 2001 Miss. LEXIS 11



January 25, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/27/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PIKE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. HOLLIS McGEHEE, II.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Pike County Chancery Court (Mississippi) finding that the wrongful death beneficiary of a three-year-old boy was the estate of his deceased mother.


OVERVIEW: The boy's mother and natural father had an affair lasting four months while the two were college students. When she became pregnant and told the father the child was his, he disagreed, but told her that he would take a blood test and discuss the situation afterwards. The father did not know when his son was born because he had not communicated with the boy's mother. The father never met his son and provided no support for his son's birth or medical expenses, food, or clothing. When the boy and his mother were killed in an car accident, the father paid nothing toward his son's funeral bill. He had received confirmation only four days before his son's death that he was the natural father. Judgment denying wrongful death benefits to deceased boy's half-brother, appellant, who was fathered by father, was affirmed. The uncontradicted proof failed to support the claim that appellant half-brother was an heir-at-law of the deceased boy through their common father. The father was not allowed to receive a windfall when he refused to openly treat his deceased son as his own or to comply with his duty to provide essential support, until it appeared he might receive a sizable inheritance.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; deceased's boy's natural father never openly treated his son as his own child and never provided support for the boy. Consequently, father's other son, appellant, conceived in another relationship, was not entitled to wrongful death benefits as an heir to his half-brother.

In re Proposed Initiative Measure No. 20 v. Mahoney


NO. 1999-CA-00912-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


774 So. 2d 397; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 268



December 21, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of September 7, 2000, Previously Reported at: 2000 Miss. LEXIS 205.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant proponent of anti-gambling ballot initiative appealed Circuit Court, First Judicial District, Hinds County (Mississippi), declaratory judgment ruling initiative null and void as violative of Mississippi Bill of Rights and Miss. Const. art. 15, § 273(4). She questioned courts' jurisdiction over merits of initiatives and whether plaintiff challengers had standing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant proponent presented her third anti-gambling initiative for inclusion on the Mississippi ballots. Plaintiff citizens challenged the initiative as violative of unspecified state Bill of Rights provisions as well as Miss. Const., art. 15, § 273(4), which required disclosure of any anticipated negative impact on government revenues. Defendant had simply attached a statement that no negative impact would occur. The court found this assertion unreasonable on its face, and voided the initiative. Defendant had also argued that since a statute specifically provided for initiative litigation to proceed in a single trial court, all others lacked jurisdiction. The court ruled that the statute simply designated venue for reasons of convenience, and that while courts would not judge the wisdom of initiatives, they would judge their compliance with constitutional rules. Finally, every Mississippi elector had standing to challenge the legality of initiatives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed declaratory judgment. All circuit and higher courts could review initiatives, despite legislative placement of venue in only one. Plaintiffs had standing as voters. Although their challenges under the Bill of Rights lacked clarity, it was obvious that government revenue would be affected, whatever defendant said.

Narkeeta Timber Co. v. Jenkins


NO. 1999-CA-01099-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


777 So. 2d 39; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 235



November 30, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NOXUBEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/21/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LEE J. HOWARD.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Noxubee County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which denied appellants' motion to authorize the circuit clerk to cancel judgments against appellants resulting from an action arising from a multiple vehicle accident.


OVERVIEW: After a multiple vehicle accident, appellees filed suits for damages. The jury found in favor of appellees and awarded money judgments. Later, appellants filed a motion to authorize the circuit clerk to cancel judgments against appellants; which the trial court denied. On appeal, appellants argued the trial court erred by requiring appellants to pay an additional $ 100,000 over the $ 925,533 already paid since the result would be tantamount to holding them jointly and severally liable to such an extent as to allow appellees to recover more that 50 percent of their recoverable damages under Miss. Code Ann. § 85-5-7(2) (1999). The court reversed the judgment, determining that appellants had satisfied the judgment against them because 50 percent of the total judgment had been paid to appellees. Implementing the statute, appellants and defendant driver were jointly and severally liable for up to 50 percent of the judgment. Therefore, the court concluded appellants were released from any further obligation to appellees pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 85-5-7 (1999).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying appellants' motion to authorize the circuit clerk to cancel the judgments against them, and the court rendered judgment that the judgments against appellants were satisfied and canceled.

Mason v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01163-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


781 So. 2d 99; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 215



October 26, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Date of Judgment June 11, 1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ITAWAMBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK A. RUSSELL.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF DUI DEATH AND SENTENCE OF TWENTY-FIVE (25) YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS WITH TEN (10) YEARS SUSPENDED, WITH CONDITIONS, POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION OF FIVE (5) YEARS PURSUANT TO MISS. CODE ANN., SECTION 47-7-34, AND PAYMENT OF COURT COSTS, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed convictions, in Itawamba County Circuit Court (Mississippi), of killing and maiming while negligently operating automobile with blood alcohol level of .02 percent or greater, while under 21, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (Supp. 1999), arguing that statute violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV equal protection guarantees.


OVERVIEW: The morning after a teen-agers' drinking party, with blood alcohol still in excess of .02 percent, defendant was involved in an accident that killed one person and maimed another. He was convicted of violating Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (Supp. 1999), which made it unlawful for a person under 21 to drive with even that low a blood alcohol content, and made negligent causing of death or maiming in that situation a felony carrying a long sentence. He challenged the statute as violative of U.S. Const. amend. XIV equal protection guarantees. Since age was not a suspect classification, the court reviewed for rational relationship to legitimate governmental ends. After reviewing federal highway legislation and case law involving similar statutes in other states, the court determined that the statute was rationally related to legitimate governmental ends of protecting public safety and prohibiting under-age drinking and driving.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, because the statute's age-based distinction was rationally related to the legitimate governmental ends of protecting public safety and prohibiting under-age drinking and driving.

 

536 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00675-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


772 So. 2d 1010; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 226



October 19, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PRENTISS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/05/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BARRY W. FORD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Prentiss County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicting him of capital rape, fondling, and attempted sexual battery and sentencing him as a habitual offender to life in prison without the possibility of parole, 10 years in prison, and 30 years in prison, for his offenses, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of raping his 12-year-old daughter. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing appellant's request for a continuance when the State disclosed on the first day of trial a confession letter appellant had written to his daughter, which was given to the State that same day by appellant's ex-wife, because the trial court declined to rule on the letter until the next day, giving appellant an overnight chance to review it. Because there was no evidence showing that appellant assaulted his daughter but did not at the same time rape, fondle, and commit sexual battery on her, given the overwhelming proof, including the daughter's and eyewitnesses' testimony, the trial court did not err by refusing to give a simple assault instruction. The trial court did not err by sentencing appellant to life in prison because it was entitled to do so under the habitual offender statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because appellant was given the chance to review overnight a letter disclosed by the State on the first day of trial, no evidence showed that a jury instruction on simple assault was warranted given the overwhelming evidence against appellant, and appellant's life sentence as a habitual offender was proper.

Smith v. Braden


NO. 97-CA-01290-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 98-CA-00235


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


765 So. 2d 546; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 201



August 24, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/26/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order in the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), First Judicial District, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant doctor, upon a finding that defendant was an employee of a state entity and that plaintiffs failed to file their action within the one-year statute of limitations provided by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11 (Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' minor child died after a medical procedure performed by defendant doctor at a state university medical center. The trial court limited discovery by plaintiffs as to defendant's employment status, and granted defendant's summary judgment motion after finding defendant was a state university employee, and that plaintiffs' action was time-barred. The court reversed and remanded for further discovery on the issue of defendant's employment status, with directions to the trial court to apply the Miller five-part test to determine defendant's status. Because there were questions of fact, specifically with regard to defendant's medical partnerships, coupled with plaintiffs' previous attempt to conduct discovery, the trial court's grant of summary judgment was premature. Further, there was a question of fact as to when the limitations period began to run. Although plaintiffs did not file a motion to compel in response to motions to quash discovery, they did file a response pleading and requested at the hearing on the motion to dismiss that the trial judge require compliance with the subpoenas; thus, plaintiffs were not dilatory in attempting discovery on the issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded for additional discovery and application by the trial judge of the five-part test to determine defendant doctor's employment status. There was also an issue of fact regarding when the statute of limitations began to run against plaintiffs' action.

Tubwell v. Anderson


NO. 1999-CP-00232-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


776 So. 2d 654; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 189



August 17, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 26, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/12/1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) dismissing his various lawsuits against appellee Commission of Corrections, alleging that his earned "good time" credits should not have been revoked under Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 (Supp. 1999) after dismissal because the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court determined that appellant's various lawsuits against appellee were frivolous and dismissed the actions, appellee revoked his earned "good time" credits pursuant to Miss. Code. Ann. § 47-5-138 (Supp. 1999). Appellant challenged, arguing that § 47-5-138 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 47-5-138 was constitutional; the fact that it provided inmates no automatic right to file in forma pauperis appeals in suits which had been deemed to be frivolous did not render the statute unconstitutional, given that no such right existed for non-frivolous lawsuits. The statute was also not unconstitutional because it failed to grant inmates a right to counsel in appealing a revocation of good time credits under the statute, given that paid assistance of counsel in non-capital post-conviction appeals was not required. Appellant was not denied due process because the court had previously affirmed the dismissal as frivolous of appellant's habeas corpus motion.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-138 was constitutional and because appellant was not denied due process.

Sullivan v. Washington


NO. 1998-CA-01518-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


768 So. 2d 881; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 193



August 17, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/27/1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pertaining to medical malpractice action in which judgment was rendered against appellants, appellants sought review of decision of Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying their motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or in alternative, for a new trial, raising issue of immunity under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7(2) (amended 1991).


OVERVIEW: In this medical malpractice action in which judgment pursuant to jury verdict was entered against appellant physicians in the amount of $ 1.7 million, appellants sought review of the trial court's denial of their motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, or in the alternative, for a new trial. The court reversed and rendered judgment for appellants. The court concluded that the outcome of this case was controlled by Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7(2) (amended 1991). It was found that pursuant to § 11-46-7(2) (amended 1991), which applied to actions such as this one that accrued between September 16, 1992 and April 1, 1993, no state employee was to be held personally liable for acts or omissions occurring within the course and scope of the employee's duties. The court concluded that appellants were entitled to immunity from personal liability pursuant to that provision. Under the Miller test, it was concluded that appellants were employees of the state for purposes of liability under the Sovereign Immunity Act.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision was reversed and judgment was rendered for appellants. Court concluded that appellant physicians were employees of the state for purposes of the Sovereign Immunity Act, such that they were immune from personal liability in medical malpractice action based on procedure occurring within course and scope of employment.

Lewis v. State


NO. 1998-KA-01416-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


765 So. 2d 493; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 138



June 8, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/19/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KOSTA N. VLAHOS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment in the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Harrison County (Mississippi), which convicted him on five separate sales of crack cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for selling crack cocaine, based upon testimony of narcotics special agents and a confidential informant. The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions, finding that the "self-help" provision of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(f) was void for vagueness, but the provision of the statute creating the offense was severable and, because defendant could not have availed himself of the "self-help" under any imaginable set of guidelines, his conviction and sentence would not be disturbed. The indictment included five acts which constituted a common scheme to deal in a controlled substance, and the State was not attempting to secure convictions on each of the five transfers, thus Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. 7.07 was not violated. A narcotic's agent's explanation of a street phrase was admissible due to its unusual meaning particular to the drug trade.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. "Self-help" provision of statute was void for vagueness, but was severable from the portion of the statute which created the offense of selling cocaine. Multi-count indictment was permitted because the offenses were based upon transactions connected together or constituting parts of a common scheme or plan.

Mississippi Div. of the United Sons of Confederate Veterans v. Mississippi State Conf. of NAACP Branches


NO. 94-CA-00615-SCT, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 94-CA-00099-SCT, AND NO. 96-CA-01167-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


774 So. 2d 388; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 105



May 4, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 5/27/1994. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. O. DILLARD.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory relief action, appellant civil rights organization appealed judgment of the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which upheld the constitutionality of the Mississippi state flag and denied appellee's motions for sanctions.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal concerned the denial of appellee's motion for sanctions against appellant and appellant's challenges to the constitutionality of the Mississippi state flag solely on the grounds of Mississippi's Constitution. The court determined that sanctions against appellant were inappropriate, as the issues raised had arguable merit. The court concluded that the state flag containing within it the Confederate battle flag could have been flown by the state without violation of the Mississippi or United States Constitutions, as neither the flying of the state flag, nor the flag itself, caused any constitutionally recognizable injury. The court also noted that the flag was Mississippi's flag by custom and usage only. Because 1894 legislation establishing the state flag was repealed in 1906, appellant's contention that the 1894 flag law was unconstitutionally vague was moot. Whether the flag in use continued as the state flag by use and custom was a political decision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; Mississippi state flag containing within it the Confederate battle flag could have been flown by the state without violation of the Mississippi Constitution, and whether flag continued as the state flag by use and custom was a political decision.

McDuff v. State


NO. 1998-KA-01010-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


763 So. 2d 850; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 110



May 4, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 05/08/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE B. READY.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction for negligently causing death while driving under the influence of alcohol in Desoto County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which found Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-8 (1998) was constitutional, permitting appellant's blood to be drawn and tested for alcohol without probable cause.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was traveling on a highway when she lost control of her car and struck an on-coming vehicle, killing the driver. An officer ordered a medical technician to draw blood from appellant, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-8. However, there was no showing of probable cause. The statute authorized a mandatory blood alcohol test after a fatal car accident, regardless of the existence of probable cause. The court reversed appellant's conviction, first finding the statute unconstitutional and finding officer lacked probable cause or an exigent circumstance to order the blood drawn. It was not overwhelmingly burdensome for an officer to obtain probable cause. The statute was not preventative in nature. It was not necessary to circumvent constitutional requirement of probable cause. Blood drawn at by the technician was solely at the request of law enforcement who, at the time, did not have probable cause.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed because the statute was unconstitutional insofar as it mandated the taking of a person's blood and testing it for alcohol without probable case. The state, upon retrial could use blood drawn by medical personnel for diagnostic purposes.

I, § 10 and Miss. Const. art. 3 § 16, and which awarded respondent her deceased brother's pre-retirement death benefits as his designated beneficiary.


OVERVIEW: Decedent was married when he became a member of petitioner public retirement system. Decedent and his wife later separated but did not divorce, and the decedent subsequently designated respondent, his sister as his beneficiary. Upon his pre-retirement death, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-114 (2)(a)(amended 1992), the decedent's benefits were designated to his surviving spouse. Petitioner's claims committee also ruled in favor of the surviving spouse, but the trial court deemed the statute unconstitutional pursuant to U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and Miss. Const. art. 3 § 16. On appeal, the state supreme court affirmed in part and vacated in part, reasoning the statute was unconstitutional as applied to the case because it impaired the decedent's right to designate his beneficiary without conferring a comparable right upon the decedent. The state supreme court determined however, insufficient evidence existed to hold the statute invalid in all situations.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and vacated in part, because the lower court properly determined that the relevant statute deprived the decedent of his constitutional right to contract, but insufficient evidence was submitted regarding whether the statute was unconstitutional in all cases.

Mississippi Comm'n on Judicial Performance v. Byers


NO. 1998-JP-01835-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


757 So. 2d 961; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 27



February 17, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: December 11, 1998. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COMMISSION ON JUDICIAL PERFORMANCE.



DISPOSITION: PUBLIC REPRIMAND AND FINE OF $ 1,500 AND PAYMENT OF $ 2,023. 59 IN COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent judge appealed from recommendations of the Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance that respondent judge be removed from office and ordered to pay a fine and all costs associated with the review of respondent's judicial performance.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged with judicial misconduct. Petitioner adopted the recommendations of its committee that conducted a trial that judicial sanctions be imposed on respondent. Respondent alleged prosecutorial misconduct and equal protection violations. After reviewing the entire record, the court found that there were no specific acts that constituted bias and petitioner promptly corrected whatever bias might have existed. Additionally, no proof was presented that warranted a finding of abuse of prosecutorial discretion based on respondent's race or gender. The court found that while respondent clearly committed errors in judgment violating statutes and judicial canons, her actions did not constitute willful misconduct. However, respondent's abuse of her contempt powers violated Miss. Const. § 177A. The court found by clear and convincing evidence that respondent's conduct, in its totality, constituted willful misconduct in office and conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice. She was fined and ordered publicly reprimanded.


OUTCOME: Respondent was ordered to be publicly reprimanded because she either knew or should have known her actions exceeded her authority and jurisdiction. She engaged in willful misconduct in office and engaged in conduct which was prejudicial to the administration of justice which brought the judicial office into disrepute.

Triplett v. Mayor of Vicksburg


NO. 1998-CA-01530-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


758 So. 2d 399; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 28



February 17, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: July 28, 1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK G. VOLLOR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Warren County Circuit Court, dismissing his bill of exceptions, filed in response to an assessment for charges for cleaning his property.


OVERVIEW: Appellees held a meeting wherein it was decided that the city should clean up appellant's property because it posed a public health and safety hazard. Charges for the cleaning of the property were to be assessed against appellant. Appellant filed a bill of exceptions, containing general allegations that the decision was not supported by substantial, credible evidence; that the ruling was arbitrary and capricious, beyond the power of appellees; and that the provisions for appeal in the city ordinance were inadequate. The trial judge dismissed the bill of exceptions as not complying with statutory requirements. The court found that because there was no hearing on the merits of the appeal, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-45 (1994) required that appellant be given leave to amend his bill of exceptions to cure the defects so that his appeal could proceed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded; statute required that appellant be given leave to amend his bill of exceptions to cure any alleged deficiencies.

Mississippi Transp. Comm'n v. Ronald Adams Contr., Inc.


NO. 98-CA-00040-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


753 So. 2d 1077; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 31



February 17, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 11/06/1997. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT LEWIS GIBBS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ON DIRECT APPEAL; REVERSED ON CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties appealed from a judgment in the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which entered final judgment and awarded plaintiff damages in a breach of construction contract action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contractor was awarded a contract by the defendant transportation commission for a highway improvement construction project. The contract contained a "no damage for delay" clause. Defendant did not issue the Notice to Proceed, a key term of the contract, until 86 days after the date indicated in the contract. Plaintiff instituted an action against defendant for damages allegedly incurred as a result of the delay. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that the contract was unambiguous and a matter for determination by the court rather than the jury. The trial court denied the motion on the grounds that the contract was ambiguous and therefore a matter of determination for the jury. A jury awarded plaintiff a judgment and defendant appealed, arguing that the court erred in refusing defendant's motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed the decision because the jury was correctly presented with issues that only could be resolved by the trier of fact.


OUTCOME: Because the defendant did not make an objection to instructions given to the jury, and the jury was correctly presented with issues that only could be resolved by the trier of fact, the court affirmed the decision holding that that portion of the appeal was without merit.

Crawford v. State


NO. 1998-KA-01578-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


754 So. 2d 1211; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 8



January 20, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/07/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE C. CARLSON, JR. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: TATE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi) capital rape conviction under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-65(1) and subsequent life imprisonment sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his capital rape conviction of his 12-year-old stepdaughter. The court affirmed. Testimony by appellee State's expert witness was proper because her testimony met the Frye test in that it would have been accepted within the medical community, and was admissible under Miss. R. Evid. 702 as scientific, technical, and specialized evidence that assisted the jury. Amending the indictment did not prejudice appellant because both the original and amended indictments were made well within the two-year limitation period. Prosecution was commenced by the initial indictment well within two years from the dates the crimes occurred. Use of the word "rape" in the indictment was not so vague that it denied appellant his due process. Evidence of appellant's prior sexual acts with the victim was admissible because it showed appellant's lascivious disposition toward his particular victim. Irrelevant testimony was properly excluded and there was ample evidence to convict.


OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed. Expert testimony was properly admitted; amending the indictment did not prejudice appellant; using the word "rape" in the indictment was not so vague as to violate due process; evidence of prior sexual acts with the victim was admissible; and sufficient evidence existed to convict.

Boatner v. State


NO. 1998-KM-01780-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


754 So. 2d 1184; 2000 Miss. LEXIS 57



January 13, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: GREENE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 01/15/1998. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Greene County Circuit Court (Mississippi) where she was found guilty of misdemeanor abuse of a vulnerable adult under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-47-19(1), (2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of misdemeanor abuse of a vulnerable adult under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-47-19(1), (2), and was tried and convicted. In light of the plain language of Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-47-5(a), 43-47-5(i), 43-47-5(k), 43-47-19, the statute in question was clear and did not constitute a denial of due process. Defendant raised for the first time on appeal that she was denied her U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront witnesses against her, and so the issue was waived. The sentence imposed against defendant did not exceed the maximum fine or imprisonment. The evidence was sufficient to support the verdict and so the verdict could not be overturned.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because there was no reversible error; the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, defendant could not raise for the first time on appeal her claim that her U.S. Const. amend. VI rights were violated, the sentence imposed by the trial court was within its authority, and the evidence supported the judgment.

Putnam v. State


NO. 2002-CP-01538-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


877 So. 2d 468; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1205



December 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Putnam v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 328 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Putnam v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 389 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 30, 2004)
Writ of certiorari denied Putnam v. State, 878 So. 2d 67, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 861 (Miss., 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Putnam v. Dove, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45812 (S.D. Miss., Feb. 10, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Putnam v. Epps, 2007 Miss. App. LEXIS 36 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 6, 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Putnam v. State, 2016 Miss. App. LEXIS 677 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 8/29/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF BASED ON INVOLUNTARY GUILTY PLEA IS DENIED.
Putnam v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 422 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi) denying the inmate's motion for post-conviction relief with regard to the inmate's conviction of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: In his post-conviction petition, the inmate challenged his armed robbery conviction. The armed robbery indictment stated the essential facts constituting the offense charged as required under Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. R. 7.06 even though the inmate never took and carried away the property of another. Under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 (Rev. 2000), the inmate could be convicted of armed robbery while attempting to complete the crime. The inmate's guilty plea was entered knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily, because he was unaware that he did not complete one of the essential elements, in that he did not take and carry away the personal property of another. The inmate completed the essential elements, as the inmate could be convicted without taking and carrying away the property of another under § 97-3-79. Counsel was not ineffective where counsel allegedly failed to inform the inmate that the inmate's failure to take and carry away the property of another meant that he did not satisfy the elements of the offense of armed robbery. There was no such requirement for a conviction under § 97-3-79.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
