Torns v. State


NO. 2002-CP-00431-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


866 So. 2d 486; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1115



November 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Motion denied by Torns v. Mississippi, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20181 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 2/20/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED WITH PREJUDICE.
Torns v. State, 687 So. 2d 770, 1996 Miss. App. LEXIS 233 (Miss. Ct. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a pro se motion for post-conviction relief alleging that his convictions and sentences were unconstitutional and that he was entitled to relief on the basis of due process and equal protection. The Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) dismissed the motion. His motion for leave to proceed before the highest appellate court was also denied. His second post-conviction motion was denied and dismissed. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his motions the inmate sought post-conviction relief for a 1986 conviction and for two 1993 convictions. His first motion was filed in March 2001, and his second motion was filed in August 2001. The court dismissed the appeal from order denying the first post-conviction motion. First, the inmate never obtained permission from the highest state appellate court to file a post conviction relief motion with respect to the 1993 convictions; therefore, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-7 (Supp. 2003) the court was without jurisdiction to address the allegations regarding those convictions. Regarding the 1986 conviction, the inmate's appeal from the denial of the motion was untimely under Miss. R. App. P. 4(a) because the appeal was filed 11 months after denial of the motion for post-conviction relief. Further, the court was without jurisdiction even if the appeal were from denial of the second motion because the filing of a second such motion was barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(6) (Supp. 2003).


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal and taxed all costs to the county.

 

554 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Warren


NO. 2002-CA-00274-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


858 So. 2d 168; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 965



October 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Brown v. Warren, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1057 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 1/15/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. W. SWAN YERGER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: SUMMARY JUDGMENT FOR APPELLEES.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient suffered from acute heart disease, and underwent heart bypass surgery. Subsequently her legs were amputated, as a result of blood clots, which arose from a prescribed medication. She sued defendants, the primary doctor, and a hematologist, for medical malpractice. The Hinds County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted summary judgment for the doctors on grounds of immunity as State employees. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue was whether the doctors were acting as employees of the University of Mississippi Medical Center (UMMC), or whether they were independent contractors, for purposes of immunity or liability. The operational purpose of UMMC was to serve the State, and also to provide care for persons on Medicaid. However, the doctors did wear two hats, as they were entitled to engage in separate private practice, to a degree. Applying the standard of Miller v. Meeks, the appellate court noted the Board of Trustees of State Institutions of Higher Learning, exercised reasonable control over the doctors, and the State had the power to terminate the doctors' contract. The fact the doctors exercised their professional judgment in treating patients, did not mean that they were independent contractors. One doctor testified he was serving a public function, and providing care for the subject patient, through Medicaid. The appellate court held the uncontroverted evidence was that the doctors were acting as employees of UMMC. Thus, pursuant to Mississippi's former sovereign immunity law, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-7(2) (Supp. 1991), the doctors were immune from liability.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs on appeal were assessed to the patient.

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI

Pickle v. Miss. State Parole Bd.


NO. 2002-CP-00839-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


850 So. 2d 195; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 630



July 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Pickle v. Miss. State Parole Bd., 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 688 (Miss. Ct. App., July 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SUNFLOWER COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 4/30/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD A. SMITH. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was considered for parole by the Mississippi State Parole Board (board) and denied release. The board's ruling stated that no further review of the inmate's eligibility would be undertaken for five years. The inmate filed a petition for writ of mandamus to compel the board to conduct annual reviews of eligibility for parole. The Sunflower County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate argued that the portion of the board's decision to hold no further review for five years violated the former Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-5(7) (Rev. 2000). The inmate argued that the former subsection required that every potentially eligible inmate receive reconsideration for parole on an annual basis. The board countered that the subsection required only a one-time action by the board. Additionally, the board noted that the subsection was removed in the amended statute. The appellate court rejected the inmate's arguments. The court found that the plain reading of the former section indicated that the Mississippi Legislature intended to mandate a one-time review in the year 2000 of all inmates then falling within the class of offenders defined in the subsection. Had the Legislature intended to institute an on-going requirement that, henceforth, all potentially-eligible inmates would receive at least an annual formal evaluation of eligibility, the court found that the Legislature would have said so in clear terms. Thus, the court declined to undertake the strained reading of this passage that would be required to obtain the inmate's meaning of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gardner v. State


NO. 2002-CP-00327-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


848 So. 2d 900; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 570



June 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Gardner v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 649 (Miss. Ct. App., June 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 5/16/2002. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NESHOBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. MARCUS D. GORDON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision of the Neshoba County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had pleaded guilty to burglary and was serving time. While working on a road crew, the inmate escaped and burglarized another home. He was ultimately placed back in custody. He pleaded guilty to the new charges and was sentenced to serve six years for the burglary and three years for the escape. He sought post-conviction relief, which the trial court denied. The court affirmed on appeal. While the inmate raised several issues on appeal, the court found them all time barred and procedurally barred according to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (Supp. 2002) because the inmate filed his motion for post-conviction relief well beyond the three-year limitations period. There were no exceptions that extended this period, and the inmate's pro se status and ignorance of the law alone were insufficient to establish cause. Without waiving the procedural bar, the court addressed the inmate's claim that he received an unconstitutional sentence. The court found no error. The inmate was properly charged under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-9-45 (Rev. 2002) and entered a plea of guilty, and the sentence he received was well within the maximum prescribed by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Friley v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00041-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 654; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 584



June 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Friley v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 1041 (Miss. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2003)
Later proceeding at Friley v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 174 (Miss., Feb. 5, 2004)
Later proceeding at Friley v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 271 (Miss., Mar. 18, 2004)
Motion denied by Friley v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 389 (Miss., Apr. 15, 2004)
Writ of certiorari granted Friley v. State, 870 So. 2d 666, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 394 (Miss., 2004)
Reversed by Friley v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 998 (Miss., Aug. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: WARREN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 1/17/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ISADORE W. PATRICK, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DEFENDANT SENTENCED TO FIFTEEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Warren County Circuit Court, Mississippi, with the sexual battery of a female child. The jury returned a verdict of not guilty to the charge of sexual battery, but guilty to the lesser offense of molestation, and the trial court sentenced him to 15 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court erred by granting a jury instruction which authorized the jury to find him guilty of molestation. The appellate court initially noted jury instructions which were unsupported by the evidence or incorrectly stated the law were not to be given to the jury. The appellate court found, according to the record, that the trial judge mistakenly determined the crime of molestation under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-23 (2000) to be a lesser-included offense of sexual battery. The appellate court held molestation was recognized as a separate offense from sexual battery as defendants were frequently charged with both crimes simultaneously. The appellate court concluded to allow defendant to be convicted of a crime for which he was never charged would have created an injustice as the legislature felt it necessary to construct two separate and distinct statutes regarding sexual battery and molestation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and rendered.

McClurg v. State


NO. 2002-CP-00324-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 592



June 24, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by McClurg v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 413 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 13, 2004)
Substituted opinion at McClurg v. State, 2004 Miss. App. LEXIS 572 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 9/13/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. BETTY W. SANDERS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: COMPLAINT DISMISSED WITH PREJUDICE; MOTION TO AMEND OR ALTER THE JUDGMENT DENIED.
McClurg v. State, 758 So. 2d 473, 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 168 (Miss. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sued the State, alleging that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3(1)(g) (Supp. 2002), an amendment to a parole statute, violated his right to equal protection of the law. The Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi) found that the inmate did not have standing to challenge the amendment and dismissed the complaint. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 47-7-3(1)(g) barred parole for nonviolent first offenders convicted between July 1, 1995 and January 1, 2000. The inmate maintained (though the record was silent on this issue) that he was convicted between June 30, 1995, and January 1, 2000; therefore, he was ineligible for parole even if he was a "first offender." The appeals court held the case was not subject to dismissal due to the absence of any proof of service of process, since the State participated in the appeal, thereby waving proper service under Miss. R. Civ. P. 4(e). There was no evidence in the record as to the number of convictions or the sentences to which the inmate was subject. The trial court denied relief based on its factual finding that the inmate was not a "first offender" and therefore lacked standing to challenge Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3(1)(g). It erred because it relied on extra-record information to make that finding. On remand, the State had to prove whether the inmate was a "first offender" under § 47-7-3(1)(g) -- i.e., had two or more convictions under charges separately brought and arising out of separate incidents at different times. If so, dismissal for lack of standing would be proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the complaint was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Atwell v. State


NO. 2002-CP-01572-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


848 So. 2d 190; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 348



April 22, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 23, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Atwell v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 625 (Miss. Ct. App., June 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 9/6/2002. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY, SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denying the inmate's motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pled guilty to felony driving under the influence. He received a five year suspended sentence with two years of post-release supervision. A provision of the sentencing order permitted the inmate to transfer his supervision to either Tennessee or Georgia, if he was accepted by one of those states. The suspension was revoked after the inmate failed to report to his probation officer, left the state, and was twice arrested for driving under the influence. The suspension was revoked in its entirety. The inmate claimed that the felony driving under the influence conviction pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(2)(c) (Rev. 1996) was improper, because both of the predicate convictions occurred out-of-state. Out-of-state convictions, however, constituted predicate convictions pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(7) (Rev. 1996). The inmate's suspension was properly revoked because he left the state, although the sentencing order permitted him to do so. The inmate had to first seek permission to transfer his supervision, and he failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gross v. State


NO. 2001-CA-01185-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


852 So. 2d 671; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 225



March 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Gross v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 577 (Miss. Ct. App., May 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: DESOTO COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 6/14/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GEORGE B. READY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ORDER DISMISSING MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF. MOTION TO RECONSIDER DISMISSAL DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief in the Circuit Court of Desoto County, Mississippi. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty in 1998 to driving under the influence of intoxicants thereby causing the death of another, after the trial court denied his motion to suppress blood test results taken under the authority of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-8 (Rev. 1996) while defendant was being treated in a hospital following an accident. The statute was declared unconstitutional in 2000 in the case of McDuff v. State. The appellate court held that defendant's petition was properly denied. The fact that defendant chose to plea guilty rather than challenging the trial court's evidentiary ruling did not entitle defendant to challenge the ruling outside the time limits on seeking post-conviction relief.

Weaver v. State


NO. 2001-CA-00725-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 407; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 234



March 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Weaver v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 618 (Miss. Ct. App., June 17, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Weaver v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 663 (Miss. Ct. App., June 17, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied Weaver v. State, 859 So. 2d 1017, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 515 (Miss., Oct. 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 10/12/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DEFENDANT'S MOTION TO VACATE AND SET ASIDE SENTENCE DENIED.
Weaver v. State, 764 So. 2d 479, 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 351 (Miss. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Chickasaw County (Mississippi) modifying the conditions by which he could avoid spending the final 15 years of a 20 year sentence in confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to one count of burglary of a dwelling. The judgment of sentence stated that defendant was to be banished from a city for the period of his suspended sentence. After a hearing on remand, the circuit court amended the original judgment to remove the provision for banishment and placed defendant on supervised probation for a period of five years upon his release from custody. On appeal, defendant contended that the added requirement of supervised probation was a new and additional element of punishment, more onerous than his original sentence, resulting in his being punished twice for the same crime in violation of the Double Jeopardy provisions of the United States Constitution. The appellate court concluded that the substitution of some period of formal probationary supervision in place of a like term of banishment did not constitute an increase in the degree or character of defendant's punishment that would invoke constitutional concerns of double jeopardy. Also, the supervised probation was essentially rehabilitative in its objectives and not punitive. Thus, the change in probation terms was within the circuit court's authority.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

564 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Dunbar v. Renfroe (In re Savell)


NO. 2001-CP-01208-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 378; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 179



March 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Dunbar v. Renfroe, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 525 (Miss. Ct. App., May 20, 2003)
Later proceeding at, En banc In re Savell v. Renfroe, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 517 (Miss., Oct. 9, 2003)
Writ of certiorari granted Dunbar v. Renfroe (In re Guardianship of Savell), 860 So. 2d 315, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 661 (Miss., 2003)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by In re Savell v. Renfroe, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 800 (Miss., July 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 7/18/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SCOTT COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. H. DAVID CLARK, II. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AMENDMENT TO ATTORNEY'S FEES.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee conservatrix filed a petition for authority to settle a doubtful claim on behalf of the ward's estate. The Scott County Chancery Court (Mississippi) approved the settlement of the doubtful claim with the appellant law firm, but approved attorney's fees of only 33 1/3 percent for the law firm. The law firm appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the law firm argued that because it was employed under a durable power of attorney, the chancellor lacked authority to award attorney's fees in an amount less than that identified by the parties' employment contract. The law firm argued that under Durable Power of Attorney Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 87-3-101 et seq., the chancellor was obligated to approve the employment contract as written. The appellate court rejected the law firm's argument. While not mandated by law to do so, all of the parties to the contract chose to voluntarily submit to the chancellor for approval the settlement of the claim, and the disbursement of funds paid in settlement of this claim. By voluntarily submitting this matter to the chancellor for approval, the parties did so for all purposes. Included within the chancellor's power to approve was of necessity included the power to disapprove. Having found that the chancellor had the power to disapprove of the parties' claim, the appellate court found that the chancellor's actions were supported by substantial credible evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ivory v. State


NO. 2002-KA-00077-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


840 So. 2d 755; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 211



March 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Ivory v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 423 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: ADAMS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 11/30/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FORREST A. JOHNSON, JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: GUILTY AS CHARGED OF THE SALE OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED TO 30 YEARS WITH 10 SUSPENDED, FIVE YEARS' POST-RELEASE SUPERVISION, AND FINED $ 5,000 PLUS COSTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Adams County, Mississippi, of sale of cocaine, and was sentenced to 30 years in prison, with 10 years suspended and five years post-release supervision. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine to a police informant in a controlled buy. Defendant turned himself in to police after having briefly left the state. At trial, defendant denied having sold cocaine to the informant, claiming that the informant was lying to help his own case. Defendant also claimed that the police badgered him and that his incriminating statements were made without having been advised of his rights. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motions for a directed verdict or a new trial and that the sentence was excessive. The appellate court held that there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict and the resolution in conflicts in the evidence was the province of the jury, not the appellate court. Defendant's statements were properly admitted. Defendant waived the right to object to the sentence by not raising the issue in the trial court. Even if the issue was not waived, the sentence was within the statutory limits for the offense and was within the discretion of the trial court to impose.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

 

566 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Gautier v. Miss. Transp. Comm'n


NO. 2001-CA-01795-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


839 So. 2d 588; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 154



March 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Gautier v. Miss. Transp. Comm'n, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 266 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: JACKSON COUNTY SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 9/18/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. T. LARRY WILSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: APPELLANTS AWARDED $ 831,100 FOR CONDEMNED PROPERTY; TITLE TO PROPERTY CONFIRMED IN APPELLEE AND APPELLEE ORDERED TO PAY COSTS OF COURT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State instituted an eminent domain proceeding to condemn appellant owners' property to build a new bridge. Following a trial, the Jackson County Special Court of Eminent Domain (Mississippi) returned a verdict stating that the State pay the owners $ 831,000 for the taking of their property and denied the owners' subsequent motion for additur or in the alternative a new trial. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the owners argued, inter alia, that the verdict was contrary to the overwhelming weight of the credible evidence or the result of bias, prejudice, or passion on the part of the jury. The owners also argued the trial court erred by refusing to grant the owners an additur or, in the alternative, a new trial. The appellate court rejected the owners' arguments. The State presented two experts who testified that the value of the owners' property was $ 940,936 and $ 831,100 respectively. The owners' expert testified that the property was worth $ 990,995. The jury relied most heavily on one of the State's experts. As the amount set by the jury was between those values offered by all three experts, the court could not find that bias, passion, or prejudice influenced the award. The court further held that, because the weight of evidence was not against the jury's verdict, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the owners' motion for additur or new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McKenzie v. State


NO. 2001-CP-01991-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


856 So. 2d 344; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 132



March 4, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McKenzie v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 804 (Miss. Ct. App., Aug. 26, 2003)

Post-conviction relief denied at McKenzie v. State, 946 So. 2d 392, 2006 Miss. App. LEXIS 388 (Miss. Ct. App., 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc McKenzie v. State, 947 So. 2d 960, 2007 Miss. LEXIS 57 (Miss., 2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Transferred by McKenzie v. Brewer, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16833 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 8, 2007)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at McKenzie v. State, 30 So. 3d 368, 2009 Miss. App. LEXIS 624 (Miss. Ct. App., 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed McKenzie v. Mississippi, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 37064 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 24, 2011)
Related proceeding at McKenzie v. Mississippi, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 78446 (S.D. Miss., June 17, 2015)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McKenzie v. Hood, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14329 (S.D. Miss., Jan. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/4/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POST-CONVICTION RELIEF DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant, upon his guilty plea, of statutory rape. After denial of his request for post-conviction relief, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high-school teacher who engaged in a sexual relationship with the victim, one of his 15-year-old students. Eventually, defendant pled guilty to the crime of statutory rape. While the plea agreement did not specifically state that there would be a loss of the right against self-incrimination, it was apparent that the equivalent was stated in the plea agreement. Thus, defendant's guilty plea was made voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently. Also, the appellate court found that defendant understood the charges and sentences available and he pled guilty with full knowledge. Thus, his guilty plea was voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently made. Additionally, defendant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel. In addition, because the first indictment was nolle prosequi before he pled guilty, defendant was not subject to double jeopardy. Further, the indictment sufficiently alleged the identity of the victim, chaste character was not required under the new statute, and the location of the crime was included. In addition, there was sufficient evidence to support a guilty finding. Finally, defendant's sentence was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Readus v. State


NO. 2001-CA-01182-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


837 So. 2d 209; 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 42



February 4, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PANOLA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 6/26/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PCR ACTION SUMMARILY DISMISSED BY TRIAL COURT.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty before the Panola County Circuit Court, Mississippi, to 14 charges of burglary and attempted burglary. The trial court imposed 2 consecutive 25-year sentences and consecutive 10-year suspended sentences on each remaining charge. Thereafter, defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief, which was summarily dismissed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on his post-conviction relief motion, as his motion and affidavits raised questions as to whether his guilty pleas were involuntary, whether counsel was ineffective, and whether the sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate to the crime. In his motion and the affidavit of his mother, defendant contended he entered the guilty plea because of his attorney's representation of a lesser sentence than what he actually received. The appellate court initially noted that if a defendant attached an affidavit of another person supporting his post-conviction relief motion, he could avoid summary dismissal if his motion alleged facts that required further inquiry in the expanded setting of an evidentiary hearing. The appellate court held defendant's motion was sufficient to raise a question as to whether his plea was actually voluntary and whether he was denied the effective assistance of counsel. The appellate court concluded the trial court should not have summarily dismissed the motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded to consider the merits of defendant's allegations of an involuntary plea and ineffective assistance of counsel.

Ray v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


844 So. 2d 483; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 690



December 3, 2002, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 4/16/2001. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONTGOMERY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. C. E. MORGAN, III DISTRICT ATTORNEY: TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CONVICTED OF AGGRAVATED ASSAULT; SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF 20 YEARS' IMPRISONMENT WITH 8 YEARS SUSPENDED FOR A PERIOD OF FIVE YEARS, AND PAY ALL COSTS, FEES AND ASSESSMENTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault in the Montgomery County, Mississippi, Circuit Court, and was sentenced to 20 years in prison, of which 8 years were suspended for a period of 5 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove to his son-in-law's house and shot the son-in-law in the head during an argument over the repair of a roof. Defendant argued that he had been improperly rearrested after having been released on bond, that the district attorney should have recused himself because he was related to the victim, that the sentence was unlawful and excessive, that he had been denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the trial court erred in refusing to give certain jury instructions. Defendant's claims of ineffective assistance were without merit. The substance of defendant's requested instructions on defendant's right to carry a weapon and self-defense were adequately covered in other areas.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Lewis v. State


NO. 2001-KA-01050-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


831 So. 2d 553; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 672



November 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 3/30/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. STEPHEN B. SIMPSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: GUILTY FELONY DUI. SERVE 3 YEARS IN THE MDOC; SUCCESSFULLY COMPLETE LONG TERM DRUG AND ALCOHOL REHABILITATION TREATMENT PROGRAM.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of felony driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seated in the driver's seat of a parked vehicle. When approached by an officer, defendant stated that the vehicle was out of gas. He was charged with driving under the influence. Defendant later contended that the driver left him in the vehicle when he went to purchase more gas. After defendant was convicted, he sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the trial court erred in defining the word "operate." Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 required that the vehicle must have been capable of being moved by defendant, whether or not he was then in the act of causing it to move. Both defendant and the vehicle must have had a present ability to move. The instruction given could have led to a conviction, even if the jurors believed defendant's story that he was only behind the wheel after the car had run out of gas. However, the court found that the trial court was not required to give an instruction on circumstantial evidence, because direct evidence of the crime was offered. Finally, the court held that a prior driving under the influence conviction was self authenticating under Miss. R. Evid. 902, despite the fact that the seal was not recognizable on the copy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Agee v. State


NO. 2001-CP-00609-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


829 So. 2d 726; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 573



October 29, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SIMPSON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 03/09/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT G. EVANS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POSTCONVICTION RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for postconviction relief in the Circuit Court of Simpson County, Mississippi. The trial court denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of sexual battery on a child under the age of 14 and was sentenced to two concurrent five-year prison terms. Defendant argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because his attorney did not challenge an unconstitutional indictment or assert a valid statute of limitations defense. The appellate court found no error. Defendant's claim regarding the indictment was not that the indictment itself was unconstitutional, only that defendant had been charged under the wrong subsection of the statute. The court rejected that argument because the indictment properly charged defendant with the offense under the version of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (1)(c) that was in effect at the time of the offense. The prosecution commenced by indictment 17 months after the date of the alleged offense and was within the two year limitation period provided in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-1-5 (Rev. 2000). The fact that the trial occurred more than two years after the offense affected only defendant's speedy trial rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kearley v. State


NO. 2001-KA-00374-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


843 So. 2d 66; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 560



October 22, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Kearley v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 28 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 14, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Kearley v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 29 (Miss. Ct. App., Jan. 14, 2003)
Petition for certiorari filed at (non-U.S. Supreme Court datelines) Kearley v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 76 (Miss., Feb. 12, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied Kearley v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 410 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 02/15/2001 COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAUDERDALE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LARRY EUGENE ROBERTS TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: SEXUAL BATTERY: SENTENCED TO 20 YEARS WITH 15 YEARS SUSPENDED, 5 YEARS TO SERVE, AND 5 YEARS SUPERVISED PROBATION TO FOLLOW.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery in the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi). Defendant appealed, asserting that the trial court: (1) made comments prejudicial to his defense, (2) improperly excluded evidence of the alleged victim's character, (3) failed to require proper authentication of the alleged correspondence from defendant to the victim. Defendant also alleged his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with having inserted his finger into the 15 year-old victim's vagina, and subsequently sending very explicit e-mails to the victim. Defendant argued that he was prejudiced by the trial judge's reference to a party who did not testify as "a witness," and the references to the child as the "victim" in jury instructions. However, defendant failed to objected to any of these matters at trial and they were not preserved for appeal. Defendant made a number of assertions as to why his counsel was ineffective, including that his attorney failed to object to leaving a female on the jury who had previously rendered a guilty verdict in a rape case. However, the appellate court found nothing about defendant's claims that would have had the likely effect of changing the outcome of the case. The trial court properly excluded evidence of the victim's prior bad character, because it was not relevant to the charge of sexual battery under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95(1)(c) (Rev. 2000). Finally, the e-mails were properly admitted because the trial judge found that the victim had vouched for their accuracy, and an officer testified that defendant admitted that he sent the e-mails.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Oby v. State


NO. 2001-KA-01636-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


827 So. 2d 731; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 528



October 1, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PANOLA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 10/12/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ANDREW C. BAKER. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: APPELLANT FOUND GUILTY OF POSSESSION OF COCAINE AND SENTENCED TO LIFE IN PRISON WITHOUT POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine by the Circuit Court of Panola County, Mississippi. He was sentenced as a habitual offender to life in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections without the possibility of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Late one evening, defendant was sitting in a car parked on the edge of a cemetery. A narcotics officer pulled up beside defendant, exited his vehicle, and instructed defendant to show his hands. Defendant drove off. During a pursuit, the officer saw defendant throw a plastic bag and other objects out of the car window. Defendant eventually stopped his car. The officer searched the roadside and found three rocks of crack cocaine inside a plastic bag. On appeal, defendant argued the trial court improperly allowed the State to introduce his testimony from a prior revocation hearing. At the hearing defendant explained that he was parked at the cemetery to meet a woman in order to swap crack cocaine for sex. This contradicted his trial testimony in which he claimed he had no cocaine. The appeals court held defendant's prior assertion was a statement made by a party opponent and, thus, was admissible as an exception to the hearsay rule. His life sentence without parole was not grossly disproportionate to a habitual offender's crime of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant's case was not prejudiced by an amendment to the indictment, as the amendment affected the penalty only.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McDonald v. McDonald


NO. 1999-CP-00848-COA CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 1999-CP-01259-COA & NO. 1999-CP-01384-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


850 So. 2d 1182; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 527



October 1, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by McDonald v. McDonald, 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 806 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 17, 2002)
Writ of certiorari granted McDonald v. McDonald, 840 So. 2d 716, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 164 (Miss., 2003)
Affirmed by McDonald v. McDonald, 876 So. 2d 296, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 795 (Miss., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 03/17/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM L. GRIFFIN JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: MODIFICATION OF ORIGINAL DIVORCE DECREE; APPELLANT FOUND IN CONTEMPT FOR WILFUL VIOLATION OF VISITATION RIGHTS; TEMPORARY ORDER TRANSFERRING CUSTODY OF TWO CHILDREN TO THE APPELLEE.
McDonald v. Griffin, 228 F.3d 409, 2000 U.S. App. LEXIS 18860 (5th Cir. Miss., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband filed from divorce from appellee wife. The Lee County Chancery Court, Mississippi, issued an order regarding visitation that neither the husband nor his attorney signed, awarded the wife $ 1106 in court costs, and held the husband in contempt of court. The husband appealed each order and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: After the husband and the wife divorced, the husband was granted custody of two of their children, and the wife had visitation. The wife moved for a modification of the visitation rights as the husband was interfering with her visitation. The matter was hard by a former chancellor as all of the county's chancellors had been recused. The court entered a new visitation schedule, but neither the husband nor his attorney signed the order. The wife moved for a contempt order against the husband when he continued to interfere with her visitation rights. The chancellor held the husband in contempt and ordered that he pay the wife's attorney fees and costs. The appellate court held that the visitation order was valid even though it had not been signed by the husband or his attorney, as it was agreed to in open court. Further, as there was a constitutional basis for appointing the former chancellor to hear the case, his rulings were valid. The appellate court held that fees assessed against the husband were statutorily authorized and proper. Finally, the issuance of the contempt order was proper as the husband had refused to cooperate with his wife.


OUTCOME: The orders of the chancery court, including the change in visitation, the imposition of costs against the husband, and holding the husband in contempt, were affirmed.

Alonso v. State


NO. 2000-KA-02058-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


838 So. 2d 309; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 493



September 3, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Alonso v. State, 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 763 (Miss. Ct. App., Dec. 3, 2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Alonso v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 178 (Miss. Ct. App., Feb. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/07/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM F. COLEMAN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 12/07/2000: AGGRAVATED ASSAULT SENTENCED TO 5 YEARS, WITH 4 YEARS SUSPENDED LEAVING 1 YEAR TO SERVE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court, Mississippi, which convicted him of aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made several arguments on appeal. He argued that the trial court erred in failing to sustain his motion for a directed verdict and or for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict because the jury's verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. The instant court noted that defendant's first three issues were raised for the first time on appeal and were not properly preserved for appellate review. Regarding defendant's argument that the trial court erred in allowing a surgeon who treated the victim to testify as to the meaning of a legal term, "serious bodily injury," thereby invading the province of the jury, the surgeon was properly allowed to offer an opinion as to whether the victim sustained a "serious bodily injury." Defendant failed to demonstrate the likelihood of a different outcome had counsel performed in a different manner. This failure precluded a finding of ineffective assistance of counsel. There was clearly substantial credible evidence upon which the jury could and did find that defendant assaulted the victim. There was no credible basis upon which the instant court could find the verdict of guilty to be contrary to the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Holloman v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00868-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


820 So. 2d 52; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 345



June 18, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COAHOMA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 05/26/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HOWARD Q. DAVIS JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: VEHICULAR HOMICIDE: SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF 20 YEARS IN THE MDOC, WITH THE LAST 10 SUSPENDED. THE FIRST 5 YEARS OF THE SUSPENDED TIME IS ORDERED TO BE SERVED ON POST RELEASE SUPERVISION AND 5 YEARS PROBATION. DEFENDANT IS ORDERED TO PAY ALL COSTS AND ASSESSMENTS INCLUDING LAB FEES AND $ 4500 TO CRIME VICTIMS' RESTITUTION FUND.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal of a criminal conviction returned by a jury in the Circuit Court of Coahoma County (Mississippi), defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide for allegedly negligently causing an accident resulting in the death of another while he was under the influence of methamphetamine and cocaine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In a vehicular accident, defendant caused the death of a passenger in another vehicle. Officers investigating the accident testified that the debris from defendant's vehicle contained empty beer cans, packages of syringes, and bottles containing unidentified liquids and residue. Based on those discoveries, a blood sample was drawn and a urine sample taken from defendant that tested positive for the presence of cocaine and methamphetamines in defendant's system. The appellate court found that probable cause existed to draw fluid samples from defendant, thereby rendering admissible the results of the scientific testing of those samples. The appellate court was satisfied that the uncontroverted evidence that defendant had ingested illegal narcotics that were still present in measurable quantities in his body, together with evidence of remarkably unusual behavior and his demonstrably reckless operation of a motor vehicle were enough, when considered in conjunction, to support a reasonable inference by the jurors that defendant was, in fact, under the influence of the narcotic substances at the time of the fatal accident. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

578 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Cotten v. State


NO. 2001-CA-00438-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


817 So. 2d 639; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 303



May 21, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: COPIAH COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/01/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. LAMAR PICKARD. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DISMISSED FOR LACK OF JURISDICTION TO HEAR THE PETITION.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Copiah County (Mississippi) which dismissed her petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued in her petition that Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-147, the statute under which she was sentenced, was unconstitutional. Specifically, defendant contended the enhancement statute did not have a time limit for a prior conviction to enhance the penalty for a second offense, and due to this lack of time period restriction, her constitutional right to due process was violated. The trial court found that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the petition. On appeal, the appellate court concluded the trial court erred in dismissing the petition for lack of jurisdiction. In addition, the appellate court noted the issue of remoteness for a prior offense had not been addressed before as it related to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-147. However, the appellate court noted the supreme court had upheld the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81, a similar habitual offender sentencing statute. The appellate court advised that it saw no reason to hold differently in a case dealing with Miss. Code Ann. § 41-129-147. Consequently, the appellate court found the erroneous dismissal for lack of jurisdiction by the trial court was harmless.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment and denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

 

579 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Harwell v. State


NO. 2000-CP-01642-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


817 So. 2d 598; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 241



May 7, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 02/09/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. HENRY L. LACKEY. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. JIM HOOD. DISTRICT ATTORNEY: TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PCR SUMMARILY DENIED.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lafayette County Circuit Court, Mississippi, denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief after defendant was convicted of simple robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not appointing counsel for the probation revocation hearing. The appellate court found that probationers did not have a per se right to counsel at revocation hearings. The right to counsel did not attach because a probation revocation proceeding did not fall within the critical stages of a criminal prosecution where a substantial right of the accused might be affected. Defendant neither obtained nor requested counsel during any stage of his revocation proceeding. The defenses argued by defendant were straightforward and not complex or otherwise difficult to develop or present. The trial court was under no duty to appoint counsel during the revocation proceeding. There was no evidence in the record establishing that the trial court suspended defendant's sentence without attaching conditions of probation; therefore, the appellate court could not reverse the trial court's denial of post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

580 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00407-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


881 So. 2d 209; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 869



April 9, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 480 (Miss. Ct. App., May 6, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 852 So. 2d 577, 2003 Miss. App. LEXIS 544 (Miss. Ct. App., 2003)
Affirmed by Jones v. State, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 588 (Miss., Oct. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: BOLIVAR COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 12/14/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KENNETH L. THOMAS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 12/14/1999: VEHICULAR HOMICIDE: DEFENDANT IS SENTENCED TO 20 YEARS WITH 5 YEARS SUSPENDED AFTER SERVING 15 YEARS; MOTION FOR REHEARING FILED: 05/03/2002 - DENIED; AFFIRMED - 05/06/03.
Jones v. State, 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 185 (Miss. Ct. App., Apr. 9, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, as charged by the State, of negligently causing the death of another while operating a vehicle under the influence of cocaine. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck the victim's vehicle from the rear. Both were injured, and the victim later died at the hospital. As part of the diagnostic treatment administered to defendant, the hospital performed a urine analysis, which tested positive for cocaine. Defendant was charged and convicted of negligently causing the victim's death. The court affirmed on appeal and denied defendant's rehearing motion. Without the results of the urine analysis, the State would not have been able to prove that defendant was under the influence of cocaine when he collided with the victim's vehicle. Thus, the medical records regarding the analysis had to be removed from the protection of the physician-patient privilege found in Miss. Code Ann. § 13-1-21(1) (Supp. 2001) and Miss. R. Evid. 503(b). The trial court did not err in refusing to exclude the results of the urine analysis done by the hospital employee simply because she did not hold a valid permit from the state crime laboratory pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-19 (Supp. 2001). The analysis performed was reasonable, and the results were admissible. While the analysis confirmation report was improperly admitted, it was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for rehearing, withdrew its earlier opinion, substituted this opinion, and otherwise affirmed.

TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POSSESSION OF MORE THAN ONE KILOGRAM BUT LESS THAN FIVE KILOGRAMS OF MARIHUANA: SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF 20 YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grenada County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant for possession of a controlled substance, more than one kilogram but less than five kilograms of marijuana, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(c)(2)(F) (Rev. 2001). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying all peremptory motions and the verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. Defendant contended the State failed to prove constructive possession of the marijuana and therefore defendant could not be convicted of the possession charge. The appellate court found that testimony at trial linked defendant and only defendant to the marijuana. The narcotics agent specifically testified that the agents did not find anything in the vehicle or the bag that would link any other suspect to the crime. Defendant admitted that the bag belonged to him and he was listed as the renter of the vehicle. There was abundant evidence presented during trial as to defendant's guilt. The trial judge exercised his discretion and chose to sentence defendant to a term less than the maximum allowed by statute. His sentence was not disproportionate to the crime or excessive in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bailey v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


808 So. 2d 987; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 86



February 26, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 01/22/2001. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. FRANK A. RUSSELL. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: PCR MOTION DISMISSED.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lee County Circuit Court, Mississippi, dismissed defendant's post-conviction relief motion after he was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to sell. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel in the post-conviction trial proceedings, that his transfer from the intensive supervision program (ISP) violated due process, and that his attorney failed to perfect an appeal. The appellate court found that defendant cited no authority for the proposition that he was entitled to counsel at the revocation hearing wherein his participation in the ISP was terminated. Because it was an administrative matter before the Mississippi Department of Corrections, defendant was not constitutionally entitled to a state-appointed counsel. Whether defendant's post-conviction relief counsel breached any agreement that defendant may have had with him was not before the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Robinson v. State


NO. 2000-CP-02087-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 96



February 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied April 23, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MONROE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 08/16/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER III. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: POSTCONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF DENIED.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Monroe County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered judgment denying, without an evidentiary hearing, defendant's petition for postconviction relief from his conviction for uttering a forgery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on two counts of sexual battery. He pled guilty to one count and the remaining count was retired. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison; however, the entire sentence was suspended. Thereafter, he was arrested on three counts of uttering a forgery. The State sought to revoke his probation. The trial court, following a hearing, revoked it and ordered him to serve the remainder of his 20-year sentence. Defendant's posttrial motion was denied without an evidentiary hearing. After the judgment of denial was entered, the appellate court found he was not entitled to relief based on his argument that the prior sentence was invalid given that he was not entitled to receive probation on his sexual battery conviction. It reasoned that he could not take advantage of his impermissibly lenient sentence to obtain postconviction relief after the lenient sentence was forfeited due to his own conduct. It also found: (1) that he was not denied effective assistance of counsel, (2) that he was not entitled to counsel at his revocation hearing and the State proved revocation was proper, and (3) that any error due to an incomplete record was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bowie v. City of Jackson Police Dep't


NO. 2000-CC-01244-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


816 So. 2d 1012; 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 36



January 22, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 06/14/2000. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. TOMIE T. GREEN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: COMMISSION'S DECISION THAT THE TERMINATION WAS FOR CAUSE AFFIRMED BY THE CIRCUIT COURT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) that affirmed a judgment of the Civil Service Commission that upheld defendant police department's dismissal of him.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the officer argued that he was denied his right to procedural due process. The officer violated civil service rules preventing the use of unnecessary force and brutality to persons under arrest. The officer kicked the victim in the ribs, and the victim later reported to the hospital where he was found to have broken ribs and a collapsed lung. That type of behavior was exactly the type that caused harm to private citizens and was detrimental to city government in that it lessened the trust of the public in those sworn to protect them. Bowie was given proper notice regarding the pre-termination notice. The letter met all the requirements set out in the statute, and was very specific in laying out the grounds for Bowie's termination. The actions taken by the Commission were for good cause. There was substantial evidence that supported the Commission's decision to terminate the officer, and the basis provided in the Commission's findings of fact proved that the decision was not arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wolfe v. City of D'Iberville


NO. 2000-CP-01295-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


799 So. 2d 142; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 409



October 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 07/17/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN H. WHITFIELD TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DEFENDANT'S MOTION TO DISMISS IS GRANTED.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sued defendant city in county court for failure to connect his properties to the water and sewer lines. The county court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The property owner appealed to the Circuit Court of Harrison County (Mississippi) which affirmed and ruled that the property owner's notice of appeal was untimely and thereby statutorily barred. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner never brought his account current by paying the complete balance, citing that he did not owe the charges. Therefore, the district refused to connect his business to the water and sewer lines until his account balance was settled. The property owner claimed that his appeal to the circuit court was filed in a timely manner because he filed it within the 30 days required by Miss. Unif. Cir. & County Ct. Prac. R. 5.04 and contended that the rule superseded Miss. Code Ann. § 11-51-79 (1972), which gave a complainant 10 days from the county court judgment to file a proper notice of appeal. The court of appeals agreed that the rule superceded the statute. However the appellate court held that the property owner had not conquered the issue of summary judgment. The legal issue of whether a property owner could be compelled to pay the fees in question had already been settled by a decision of the supreme court in another case. That decision left nothing for the property owner to argue and no remaining facts in dispute that were material to the case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Burge v. Richton Mun. Separate Sch. Dist.


NO. 2000-CA-01844-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


797 So. 2d 1062; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 416



October 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 09/28/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: PERRY COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. RICHARD W. MCKENZIE. TRIAL COURT.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, father and child, sued defendant school district claiming it was negligent when it allowed the child's mother, the non-custodial parent to pick the child up from school without written authorization from the father to do so. The Perry County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted the school district's motion to dismiss. The father and child appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father and child argued that, because the courts had moved from a mandatory compliance standard to a substantial compliance standard on the notice of claim requirement under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(1) (Supp. 2000), the same standard should apply to the subsection of that statute which dictated the limitations period in which to file a complaint. Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-11(3) (Supp. 2000). The court of appeals disagreed. The father and child, after their timely notice of claim, had 1 year and 95 days thereafter to file their complaint. They did not do so. The court declined to apply amendments to the statute that lengthened the time period because the state constitution precluded legislative revival of actions lost to time limitation requirements.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Ott v. Mitchell


NO. 2000-CP-01252-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


792 So. 2d 332; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 319



August 14, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 06/21/2000. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CLARKE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. ROBERT WALTER BAILEY. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 06/21/2000: ORDER GRANTING MOTION TO DISMISS AS TO STATE DEFENDANTS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clarke County Circuit Court, Mississippi, granted a motion to dismiss against appellant. The appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the court's order granting a motion to dismiss pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(1), (6), against him in his civil action, contending that his constitutional rights had been violated by the underlying convictions for intimidating a witness. The court of appeals disagreed. Appellant's arguments were barred due to the Heck standard, as a collateral attack on an outstanding state criminal judgment, unless the conviction had been reversed or invalidated through state appeal. This did not occur in appellant's circumstance. In fact, the conviction was affirmed on appeal. Neither appellant nor anyone else could sue for monetary relief based on the alleged unconstitutionality of the arrest and conviction unless the conviction obtained thereunder had been appealed and reversed, or otherwise expunged or invalidated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Vinson v. Benson


NO. 2000-CP-01524-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


805 So. 2d 571; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 314



August 7, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied October 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 04/14/2000 TRIAL JUDGE: HON. THOMAS J. GARDNER III TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT DECLINED TO RECONSIDER DISMISSAL OF ACTION AGAINST CONSERVATOR.
Vinson v. Benson, 235 F.3d 1342, 2000 U.S. App. LEXIS 28213 (5th Cir. Miss., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellants, father/son, sued the Lee County Chancery Court (Mississippi) clerk, for his refusal to allow them to remove the appellate records of the two chancery court actions below, from the courthouse. The case was dismissed and their motion for reconsideration denied. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellants, a father and son, petitioned the trial court to appoint a conservator for elderly parents, who then petitioned for injunctive relief stemming from the father/son's exercise of power of attorney obtained from the parents. The court clerk was appointed conservator. When they sought to remove the record on appeal from the courthouse so they could review it in preparation for an appeal, and the clerk would not allow it, they sued him and his surety. Finding the clerk was protected by absolute quasi-judicial immunity, the trial court granted his motion to dismiss with prejudice. They appealed to the Mississippi Supreme Court, pro se. The crucial question before the Supreme Court on appeal was whether the circuit judge abused his discretion in dismissing their case with prejudice. The Supreme Court concluded that it had not and that the dismissal was appropriate because they should have petitioned for mandamus.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the claims and imposing filing restrictions was affirmed.

Maldonado v. State


NO. 2000-KA-00076-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


796 So. 2d 247; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 298



July 24, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/01/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN T. KITCHENS. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 06/01/1999: GUILTY OF POSSESSION OF MORE THAN 30 GRAMS OF COCAINE. SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF 30 YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF MDOC. TIME SERVED IN PRETRIAL DETAINMENT IS CREDITED AGAINST THIS SENTENCE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Rankin County Circuit Court, Mississippi, convicted defendant of possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine and sentenced her to 30 years. Subsequently, the trial court denied defendant's motion for new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The officer had probable cause to pull the accomplice driver over, the accomplice consented to the search of the car, and defendant had no expectation of privacy as a passenger in the car that the accomplice was driving, as it was neither in her name, nor was there any evidence that she was a person responsible for the car. Therefore, defendant had no standing to challenge the search of the car or the seizure of the drugs, even if the contents were found to be her personal property. The trial judge was correct in preventing the jury from hearing the proffered evidence of the purse and its contents because of untimeliness of the defense in seeking to introduce it as evidence. Also, the jury verdict was not against the overwhelming weight of the evidence as accomplice's testimony, which was adopted by the jury as true, showed that defendant was not only aware of the presence of the cocaine in the vehicle, but that she was intentionally and consciously in possession of it. Finally, the appellate court determined that the 30-year sentence was not grossly disproportional to the crime of possessing and attempting to transfer 716 pounds of cocaine.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

McDonald v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01680-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


784 So. 2d 261; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 173



May 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 09/24/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JOHN T. KITCHENS. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DISTRICT ATTORNEY: RICHARD D. MITCHELL. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: SIMPLE ASSAULT ON A POLICE OFFICER, SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF 5 YRS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC. PAY COURT COSTS BEFORE 60TH DAY FOLLOWING RELEASE; OBLIGATION IS CONDITION OF PAROLE; PROBATION OR OTHER EXECUTIVE RELEASE; SENTENCED TO 5 YRS SUPERVISED PROBATION WITH MDOC.



DISPOSITION: THE JUDGMENT OF THE MADISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT OF CONVICTION OF SIMPLE ASSAULT ON A POLICE OFFICER AND SENTENCE TO FIVE YEARS REVERSED AND THE MATTER IS REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL IN ACCORDANCE WITH THE TERMS OF THIS OPINION. ALL COSTS OF THIS APPEAL ARE ASSESSED TO MADISON COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a jury's verdict of guilty of simple assault on a police officer and the sentence of the Madison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of five years.


OVERVIEW: A police officer responded to a call of an alleged fight. The testimony at trial established that (1) police officers attempted to arrest defendant; (2) defendant walked away from the officers; (3) defendant struggled with one of the officers. On appeal, the appellate court only addressed those two issues which were pertinent to the appellate court's resolution of the case, namely (1) that the trial court erred in refusing to grant a lesser-included offense instruction and (2) that the trial judge erred in refusing to recuse himself from the case. There was a sufficient evidentiary basis in the record to support an instruction on resisting arrest. Had that instruction been given, it was quite possible that a jury might have found defendant guilty of resisting arrest rather than simple assault on a police officer. Moreover, the trial judge should have recused himself. He did not recuse himself, but instead accepted defendant's waiver of objection. Although the waiver was effective, the better reasoned approach would have been to recuse and avoid even the appearance of conflict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the matter was remanded for a new trial.

S. B. v. L.W.


NO. 1999-CA-01540-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


793 So. 2d 656; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 101



March 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LAFAYETTE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 08/17/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. GLENN ALDERSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: CUSTODY GRANTED TO L. W. S.B. ORDERED TO PAY $ 200 PER MONTH IN CHILD SUPPORT. VISITATION RIGHTS GRANTED TO S.B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the Lafayette County Chancery Court, Mississippi, which granted custody of her child to appellee father.


OVERVIEW: The parties had a child out of wedlock and were never married. Appellee father petitioned the court for a declaration of custody when appellant mother expressed her intent to move. The trial court awarded appellee father custody and appellant mother sought review. The appellate court held that the chancellor properly decided the case as one for initial custody since there had been no prior custody determination. The appellate court found that in addition to appellant mother's bisexual lifestyle, the chancellor was disturbed at her lack of financial and emotional stability. He was concerned that appellant mother quit a well-paying full time job to move and to start a business and was impressed with the appellee father's ability to provide a stable environment for his daughter in the form of an established home. Therefore, the appellate court held that although the morality of the mother's lifestyle was one important factor to the chancellor's decision, it was not the sole factor; thus, there was no clear error and the chancellor did not abuse his discretion in awarding custody to the father.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; the chancellor properly considered the Albright factors and properly applied the standard of law used in divorce proceedings since there was no prior determination of custody.

Ware v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01122-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


790 So. 2d 201; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 87



February 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: SCOTT COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 06/30/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. V. R. COTTEN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DUI MANSLAUGHTER: SENTENCED TO 20 YEARS IN THE MDOC. UPON SERVING 15 YEARS OF SAID SENTENCE, THE REMAINING 5 YEARS ARE SUSPENDED, AND THE DEFENDANT WILL BE PLACED ON PROBATION FOR 5 YEARS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Scott County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted appellant of DUI manslaughter and sentenced him to 20 years in prison, 5 years suspended, and probation and restitution. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant in a pickup pulling a trailer with 3 horses went through an intersection stop sign at 30 miles per hour. In the intersection appellant hit a vehicle with three occupants that had the right of way, killing its passengers. Appellant's blood sample showed an illegal alcohol level, and the remaining portion of it was destroyed by the State before he was indicted. None of the other vehicle's driver's blood sample, negative for alcohol, was destroyed. Appellant was convicted of DUI manslaughter and sentenced to 20 years in prison, 5 years suspended, with probation and restitution. The court affirmed. Photos introduced were admissible and not too gruesome. The trial court erred in admitting a diagram as to point of impact made by an officer who was not an accident reconstructionist. Also, the expert who testified should have made a personal determination about point of impact. However that was not reversible error because of the plethora of other evidence. There had been probable cause to draw blood. Appellant did not show that independent blood analysis would have differed in result. Failure to give a proximate cause jury instruction was error, but not reversible error.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence were affirmed. Error as to accident reconstruction evidence was harmless, failure to give proximate cause jury instruction was error but not reversible error, and there had been probable cause to draw appellant's blood. Appellant did not show that independent blood analysis would have differed in result. The juror selection process had been proper.
