Wash v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00738-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


790 So. 2d 856; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 69



February 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied April 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/31/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: NESHOBA COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. V. R. COTTEN. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: DUI MANSLAUGHTER: SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF (20) YEARS IN THE MDOC. UPON SERVING (16) YEARS OF SAID SENTENCE, THE REMAINING (4) YEARS ARE SUSPENDED, AND THE DEFENDANT WILL BE PLACED ON PROBATION FOR A PERIOD OF (5) YEARS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his negligent homicide conviction from the Neshoba County Circuit Court, Mississippi, raising issues concerning evidence introduced at trial, the denial of several motions, and the award of restitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of negligent homicide while driving under the influence. On appeal, he raised issue concerning evidence introduced at trial, the denial of several post-conviction motions, and the award of restitution to the wife of the victim. The appeals court affirmed the conviction, reasoning the administration of the blood test was valid, notwithstanding the invalidity of the statute, as the surrounding circumstances of the accident were adequate to establish probable cause. Further, although the blood test was administered more than two hours after the accident, there was no evidence of deliberate delay. Admission of testimony from the attending officers was not error as they merely talked shop to each other, despite an order of sequestration. Lastly, evidence of guilt was sufficient to warrant denial of appellant's post-conviction motions, and due to failure to object, restitution argument was not properly preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. Probable cause existed to draw appellant's blood, although tests were administered more than two hours after the accident; the judge did not err in allowing officers testimony; denial of post-conviction motions was proper; and, argument against restitution was waived.

 

595 of 603 DOCUMENTS


In re Hemphill-Weathers v. Farrish


NO. 1999-CA-00610-COA CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 1999-CA-00611


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


779 So. 2d 167; 2001 Miss. App. LEXIS 25



January 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] DATE OF TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT: 03/31/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: LEFLORE COUNTY CHANCERY COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. WILLIAM G. WILLARD JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION FATHER'S MOTION TO SET ASIDE SETTLEMENT DENIED.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father challenged a judgment of the Leflore County Chancery Court (Mississippi) dismissing his petition to set aside litigation settlements entered on behalf of his alleged two children six years earlier. Petitioner argued he should have been joined in the settlement proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The two minor children were injured in a car-truck accident in 1991. A truck driven by an employee of respondent trucking company collided with the van that carried the children. The mother of the two children reached a settlement with respondent in 1992. In both children's petition for settlement, their mother named petitioner as the father. She alleged that she and petitioner had never married, that he did not live with them, and that he did not provide monetary support for either child. Six years later, petitioner sought to set aside both settlement orders. Petitioner argued the 1992 orders were void because he was not joined as a party. Because no proof of petitioner's paternity was presented, the trial court dismissed his petition. Judgment was affirmed. At the time of settlement in 1992, there was no legally recognized father. The court found that petitioner did not need to be given notice or be joined in the settlement proceedings since the children were born out of wedlock, no one had ever been adjudicated the father, and petitioner himself did not live with or support the children. The judgment on the settlements was not void.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; however inadequate petitioner believed the settlements to be, he was not required to have notice of the settlements or to be joined in the petitions to settle the minors' claims. Because there was only one legally known parent, the mother, at the settlement hearings, the trial court had the authority to approve the settlement of both minors without notifying petitioner.

 

596 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. State


NO. 1999-KA-01011-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


784 So. 2d 966; 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 571



December 12, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 04/22/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JERRY O. TERRY SR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: TRANSFER OF A CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE TO WIT: COCAINE-SENTENCED TO 25 YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MDOC, SAID SENTENCE BEING WITHOUT THE HOPE OF PAROLE OR PROBATION.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence by the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) of transferring a controlled substance, arising from an incident in which appellant sold crack cocaine to an undercover police officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of transferring a controlled substance, and was sentenced to 25 years' incarceration as a habitual offender. The charge arose from an incident in which appellant sold crack cocaine to an undercover police officer. Appellant challenged the conviction and sentence, arguing the jury should have been instructed on entrapment, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held appellant was not entitled to an entrapment instruction. To raise the defense of entrapment, appellant was required to show evidence of government inducement to commit the criminal act and a lack of predisposition to engage in the criminal act prior to contact with government agents. Appellant instigated the sale, and was in possession of the cocaine at the time of the sale. The court held appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel. Appellant's counsel initially stated he was unprepared. However, counsel stated he could prepare if the trial were postponed until later that day. Counsel demonstrated readiness through thorough cross-examination and closing arguments. The court held the sentence imposed was within statutory limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence, because appellant was not entitled to an entrapment jury instruction, appellant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, and the sentence imposed was within the limits prescribed by statute.

 

597 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Durr v. University Hosp.


NO. 1999-CA-00757-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


773 So. 2d 403; 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 566



December 5, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/23/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. JAMES E. GRAVES JR. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: ORDER DISMISSING CLAIM WITH PREJUDICE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed appellant's complaint against appellee alleging negligence during the birth of her son, on the ground that it was barred by the Mississippi Tort Claims Act and by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother gave birth to her son in appellee's hospital. Appellant filed a complaint alleging that appellee's negligence during the birth resulted in the child suffering birth defects and other complications. Appellee argued that the claim was barred by the notice provision of the Mississippi Tort Claims Act, and that it was immune from liability pursuant to the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The trial court agreed with appellee that appellant's claim was barred by the Tort Claims Act and/or the doctrine of sovereign immunity, and dismissed the complaint. The court affirmed. The trial judge did not err in granting summary judgment in appellee's favor. The court assumed, in light of appellant's contention that her cause of action accrued prior to the effective date of the Tort Claims Act, that appellant learned of the alleged defects at or about the time of the birth of her child. The court found that appellant's cause of action accrued prior to the enactment of the Tort Claims Act. Therefore, the court followed Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6, and applied common law. As a result, the doctrine of sovereign immunity protected appellee from the suit brought by appellant.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Appellant's claims against appellee were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. Appellant's cause of action accrued prior to the enactment of the Tort Claims Act, therefore the court was directed by statute to apply common law. As a result, the court found that the doctrine of sovereign immunity protected appellee from the suit.

 

598 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00607-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


788 So. 2d 788; 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 551



November 28, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 20, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: DATE OF JUDGMENT: 03/11/1999. COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: RANKIN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. SAMAC RICHARDSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 02/26/1999: VOYEURISM: SENTENCED TO SERVE A TERM OF LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN MDOC AS A VIOLENT HABITUAL OFFENDER WITHOUT POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which convicted him of voyeurism and sentenced as an habitual offender to life imprisonment without parole.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was seen peeping into the window of a home. Police arrived and saw appellant attempting to hide in the shadows. He ran but was apprehended. The trial court convicted him of voyeurism and sentenced him to life in prison without parole, as an habitual offender. The appellate court affirmed. The jury's verdict was not against the weight of the evidence as it was supported by overwhelming evidence. The lewd, licentious and indecent purpose and/or intent of the crime of voyeurism was easily inferred by the jury. Further, appellant failed to demonstrate that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. Based on the weakness of appellant's case and the strength of the State's case, appellant could not prove that the outcome would have been different, but for the actions of his counsel. Finally, although the issue regarding the constitutionality of appellant's sentence was waived for failure to raise the issue at the trial level, the appellate court found that the sentence was not disproportionate to his crime. He was an habitual offender with serious prior convictions. The strict sentence was justified and within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because the jury verdict was supported by the overwhelming weight of the evidence. Further, the strength of the evidence against appellant was such that he was unable to show that but for his attorney's errors, a different result would have been achieved. Finally, appellant failed to raise the unconstitutionality of his sentence at the trial level. Thus, the issue was waived.

Desalvo v. State


NO. 1999-KA-00479-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


776 So. 2d 704; 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 339



August 1, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied October 31, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: HANCOCK COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 02/25/1999. TRIAL JUDGE: HON. KATHY KING JACKSON. TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 02/25/1999: COUNT I BURGLARY AND COUNT X BURGLARY - SENTENCED TO SERVE A PERIOD OF SEVEN (7) YEARS ON COUNT I: BURGLARY IN THE CUSTODY OF MDOC; AND SEVEN (7) YEARS ON COUNT X: BURGLARY WITH MDOC TO RUN CONSECUTIVELY WITH SENTENCE IMPOSED IN COUNT I: BURGLARY. DEFENDANT TO PAY ALL COSTS ACCRUED IN THIS PROSECUTION AND REMAIN IN CUSTODY UNTIL SAID SENTENCE IS FULLY COMPLIED WITH.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment, based upon a jury verdict, of the Hancock County Circuit Court (Mississippi), convicting him on two counts of burglary and sentencing him to seven years' in prison on each count to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, while still a municipal police officer, was apprehended during a "sting operation" burglarizing a tax assessor's office. Appellant ultimately gave a tape-recorded statement in which he admitted committing two burglaries. On appeal, following his convictions, appellant argued the trial court erred by admitting an officer's testimony about his out-of-court opinion that appellant was "a dirty cop." The court found that statement was properly admitted as it was made in the context of the officer's thought process during the investigation to explain to the city's mayor why he acted and proceeded in the manner that he did. Further, the trial court did not improperly single out appellant for a sentence enhancement because he was a police officer. Appellant's sentence was not grossly disproportionate to others in similar situations. Finally, appellant was not denied effective assistance of counsel, as he failed to show a reasonable probability of a different outcome had his trial counsel acted differently.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; officer's testimony as to statements he made to mayor that appellant was a "dirty cop" was admitted not for truth of matter asserted, but to show why "sting operation" was organized. Appellant's sentence was not grossly disproportionate to others similarly situated. Appellant could not have proved ineffective assistance of counsel, as witness testimony still strongly supported verdict.

 

600 of 603 DOCUMENTS


Brendle v. City of Houston


NO. 1998-KM-01656-COA


COURT OF APPEALS OF MISSISSIPPI


759 So. 2d 1274; 2000 Miss. App. LEXIS 263



June 6, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] COURT FROM WHICH APPEALED: CHICKASAW COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. DATE OF JUDGMENT: 10/02/1998 TRIAL JUDGE: HON. R. KENNETH COLEMAN TRIAL COURT DISPOSITION: 10/02/1998: PUBLIC PROFANITY: SENTENCED TO PAY A FINE IN THE AMOUNT OF $ 52 & $ 68 IN STATE FEES. RESISTING ARREST: SENTENCED TO PAY A FINE IN THE AMOUNT OF $ 262 & $ 68 IN STATE FEES.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant sought review of his conviction for public profanity and resisting arrest by the Chickasaw County Circuit Court, Mississippi. The appellant challenged his conviction on the ground that his utterance, directed at a police officer, was not profane and that the profanity statute was unconstitutionally applied to him.


OVERVIEW: The appellant was arrested and charged with public profanity and resisting arrest after he allegedly addressed a police officer with profane language. The appellant was charged under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-47, which prohibited public profanity, defined as swearing or cursing profanely, or use of vulgar and indecent language. The appellant did not challenge the constitutionality of the statute, but claimed that the statute had been unconstitutionally applied to his speech. The appellant claimed his speech was political in nature and in response to profanity used by the arresting officer. The court reversed the appellant's conviction. The court held that the appellant's speech could not be proscribed as profane unless it rose to the level of "fighting words", a type of speech unprotected by the First Amendment. As the appellant's speech could not be so classified, the court dismissed the charges, including the charge of resisting arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellant's conviction. The court determined that in order to find the appellant guilty under the profanity statute, the appellant's speech would have had to be classified as "fighting words." The court found the appellant's speech did not rise to such a standard and dismissed the charge; the resisting arrest charge was also dismissed.
